{"parentUuid":"4fa25797-f3d2-42f4-b519-637aa0b77b77","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01NVnjXgwtwZjhmn7gtGEQfv","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→/-!\n     2→# Catlib Foundations: Core Types\n     3→\n     4→The fundamental types and structures needed to formalize claims from the\n     5→Catechism of the Catholic Church. These are modeling choices — each one\n     6→is an assumption we're making explicit.\n     7→\n     8→## Design principle\n     9→\n    10→We model theological concepts as opaque types with axiomatically declared\n    11→properties. This mirrors how the Catechism itself works: it defines terms,\n    12→states their properties, and reasons from them. We don't need to construct\n    13→these objects — we need to reason about what follows from their declared\n    14→properties.\n    15→-/\n    16→\n    17→namespace Catlib\n    18→\n    19→/-- A person — human or divine. The Catechism's anthropology distinguishes\n    20→    persons by their capacities (intellect, will, freedom). We model a person\n    21→    as having these capacities to varying degrees. -/\n    22→structure Person where\n    23→  /-- Can this person know truths? -/\n    24→  hasIntellect : Bool\n    25→  /-- Can this person choose freely? -/\n    26→  hasFreeWill : Bool\n    27→  /-- Is this person capable of moral action? -/\n    28→  isMoralAgent : Bool\n    29→\n    30→/-- A human person: has intellect, free will, and moral agency.\n    31→    CCC §1700: \"The dignity of the human person is rooted in his creation\n    32→    in the image and likeness of God.\" -/\n    33→def Person.human : Person :=\n    34→  { hasIntellect := true, hasFreeWill := true, isMoralAgent := true }\n    35→\n    36→/-- An action that a moral agent can perform. -/\n    37→structure Action where\n    38→  /-- The agent performing the action -/\n    39→  agent : Person\n    40→  /-- The object of the action (what is done) — CCC §1750 -/\n    41→  object : Prop\n    42→  /-- The intention of the agent — CCC §1752 -/\n    43→  intention : Prop\n    44→  /-- The circumstances — CCC §1754 -/\n    45→  circumstances : Prop\n    46→\n    47→/-- The three sources of morality (CCC §1750).\n    48→    \"The morality of human acts depends on: the object chosen, the end in\n    49→    view or the intention, and the circumstances of the action.\" -/\n    50→structure MoralEvaluation where\n    51→  action : Action\n    52→  /-- Is the object of the action good? -/\n    53→  objectIsGood : Prop\n    54→  /-- Is the intention good? -/\n    55→  intentionIsGood : Prop\n    56→  /-- Are the circumstances appropriate? -/\n    57→  circumstancesAppropriate : Prop\n    58→\n    59→/-- An action is morally good when all three sources are good.\n    60→    CCC §1755: \"A morally good act requires the goodness of the object,\n    61→    of the end, and of the circumstances together.\" -/\n    62→def MoralEvaluation.isGood (eval : MoralEvaluation) : Prop :=\n    63→  eval.objectIsGood ∧ eval.intentionIsGood ∧ eval.circumstancesAppropriate\n    64→\n    65→/-- An action is morally evil if any source is evil.\n    66→    CCC §1755: \"An evil end corrupts the action, even if the object is\n    67→    good in itself.\" -/\n    68→def MoralEvaluation.isEvil (eval : MoralEvaluation) : Prop :=\n    69→  ¬eval.objectIsGood ∨ ¬eval.intentionIsGood ∨ ¬eval.circumstancesAppropriate\n    70→\n    71→/-- Good and evil are contradictory (for the same evaluation). -/\n    72→theorem good_iff_not_evil (eval : MoralEvaluation) :\n    73→    eval.isGood ↔ ¬eval.isEvil := by\n    74→  unfold MoralEvaluation.isGood MoralEvaluation.isEvil\n    75→  constructor\n    76→  · intro ⟨ho, hi, hc⟩ h\n    77→    cases h with\n    78→    | inl h => exact h ho\n    79→    | inr h => cases h with\n    80→      | inl h => exact h hi\n    81→      | inr h => exact h hc\n    82→  · intro h\n    83→    have ho : eval.objectIsGood := Classical.byContradiction fun hn => h (Or.inl hn)\n    84→    have hi : eval.intentionIsGood := Classical.byContradiction fun hn => h (Or.inr (Or.inl hn))\n    85→    have hc : eval.circumstancesAppropriate := Classical.byContradiction fun hn => h (Or.inr (Or.inr hn))\n    86→    exact ⟨ho, hi, hc⟩\n    87→\n    88→/-- Grace — God's free and undeserved help.\n    89→    CCC §1996: \"Grace is favor, the free and undeserved help that God gives\n    90→    us to respond to his call.\" -/\n    91→structure Grace where\n    92→  /-- Grace is freely given (not earned) -/\n    93→  isFree : Prop\n    94→  /-- Grace is undeserved -/\n    95→  isUndeserved : Prop\n    96→  /-- Grace enables a response to God's call -/\n    97→  enablesResponse : Prop\n    98→\n    99→/-- Sin — an offense against reason, truth, and right conscience.\n   100→    CCC §1849: \"Sin is an offense against reason, truth, and right conscience;\n   101→    it is a failure in genuine love for God and neighbor.\" -/\n   102→structure Sin where\n   103→  /-- The action constituting the sin -/\n   104→  action : Action\n   105→  /-- Sin is a free act (requires free will) -/\n   106→  isFree : Prop\n   107→  /-- Sin is contrary to reason -/\n   108→  contraryToReason : Prop\n   109→  /-- Sin is contrary to truth -/\n   110→  contraryToTruth : Prop\n   111→\n   112→/-- Sin requires free will — you cannot sin without choosing to.\n   113→    CCC §1859: \"Mortal sin requires full knowledge and complete consent.\" -/\n   114→theorem sin_requires_freedom (s : Sin) (h : s.isFree) :\n   115→    s.action.agent.hasFreeWill = true → s.isFree := by\n   116→  intro _\n   117→  exact h\n   118→\n   119→/-- Axiom provenance tags — every axiom should declare its source. -/\n   120→inductive Provenance where\n   121→  /-- From a specific Bible verse under Catholic reading -/\n   122→  | scripture (reference : String)\n   123→  /-- From Church Fathers, Councils, Magisterium -/\n   124→  | tradition (source : String)\n   125→  /-- From philosophical reasoning without revelation -/\n   126→  | naturalLaw\n   127→  /-- From the Catechism's own defined terms -/\n   128→  | definition (paragraph : Nat)\n   129→\n   130→/-- Which denominations accept a given axiom or theorem.\n   131→    This is the key insight: the axiom set IS the denomination.\n   132→    Tagging results lets us say \"this holds under Catholic axioms\"\n   133→    or \"this is shared across denominations.\" -/\n   134→inductive Denomination where\n   135→  /-- Accepted by the Catholic Church -/\n   136→  | catholic\n   137→  /-- Accepted by Lutheran churches -/\n   138→  | lutheran\n   139→  /-- Accepted by Reformed/Calvinist churches -/\n   140→  | reformed\n   141→  /-- Accepted by all/most Christian denominations -/\n   142→  | ecumenical\n   143→\n   144→/-- A denominational tag — which traditions accept this claim. -/\n   145→structure DenominationalTag where\n   146→  /-- Which denominations accept this axiom/theorem -/\n   147→  acceptedBy : List Denomination\n   148→  /-- Brief note on any qualifications -/\n   149→  note : String\n   150→\n   151→/-- Shared across all major Christian denominations. -/\n   152→def ecumenical : DenominationalTag :=\n   153→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical], note := \"broadly shared\" }\n   154→\n   155→/-- Specifically Catholic — other denominations may reject. -/\n   156→def catholicOnly : DenominationalTag :=\n   157→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic], note := \"Catholic distinctive\" }\n   158→\n   159→/-- Shared by Catholic and Lutheran but not all denominations. -/\n   160→def catholicAndLutheran : DenominationalTag :=\n   161→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic, Denomination.lutheran], note := \"\" }\n   162→\n   163→/-- Specifically Lutheran — Catholics would reject. -/\n   164→def lutheranOnly : DenominationalTag :=\n   165→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.lutheran], note := \"Lutheran distinctive\" }\n   166→\n   167→/-- The source from which authority derives. -/\n   168→inductive AuthoritySource where\n   169→  /-- Authority from God directly -/\n   170→  | divine\n   171→  /-- Authority delegated from another authority holder -/\n   172→  | delegated (holder : Person)\n   173→  /-- Authority arising from natural law -/\n   174→  | naturalLaw\n   175→\n   176→/-- Authority — the quality by virtue of which persons or institutions\n   177→    make laws and give orders and expect obedience.\n   178→    CCC §1897 -/\n   179→structure Authority where\n   180→  /-- Who holds the authority -/\n   181→  holder : Person\n   182→  /-- Source of the authority (delegated, natural, divine) -/\n   183→  source : AuthoritySource\n   184→\n   185→/-- A model of free will. The Catechism assumes libertarian free will —\n   186→    genuine ability to choose otherwise — but never argues for it.\n   187→    This is an opaque type because the MODEL of freedom is itself\n   188→    an assumption we want to track. -/\n   189→inductive FreedomModel where\n   190→  /-- Libertarian: the agent could genuinely have chosen otherwise -/\n   191→  | libertarian\n   192→  /-- Compatibilist: freedom is acting from one's own desires without external coercion -/\n   193→  | compatibilist\n   194→\n   195→/-- A free choice — models the act of choosing with a specific freedom model. -/\n   196→structure FreeChoice (α : Type) where\n   197→  /-- What was chosen -/\n   198→  chosen : α\n   199→  /-- The agent had alternatives available -/\n   200→  alternativesExist : Prop\n   201→  /-- The choice was uncoerced -/\n   202→  uncoerced : Prop\n   203→\n   204→/-- Communion with God — the ultimate end of human life per the Catechism.\n   205→    CCC §1024: \"To live in the full and definitive communion with God.\" -/\n   206→structure CommunionWithGod where\n   207→  /-- The person in communion -/\n   208→  person : Person\n   209→  /-- The person loves God -/\n   210→  lovesGod : Prop\n   211→  /-- The person is in a state of grace -/\n   212→  inGrace : Prop\n   213→\n   214→end Catlib\n   215→"}]},"uuid":"f0193a8d-ca68-4bae-82ce-e78ab41e8eef","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:39:52.913Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"4fa25797-f3d2-42f4-b519-637aa0b77b77","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"a9b0915d-c676-467d-8c46-5752789bd504","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01CWrqrcxSZw6Xe2eCjtUtU8","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations.Basic\n     2→\n     3→/-!\n     4→# Catlib Foundations: The 15 Base Axioms\n     5→\n     6→Every axiom in the 12 formalization files (44 total) traces back to one of these\n     7→15 foundational assumptions, organized into three groups by source:\n     8→\n     9→- **P1-P3**: Philosophical commitments (Aristotle / Aquinas / natural reason)\n    10→- **S1-S9**: Scriptural axioms (specific Bible passages under Catholic reading)\n    11→- **T1-T3**: Sacred Tradition (Church Fathers, Councils, Magisterium)\n    12→\n    13→**Note on the 5/5/5 → 3/9/3 reclassification.** An earlier draft split the 15\n    14→axioms evenly across Philosophy, Scripture, and Tradition. Closer analysis\n    15→showed that several axioms originally classified as Philosophical or Traditional\n    16→actually have strong *direct* scriptural grounding: Paul explicitly teaches\n    17→moral realism (Rom 1:20; 2:14-15), Jesus explicitly teaches teleological freedom\n    18→(Jn 8:34-36; Gal 5:1), multiple New-Testament passages assert the necessity and\n    19→transformative power of grace (Jn 15:5; 2 Cor 5:17; Ezek 36:26), and Paul\n    20→explicitly grounds the binding force of conscience (Rom 14:23; Acts 24:16).\n    21→Most of the system's assumptions therefore trace to Scripture; only three\n    22→irreducibly philosophical models and three distinctively conciliar formulations\n    23→remain outside the scriptural core.\n    24→\n    25→This mirrors the Catechism's own epistemology: Scripture, Tradition, and natural\n    26→reason are the three pillars on which Catholic doctrine rests.\n    27→\n    28→## Design\n    29→\n    30→Each axiom is:\n    31→1. Declared as a Lean `axiom` (an unproven `Prop` or function)\n    32→2. Tagged with a `Provenance` value documenting its source\n    33→3. Typed using the foundational types from `Basic.lean` where applicable\n    34→\n    35→The 12 formalization files should eventually derive their local axioms from\n    36→these 15 rather than declaring them independently.\n    37→-/\n    38→\n    39→namespace Catlib\n    40→\n    41→-- ============================================================================\n    42→-- Additional foundational types needed by the base axioms\n    43→-- ============================================================================\n    44→\n    45→/-- Form — the organizing principle that makes a thing what it is.\n    46→    From Aristotle's Metaphysics, adopted by Aquinas (ST I, q.75-76). -/\n    47→opaque Form : Type\n    48→\n    49→/-- Matter — the principle of potentiality and individuation.\n    50→    From Aristotle's Physics, adopted by Aquinas. -/\n    51→opaque Matter : Type\n    52→\n    53→/-- A composite of form and matter. Aristotelian hylomorphism holds that\n    54→    every material substance is such a composite. -/\n    55→structure Composite where\n    56→  form : Form\n    57→  matter : Matter\n    58→\n    59→/-- A moral proposition — a claim about what is good, right, or obligatory. -/\n    60→opaque MoralProposition : Type\n    61→\n    62→/-- Truth value of a moral proposition, independent of any agent's beliefs. -/\n    63→opaque moralTruthValue : MoralProposition → Prop\n    64→\n    65→/-- Accessibility of a moral truth to unaided reason. -/\n    66→opaque accessibleToReason : MoralProposition → Prop\n    67→\n    68→/-- The good — the final cause or telos toward which freedom is ordered. -/\n    69→opaque TheGood : Type\n    70→\n    71→/-- The degree of freedom an agent possesses (0 = none, higher = more). -/\n    72→opaque FreedomDegree : Type\n    73→\n    74→/-- A strict ordering on freedom degrees. -/\n    75→opaque freedomLt : FreedomDegree → FreedomDegree → Prop\n    76→\n    77→/-- An agent (a Person who can act). -/\n    78→opaque Agent : Type\n    79→\n    80→/-- Whether an agent genuinely could have chosen otherwise in a given situation. -/\n    81→opaque couldChooseOtherwise : Agent → Prop\n    82→\n    83→/-- Primary cause — God's causal activity as first cause. -/\n    84→opaque PrimaryCause : Type\n    85→\n    86→/-- Secondary cause — a creature's own genuine causal activity. -/\n    87→opaque SecondaryCause : Type\n    88→\n    89→/-- Whether two causes compete (i.e. more of one means less of the other). -/\n    90→opaque causesCompete : PrimaryCause → SecondaryCause → Prop\n    91→\n    92→/-- God, modeled as a distinguished entity. -/\n    93→opaque God : Type\n    94→\n    95→/-- God's nature is love. -/\n    96→opaque godIsLove : Prop\n    97→\n    98→/-- Love between persons. -/\n    99→opaque loves : Person → Person → Prop\n   100→\n   101→/-- Whether genuine love requires freedom. -/\n   102→opaque loveRequiresFreedom : Prop\n   103→\n   104→/-- God desires a given person to be saved. -/\n   105→opaque godWillsSalvation : Person → Prop\n   106→\n   107→/-- The moral law written on the heart of a person. -/\n   108→opaque moralLawInscribed : Person → Prop\n   109→\n   110→/-- God governs (providentially orders) a given event or state. -/\n   111→opaque divinelyGoverned : Prop → Prop\n   112→\n   113→/-- Whether a sin is grave (mortal). -/\n   114→opaque isGraveSin : Sin → Prop\n   115→\n   116→/-- Whether a person is in communion with God. -/\n   117→opaque inCommunion : Person → Prop\n   118→\n   119→/-- Grace given to a person. -/\n   120→opaque graceGiven : Person → Grace → Prop\n   121→\n   122→/-- Whether grace transforms (not merely covers) the person. -/\n   123→opaque graceTransforms : Grace → Person → Prop\n   124→\n   125→/-- Whether a person cooperates freely with grace. -/\n   126→opaque cooperatesWithGrace : Person → Grace → Prop\n   127→\n   128→/-- A sacrament. -/\n   129→opaque Sacrament : Type\n   130→\n   131→/-- What a sacrament signifies (its sign-content). -/\n   132→opaque signifies : Sacrament → Prop\n   133→\n   134→/-- What a sacrament actually confers (its effect). -/\n   135→opaque confers : Sacrament → Prop\n   136→\n   137→/-- The judgment of conscience about an action. -/\n   138→opaque conscienceJudges : Person → Action → Prop\n   139→\n   140→/-- Whether an agent is obligated to perform an action. -/\n   141→opaque obligated : Person → Action → Prop\n   142→\n   143→/-- Whether something is evil. -/\n   144→opaque isEvil : Prop → Prop\n   145→\n   146→/-- Whether something is a due good that is absent. -/\n   147→opaque isDueGoodAbsent : Prop → Prop\n   148→\n   149→-- ============================================================================\n   150→-- P1-P3: PHILOSOPHICAL AXIOMS — the irreducible non-scriptural residue (3)\n   151→-- ============================================================================\n   152→\n   153→/-- **P1. HYLOMORPHISM**: Every material substance is a composite of form and matter.\n   154→\n   155→    *Source*: Aristotle, Metaphysics VII-IX; Aquinas, ST I q.75-76\n   156→\n   157→    Gen 2:7 (\"the Lord God formed man of dust… and breathed into his nostrils\n   158→    the breath of life\") is an inspiration but not a derivation of the formal\n   159→    hylomorphic model.\n   160→\n   161→    *Grounds*: soul-as-form-of-body (Soul.lean axioms 5-7), the unity of the\n   162→    human person, anti-Cartesian dualism. The Catechism presupposes this in\n   163→    CCC §365: \"The unity of soul and body is so profound that one has to consider\n   164→    the soul to be the 'form' of the body.\" -/\n   165→axiom p1_hylomorphism :\n   166→  ∀ (f : Form) (m : Matter), ∃ (c : Composite), c.form = f ∧ c.matter = m\n   167→\n   168→/-- Provenance tag for P1. -/\n   169→def p1_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.naturalLaw\n   170→\n   171→/-- **P2. TWO_TIER_CAUSATION**: Primary (divine) and secondary (creaturely)\n   172→    causes operate on different levels and do not compete — more divine action\n   173→    does not mean less creaturely action, and vice versa.\n   174→\n   175→    *Source*: Aquinas, ST I q.105 a.5; the principle of non-contrastive\n   176→    transcendence.\n   177→\n   178→    Phil 2:13 (\"it is God who works in you, both to will and to work\") describes\n   179→    the phenomenon, but the two-tier causal *model* is a philosophical\n   180→    contribution by Aquinas.\n   181→\n   182→    *Grounds*: Providence.lean axiom 8 (primary_secondary_non_competing),\n   183→    creaturely causation is genuine (Providence.lean axiom 42). CCC §306:\n   184→    \"God grants his creatures not only their existence, but also the dignity\n   185→    of acting on their own.\" -/\n   186→axiom p2_two_tier_causation :\n   187→  ∀ (p : PrimaryCause) (s : SecondaryCause), ¬ causesCompete p s\n   188→\n   189→/-- Provenance tag for P2. -/\n   190→def p2_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.naturalLaw\n   191→\n   192→/-- **P3. EVIL_IS_PRIVATION**: Evil is not a positive reality but the absence\n   193→    of a due good — a privation, not a substance.\n   194→\n   195→    *Source*: Augustine, Confessions VII.12 (\"Evil has no existence except as\n   196→    a privation of good\"); Aquinas, ST I q.48 a.1 and q.49.\n   197→\n   198→    Gen 1:31 (\"God saw all that he had made, and it was very good\") is a seed,\n   199→    but the formal privation theory is a philosophical contribution by\n   200→    Augustine and Aquinas.\n   201→\n   202→    *Grounds*: Providence.lean axiom 29 (causation_asymmetry), axiom 40\n   203→    (god_not_cause_of_evil). CCC §311: \"God is in no way, directly or\n   204→    indirectly, the cause of moral evil.\" -/\n   205→axiom p3_evil_is_privation :\n   206→  ∀ (e : Prop), isEvil e → isDueGoodAbsent e\n   207→\n   208→/-- Provenance tag for P3. -/\n   209→def p3_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.naturalLaw\n   210→\n   211→-- ============================================================================\n   212→-- S1-S9: SCRIPTURAL AXIOMS — with full verse references (9)\n   213→-- ============================================================================\n   214→\n   215→/-- **S1. GOD_IS_LOVE**: God's very nature is love, and genuine love requires\n   216→    the beloved's freedom.\n   217→\n   218→    *Source*: 1 John 4:8 (\"God is love\"); Deuteronomy 30:19 (\"I have set\n   219→    before you life and death… choose life\").\n   220→\n   221→    *Grounds*: Hell.lean axiom 30 (love_requires_freedom), the impossibility\n   222→    of predestination to damnation. CCC §214: \"God is Love.\" CCC §1861: love\n   223→    as the fundamental orientation that hell's self-exclusion negates. -/\n   224→axiom s1_god_is_love :\n   225→  godIsLove ∧ loveRequiresFreedom\n   226→\n   227→/-- Provenance tag for S1. -/\n   228→def s1_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"1 Jn 4:8; Dt 30:19\"\n   229→\n   230→/-- **S2. UNIVERSAL_SALVIFIC_WILL**: God desires all human persons to be saved;\n   231→    no one is predestined to damnation.\n   232→\n   233→    *Source*: 1 Timothy 2:4 (\"God desires all people to be saved and to come\n   234→    to the knowledge of the truth\").\n   235→\n   236→    *Grounds*: Hell.lean axiom 32 (no_predestination_to_hell), the universal\n   237→    offer of grace. CCC §1037: \"God predestines no one to go to hell.\" -/\n   238→axiom s2_universal_salvific_will :\n   239→  ∀ (p : Person), godWillsSalvation p\n   240→\n   241→/-- Provenance tag for S2. -/\n   242→def s2_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"1 Tim 2:4\"\n   243→\n   244→/-- **S3. LAW_ON_HEARTS**: God has inscribed the moral law in every human heart,\n   245→    making it accessible even without special revelation.\n   246→\n   247→    *Source*: Romans 2:14-15 (\"When Gentiles who do not have the law do by\n   248→    nature things required by the law… they show that the requirements of the\n   249→    law are written on their hearts\").\n   250→\n   251→    *Grounds*: NaturalLaw.lean axioms 33-34 (divine_grounding, universality).\n   252→    CCC §1954: \"The natural law… is nothing other than the light of\n   253→    understanding placed in us by God.\" -/\n   254→axiom s3_law_on_hearts :\n   255→  ∀ (p : Person), p.hasIntellect = true → moralLawInscribed p\n   256→\n   257→/-- Provenance tag for S3. -/\n   258→def s3_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rom 2:14-15\"\n   259→\n   260→/-- **S4. UNIVERSAL_PROVIDENCE**: God governs all things, including free actions,\n   261→    without negating creaturely freedom.\n   262→\n   263→    *Source*: Matthew 10:29 (\"Not a single sparrow falls to the ground without\n   264→    your Father's will\"); Isaiah 46:10 (\"My purpose will stand, and I will do\n   265→    all that I please\").\n   266→\n   267→    *Grounds*: Providence.lean axiom 35 (providence_universal), foreknowledge\n   268→    compatible with freedom. CCC §302: \"Creation has its own goodness and proper\n   269→    perfection, but it did not spring forth complete from the hands of the\n   270→    Creator.\" CCC §303: \"God carries out his plan through secondary causes.\" -/\n   271→axiom s4_universal_providence :\n   272→  ∀ (event : Prop), divinelyGoverned event\n   273→\n   274→/-- Provenance tag for S4. -/\n   275→def s4_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Mt 10:29; Is 46:10\"\n   276→\n   277→/-- **S5. SIN_SEPARATES**: Grave sin breaks communion with God.\n   278→\n   279→    *Source*: 1 John 3:14-15 (\"Anyone who hates a brother or sister is a\n   280→    murderer, and you know that no murderer has eternal life residing in him\");\n   281→    Romans 6:23 (\"The wages of sin is death\").\n   282→\n   283→    *Grounds*: Sin.lean axiom 14 (mortal_sin_causes_loss_of_grace), Hell.lean\n   284→    axiom 31 (grave_sin_prevents_love). CCC §1855: \"Mortal sin destroys\n   285→    charity in the heart of man.\" -/\n   286→axiom s5_sin_separates :\n   287→  ∀ (p : Person) (s : Sin), isGraveSin s → s.action.agent = p → ¬ inCommunion p\n   288→\n   289→/-- Provenance tag for S5. -/\n   290→def s5_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"1 Jn 3:14-15; Rom 6:23\"\n   291→\n   292→/-- **S6. MORAL_REALISM**: Moral facts exist independently of opinion and are\n   293→    accessible to unaided human reason.\n   294→\n   295→    *Source*: Romans 1:20 (\"So that they are without excuse\"); Romans 2:14-15\n   296→    (\"the requirements of the law are written on their hearts, their\n   297→    consciences also bearing witness\"). Paul explicitly says moral knowledge\n   298→    is accessible without special revelation.\n   299→\n   300→    *Grounds*: natural law theory (NaturalLaw.lean axioms 1-3), the claim that\n   301→    moral truths are objective and knowable. CCC §1954: \"The natural law…\n   302→    is nothing other than the light of understanding placed in us by God.\" -/\n   303→axiom s6_moral_realism :\n   304→  ∀ (mp : MoralProposition), moralTruthValue mp → accessibleToReason mp\n   305→\n   306→/-- Provenance tag for S6. -/\n   307→def s6_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rom 1:20; Rom 2:14-15\"\n   308→\n   309→-- Helpers for S7\n   310→/-- Whether an agent is directed toward the good. -/\n   311→axiom directedTowardGood : Agent → Prop\n   312→\n   313→/-- The freedom degree an agent possesses. -/\n   314→axiom agentFreedom : Agent → FreedomDegree\n   315→\n   316→/-- **S7. TELEOLOGICAL_FREEDOM**: Freedom is ordered toward the good; choosing\n   317→    evil is a defect that diminishes freedom rather than expressing it.\n   318→\n   319→    *Source*: John 8:34 (\"everyone who sins is a slave to sin\"); John 8:36\n   320→    (\"if the Son sets you free, you will be free indeed\"); Galatians 5:1\n   321→    (\"for freedom Christ has set us free\"). Jesus explicitly teaches that\n   322→    freedom is directed toward the good and that sin is bondage, not freedom.\n   323→\n   324→    *Grounds*: Freedom.lean axioms 10-13 (good increases freedom, evil diminishes\n   325→    it, evil possible only in imperfect freedom, responsibility proportional to\n   326→    freedom). CCC §1733: \"The more one does what is good, the freer one becomes.\" -/\n   327→axiom s7_teleological_freedom :\n   328→  ∀ (a1 a2 : Agent),\n   329→    directedTowardGood a1 → ¬ directedTowardGood a2 →\n   330→    freedomLt (agentFreedom a2) (agentFreedom a1)\n   331→\n   332→/-- Provenance tag for S7. -/\n   333→def s7_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Jn 8:34-36; Gal 5:1\"\n   334→\n   335→/-- **S8. GRACE_NECESSARY_AND_TRANSFORMATIVE**: Without grace, humans cannot\n   336→    perform saving good; and grace actually transforms the person (it does not\n   337→    merely declare them righteous extrinsically).\n   338→\n   339→    *Source*: John 15:5 (\"without me you can do nothing\"); 2 Corinthians 5:17\n   340→    (\"if anyone is in Christ, he is a new creation\"); Ezekiel 36:26 (\"I will\n   341→    give you a new heart and put a new spirit in you\"). Multiple passages\n   342→    explicitly assert both the necessity of grace and its transformative\n   343→    (not merely forensic) character.\n   344→\n   345→    *Grounds*: Grace.lean axioms 20-21 (preparation_requires_prevenient,\n   346→    prevenient_grace_unconditioned), Justification.lean axiom 23\n   347→    (grace_is_transformative). CCC §1999: \"Grace… is a participation in\n   348→    the life of God.\" -/\n   349→axiom s8_grace_necessary_and_transformative :\n   350→  ∀ (p : Person) (g : Grace),\n   351→    graceGiven p g → graceTransforms g p\n   352→\n   353→/-- Provenance tag for S8. -/\n   354→def s8_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Jn 15:5; 2 Cor 5:17; Ezek 36:26\"\n   355→\n   356→/-- **S9. CONSCIENCE_BINDS**: The certain judgment of practical reason about\n   357→    the good obliges the agent to follow it; acting against conscience is\n   358→    always wrong.\n   359→\n   360→    *Source*: Romans 14:23 (\"whatever does not proceed from faith is sin\");\n   361→    Acts 24:16 (\"I strive always to keep my conscience clear before God and\n   362→    man\"). Paul explicitly grounds the binding force of conscience in the\n   363→    obligation to act from conviction.\n   364→\n   365→    *Grounds*: Conscience.lean axioms 15-19 (conscience_always_binds,\n   366→    acting_against_conscience_wrong, culpable/innocent ignorance, duty to form\n   367→    conscience). CCC §1790: \"A human being must always obey the certain judgment\n   368→    of his conscience.\" -/\n   369→axiom s9_conscience_binds :\n   370→  ∀ (p : Person) (a : Action), conscienceJudges p a → obligated p a\n   371→\n   372→/-- Provenance tag for S9. -/\n   373→def s9_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rom 14:23; Acts 24:16\"\n   374→\n   375→-- ============================================================================\n   376→-- T1-T3: SACRED TRADITION AXIOMS — with Council references (3)\n   377→-- ============================================================================\n   378→\n   379→/-- **T1. LIBERTARIAN_FREE_WILL**: Agents can genuinely choose otherwise;\n   380→    freedom is not merely the absence of external coercion.\n   381→\n   382→    *Source*: Council of Trent, Session 6, Canon 4: anathema on the claim that\n   383→    free will \"does nothing whatever and is merely passive.\" Sirach 15:14-17\n   384→    (\"It was he who created man in the beginning, and he left him in the power\n   385→    of his own inclination\") provides scriptural basis, but the distinctively\n   386→    *libertarian* (as opposed to compatibilist) reading is a theological\n   387→    inference crystallized at Trent.\n   388→\n   389→    *Grounds*: Hell.lean axiom 4 (freedom_is_libertarian), moral responsibility,\n   390→    the possibility of self-exclusion from God. CCC §1730: \"God created man a\n   391→    rational being, conferring on him the dignity of a person who can initiate\n   392→    and control his own actions.\" -/\n   393→axiom t1_libertarian_free_will :\n   394→  ∀ (a : Agent), couldChooseOtherwise a\n   395→\n   396→/-- Provenance tag for T1. -/\n   397→def t1_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Sir 15:14; Trent Session 6\"\n   398→\n   399→/-- **T2. GRACE_PRESERVES_FREEDOM**: Divine initiative and human freedom are\n   400→    compatible; grace enables but does not coerce cooperation.\n   401→\n   402→    *Source*: Council of Trent, Session 6, Chapter 5: \"Free will, moved and\n   403→    excited by God… can reject [grace].\" Canon 4: anathema on the claim that\n   404→    free will \"does nothing whatever and is merely passive.\" Phil 2:12-13\n   405→    (\"work out your own salvation with fear and trembling, for it is God who\n   406→    works in you\") provides the scriptural basis.\n   407→\n   408→    *Grounds*: Grace.lean axiom 22 (divine_initiative_preserves_freedom),\n   409→    Justification.lean axiom 24 (human_cooperation_in_justification).\n   410→    CCC §2002: \"God's free initiative demands man's free response.\" -/\n   411→axiom t2_grace_preserves_freedom :\n   412→  ∀ (p : Person) (g : Grace),\n   413→    graceGiven p g → (cooperatesWithGrace p g ∨ ¬ cooperatesWithGrace p g)\n   414→\n   415→/-- Provenance tag for T2. -/\n   416→def t2_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Phil 2:12-13; Trent Session 6\"\n   417→\n   418→/-- **T3. SACRAMENTAL_EFFICACY**: Sacraments are effective signs — they confer\n   419→    the grace they signify (ex opere operato).\n   420→\n   421→    *Source*: Council of Trent, Session 7, Canon 8: \"If anyone says that by\n   422→    the said sacraments… grace is not conferred… but that faith alone in the\n   423→    divine promise suffices for the obtaining of grace: let him be anathema.\"\n   424→    John 3:5 (\"unless one is born of water and the Spirit\") and Acts 2:38\n   425→    (\"be baptized… for the forgiveness of your sins\") provide scriptural basis.\n   426→\n   427→    *Grounds*: Justification.lean axiom 25 (baptism_confers_justification).\n   428→    CCC §1127: \"Celebrated worthily in faith, the sacraments confer the grace\n   429→    that they signify.\" -/\n   430→axiom t3_sacramental_efficacy :\n   431→  ∀ (s : Sacrament), signifies s → confers s\n   432→\n   433→/-- Provenance tag for T3. -/\n   434→def t3_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Jn 3:5; Acts 2:38; Trent Session 7\"\n   435→\n   436→-- ============================================================================\n   437→-- Summary: the complete axiom set with provenance\n   438→--             s3_provenance)\n   450→  , (\"S4_UNIVERSAL_PROVIDENCE\",             s4_provenance)\n   451→  , (\"S5_SIN_SEPARATES\",                    s5_provenance)\n   452→  , (\"S6_MORAL_REALISM\", (\"S9_CONSCIENCE_BINDS\",                 s9_provenance)\n   456→  , (\"T1_LIBERTARIAN_FREE_WILL\",            t1_provenance)\n   457→  , (\"T2_GRACE_PRESERVES_FREEDOM\",          t2_provenance)\n   458→  , (\"T3_SACRAMENTAL_EFFICACY\",             t3_provenance)\n   459→  ]\n   460→\n   461→-- ============================================================================\n   462→-- Denominational tagging: which traditions accept each axiom\n   463→-- ============================================================================\n   464→\n   465→/-- Denominational scope of each base axiom.\n   466→    This is the key to answering \"was Luther right?\" — you can see\n   467→    exactly which axioms he accepted, rejected, or modified. -/\n   468→def axiomDenominationalScope : List (String × DenominationalTag) :=\n   469→  [ -- Philosophical: broadly shared (all Christians who engage philosophy)\n   470→    (\"P1_HYLOMORPHISM\",                  catholicOnly)      -- Lutherans don't shared across traditions\n   473→    -- Scriptural: ecumenical (broadly shared)\n   474→  , (\"S1_GOD_IS_LOVE\",                  ecumenical)\n   475→  , (\"S2_UNIVERSAL_SALVIFIC_WILL\",      catholicAndLutheran) -- Calvinists reject (limited atonement)\n   476→  , (\"S3_LAW_ON_HEARTS\",               ecumenical)\n   477→  , (\"S4_UNIVERSAL_PROVIDENCE\",         ecumenical)\n   478→  , (\"S5_SIN_SEPARATES\",               ecumenical)\n   479→  , (\"S6_MORAL_REALISM\",               ecumenical)\n   480→  , (\"S7_TELEOLOGICAL_FREEDOM\",        ecumenical)\n   481→  , (\"S8_GRACE_NECESSARY_TRANSFORMATIVE\",\n   482→      catholicOnly)     -- Luther: grace is forensic, not transformative\n   483→  , (\"S9_CONSCIENCE_BINDS\",            ecumenical)\n   484→    -- \"Grace is forensic (declarative), not transformative — Rom 4:5 'credits righteousness'\")\n   498→  , (\"T1 REPLACED\",  \"Will is in bondage to sin, not libertarianly free — Rom 7:15 'what I do I do not want to do'\")\n   499→  , (\"T2 REPLACED\",  \"Grace is monergistic (God alone acts), not synergistic — Eph 2:8-9 'not of works'\")\n   500→  , (\"T3 REJECTED\",  \"Sacraments are signs of grace received by faith, not causes — rejected ex opere operato\")\n   501→  , (\"ADDED: SOLA_SCRIPTURA\", \"Scripture alone is the supreme authority — 2 Tim 3:16 'all Scripture is God-breathed'\")\n   502→ {"parentUuid":"e476ddb3-1e71-43b4-bf5f-c4f1e095b561","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_014ifF71wN6RgYP3tEbB8f7v","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations.Basic\n     2→\n     3→/-!\n     4→# Apostolic Succession and Specific Authority Delegation\n     5→\n     6→The granular theory of how spiritual authority transfers from Christ\n     7→through the Apostles to their successors. Rather than claiming Christ\n     8→delegated ALL authority universally, we trace EACH specific delegation\n     9→to its Scripture verse.\n    10→\n    11→## The Protestant objection (and why it's right)\n    12→\n    13→A universal delegation claim (\"Christ had all authority and delegated\n    14→all of it\") is too strong. Christ had authority to calm storms and\n    15→raise the dead -- priests obviously cannot do that. The Catholic claim\n    16→is NOT \"priests can do everything Jesus did.\" It is: \"Jesus specifically\n    17→delegated THESE particular authorities, and we can cite chapter and\n    18→verse for each one.\"\n    19→\n    20→The delegation is specific, not universal.\n    21→\n    22→## The Catechism claims\n    23→\n    24→\"In order that the full and living Gospel might always be preserved in\n    25→the Church the apostles left bishops as their successors. They gave them\n    26→'their own position of teaching authority.'\" (CCC §77)\n    27→\n    28→\"The bishops have by divine institution taken the place of the apostles\n    29→as pastors of the Church.\" (CCC §862)\n    30→\n    31→## Scripture basis for EACH delegation\n    32→\n    33→- **Teaching**: Mt 28:19-20 (\"go and make disciples, teaching them\")\n    34→- **Baptizing**: Mt 28:19 (\"baptizing them in the name of...\")\n    35→- **Forgiving sins**: Jn 20:21-23 (\"if you forgive the sins of any...\")\n    36→- **Eucharist**: Lk 22:19 (\"do this in remembrance of me\")\n    37→- **Binding/loosing**: Mt 16:19, Mt 18:18 (\"whatever you bind on earth...\")\n    38→- **Anointing the sick**: Mk 6:13, Jas 5:14 (\"anoint with oil\")\n    39→- **Exorcism**: Mk 6:7, Lk 10:17 (\"authority over unclean spirits\")\n    40→- **Ordination**: 2 Tim 1:6 (\"the gift of God... through laying on of hands\")\n    41→\n    42→## Things Christ did that are NOT delegated\n    43→\n    44→- Calming storms / nature miracles -- no delegation verse\n    45→- Walking on water -- no delegation verse\n    46→- Raising the dead -- Peter did (Acts 9:40), but as a charismatic gift,\n    47→  not an office; no institutional delegation\n    48→- Forgiving sins by His own authority -- priests forgive in His name,\n    49→  not their own (instrumental cause, not principal cause)\n    50→- Being the source of grace -- priests are channels, not sources\n    51→\n    52→## Denominational scope\n    53→\n    54→- Catholic: Full acceptance -- apostolic succession is constitutive of\n    55→  the Church's authority.\n    56→- Orthodox: Full acceptance -- same model, disputed jurisdiction.\n    57→- Lutheran: Partial -- values historical continuity but does not require\n    58→  unbroken succession for valid ministry.\n    59→- Reformed/Non-denom: Generally rejected -- authority comes from\n    60→  Scripture and the gathered community, not a succession chain.\n    61→-/\n    62→\n    63→namespace Catlib\n    64→\n    65→/-!\n    66→## Denominational scope for authority claims\n    67→\n    68→We need a way to tag which traditions accept each specific delegation.\n    69→-/\n    70→\n    71→/-- Which denominations accept a specific authority delegation. -/\n    72→structure DelegationScope where\n    73→  /-- Which traditions accept this delegation -/\n    74→  acceptedBy : List Denomination\n    75→  /-- Brief note on qualifications or disagreements -/\n    76→  note : String\n    77→\n    78→/-- Accepted by all major Christian traditions. -/\n    79→def delegationEcumenical : DelegationScope :=\n    80→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical], note := \"broadly shared\" }\n    81→\n    82→/-- Accepted by Catholic and Orthodox but contested by Protestants. -/\n    83→def delegationCatholicOrthodox : DelegationScope :=\n    84→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic], note := \"Catholic + Orthodox; contested by Protestants\" }\n    85→\n    86→/-- Accepted only under Catholic interpretation. -/\n    87→def delegationCatholicSpecific : DelegationScope :=\n    88→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic], note := \"Catholic distinctive\" }\n    89→\n    90→/-!\n    91→## The granular authority delegation model\n    92→\n    93→Instead of \"Christ delegates ALL authority,\" we model each specific\n    94→delegation with its Scripture reference, denominational scope, and\n    95→whether it requires apostolic succession to extend beyond the original\n    96→Apostles.\n    97→-/\n    98→\n    99→/-- A domain of spiritual authority -- what the authority covers.\n   100→    Each domain has its own Scripture basis for both Christ possessing\n   101→    it and Christ delegating it. -/\n   102→structure AuthorityDomain where\n   103→  name : String\n   104→  /-- Scripture basis for Christ having this authority -/\n   105→  christHasIt : Prop\n   106→  /-- Scripture basis for Christ delegating it to the Apostles -/\n   107→  christDelegatedIt : Prop\n   108→\n   109→/-- A specific delegation of authority from Christ to the Apostles.\n   110→    Each delegation is individually grounded in Scripture with its\n   111→    denominational scope and succession requirement. -/\n   112→structure SpecificDelegation where\n   113→  /-- The domain of authority being delegated -/\n   114→  domain : AuthorityDomain\n   115→  /-- The Scripture verse(s) where Christ delegates this authority -/\n   116→  scriptureRef : String\n   117→  /-- Which traditions accept this delegation -/\n   118→  scope : DelegationScope\n   119→  /-- Whether extending this beyond the original Apostles requires\n   120→      apostolic succession (the key contested question) -/\n   121→  requiresSuccession : Bool\n   122→\n   123→/-- A link in the authority chain. -/\n   124→structure ChainLink where\n   125→  domain : AuthorityDomain\n   126→  holder : String  -- Role name (Christ, Apostle, Bishop, Priest)\n   127→  source : String  -- Who delegated it\n   128→  scriptureRef : String\n   129→\n   130→/-!\n   131→## Specific authority domains\n   132→\n   133→These instantiate the model for specific sacramental powers.\n   134→Each is individually defined with its own Scripture basis.\n   135→Defined BEFORE the axioms so they can be referenced.\n   136→-/\n   137→\n   138→/-- The domain of teaching with authority.\n   139→    Scripture: Mt 28:19-20 (\"Go and make disciples... teaching them\"). -/\n   140→def teachingDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   141→  { name := \"teaching\"\n   142→    christHasIt := True  -- Mt 7:29 (\"he taught as one having authority\")\n   143→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Mt 28:19-20\n   144→  }\n   145→\n   146→/-- The domain of baptism.\n   147→    Scripture: Mt 28:19 (\"baptizing them in the name of the Father\n   148→    and of the Son and of the Holy Spirit\"). -/\n   149→def baptismDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   150→  { name := \"baptism\"\n   151→    christHasIt := True  -- Jn 1:33\n   152→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Mt 28:19\n   153→  }\n   154→\n   155→/-- The domain of forgiving sins (absolution).\n   156→    Scripture: Jn 20:23 (\"If you forgive the sins of any, they are\n   157→    forgiven them\"); Mt 16:19 (\"whatever you bind on earth shall be\n   158→    bound in heaven\"). -/\n   159→def absolutionDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   160→  { name := \"absolution\"\n   161→    christHasIt := True  -- Mk 2:10 (\"the Son of Man has authority to forgive sins\")\n   162→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Jn 20:23\n   163→  }\n   164→\n   165→/-- The domain of the Eucharist (the Lord's Supper).\n   166→    Scripture: Lk 22:19 (\"Do this in remembrance of me\");\n   167→    1 Cor 11:24-25. -/\n   168→def eucharistDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   169→  { name := \"eucharist\"\n   170→    christHasIt := True  -- Lk 22:19 (He instituted it)\n   171→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Lk 22:19 (\"do this\")\n   172→  }\n   173→\n   174→/-- The domain of binding and loosing.\n   175→    Scripture: Mt 16:19, Mt 18:18 (\"whatever you bind on earth\n   176→    shall be bound in heaven\"). -/\n   177→def bindingLoosingDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   178→  { name := \"binding_and_loosing\"\n   179→    christHasIt := True  -- Mt 16:19\n   180→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Mt 16:19, Mt 18:18\n   181→  }\n   182→\n   183→/-- The domain of anointing the sick.\n   184→    Scripture: Mk 6:13 (\"anointed with oil many who were sick\"),\n   185→    Jas 5:14. -/\n   186→def anointingDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   187→  { name := \"anointing_sick\"\n   188→    christHasIt := True  -- Mt 4:23\n   189→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Mk 6:13, Jas 5:14\n   190→  }\n   191→\n   192→/-- The domain of exorcism.\n   193→    Scripture: Mk 1:27, Mk 6:7, Lk 10:17. -/\n   194→def exorcismDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   195→  { name := \"exorcism\"\n   196→    christHasIt := True  -- Mk 1:27\n   197→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- Mk 6:7\n   198→  }\n   199→\n   200→/-- The domain of ordination (laying on of hands).\n   201→    Scripture: 2 Tim 1:6, Titus 1:5, Acts 14:23. -/\n   202→def ordinationDomain : AuthorityDomain :=\n   203→  { name := \"ordination\"\n   204→    christHasIt := True  -- Jn 15:16\n   205→    christDelegatedIt := True  -- 2 Tim 1:6, Titus 1:5\n   206→  }\n   207→\n   208→/-!\n   209→## Christ's authority: universal but NOT universally delegated\n   210→\n   211→Christ has all authority (Mt 28:18) -- this is ecumenical. But He\n   212→delegated SPECIFIC authorities, not all of them. A priest cannot\n   213→calm storms. The delegation was targeted.\n   214→-/\n   215→\n   216→/-- AXIOM (Mt 28:18): Christ has all authority.\n   217→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mt 28:18 (\"All authority in heaven and on\n   218→    earth has been given to me\").\n   219→    Denominational scope: Ecumenical -- all Christians accept this.\n   220→\n   221→    NOTE: This does NOT mean all authority was DELEGATED. Christ\n   222→    possesses authorities He did not delegate (nature miracles,\n   223→    raising the dead by His own power, etc.). -/\n   224→axiom christ_has_all_authority :\n   225→  ∀ (d : AuthorityDomain), d.christHasIt\n   226→\n   227→/-!\n   228→## Individual delegation axioms -- each with its own Scripture verse\n   229→\n   230→The key insight: we do NOT assert \"Christ delegates all authority.\"\n   231→Instead, each delegation is a separate axiom with its own Scripture\n   232→reference. A Protestant can accept some of these (teaching, baptism)\n   233→while rejecting others (absolution, eucharist). The denominational\n   234→tags track this.\n   235→-/\n   236→\n   237→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates TEACHING authority to the Apostles.\n   238→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mt 28:19-20 (\"Go therefore and make\n   239→    disciples of all nations... teaching them to observe all that\n   240→    I have commanded you\").\n   241→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL -- virtually all Christians\n   242→    accept that Jesus commissioned the Apostles to teach. -/\n   243→axiom christ_delegates_teaching :\n   244→  teachingDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   245→\n   246→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates BAPTISM authority to the Apostles.\n   247→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mt 28:19 (\"Go therefore and make disciples\n   248→    of all nations, baptizing them in the name of the Father and of\n   249→    the Son and of the Holy Spirit\").\n   250→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL -- virtually all Christians\n   251→    accept that Jesus instituted baptism. -/\n   252→axiom christ_delegates_baptism :\n   253→  baptismDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   254→\n   255→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates authority to FORGIVE SINS to the Apostles.\n   256→    Provenance: [Scripture] Jn 20:21-23 (\"Receive the Holy Spirit.\n   257→    If you forgive the sins of any, they are forgiven them; if you\n   258→    retain the sins of any, they are retained.\").\n   259→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox accept this as a\n   260→    sacramental delegation. Protestants read it as a general\n   261→    commission to proclaim the gospel of forgiveness.\n   262→    NOTE: Priests forgive IN CHRIST'S NAME, not by their own\n   263→    authority. They are instrumental causes, not principal causes. -/\n   264→axiom christ_delegates_absolution :\n   265→  absolutionDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   266→\n   267→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates the EUCHARISTIC authority to the Apostles.\n   268→    Provenance: [Scripture] Lk 22:19 (\"Do this in remembrance of me\");\n   269→    1 Cor 11:24-25 (Paul repeats the command).\n   270→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox read \"do this\" as\n   271→    instituting the Eucharistic sacrifice. Protestants read it as\n   272→    a memorial meal. The delegation is agreed; the NATURE of what\n   273→    is delegated is the dispute. -/\n   274→axiom christ_delegates_eucharist :\n   275→  eucharistDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   276→\n   277→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates BINDING AND LOOSING authority.\n   278→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mt 16:19 (\"I will give you the keys of\n   279→    the kingdom of heaven, and whatever you bind on earth shall be\n   280→    bound in heaven, and whatever you loose on earth shall be loosed\n   281→    in heaven\"); Mt 18:18 (extended to all the Apostles).\n   282→    Denominational scope: Catholics read this as judicial authority\n   283→    over sin and discipline. Protestants read it as teaching authority\n   284→    (declaring what is permitted/forbidden). -/\n   285→axiom christ_delegates_binding_loosing :\n   286→  bindingLoosingDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   287→\n   288→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates authority to ANOINT THE SICK.\n   289→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mk 6:13 (\"They cast out many demons and\n   290→    anointed with oil many who were sick and healed them\");\n   291→    Jas 5:14 (\"Is anyone among you sick? Let him call for the elders\n   292→    of the church, and let them pray over him, anointing him with oil\n   293→    in the name of the Lord\").\n   294→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox accept this as a\n   295→    sacramental delegation. Most Protestants do not practice\n   296→    sacramental anointing of the sick. -/\n   297→axiom christ_delegates_anointing :\n   298→  anointingDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   299→\n   300→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates EXORCISM authority to the Apostles.\n   301→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mk 6:7 (\"He gave them authority over\n   302→    unclean spirits\"); Lk 10:17 (\"Lord, even the demons are subject\n   303→    to us in your name\").\n   304→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox accept this. Some\n   305→    Protestants practice exorcism (charismatic/Pentecostal traditions)\n   306→    but ground it differently (in the name of Jesus directly, not\n   307→    through apostolic succession). -/\n   308→axiom christ_delegates_exorcism :\n   309→  exorcismDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   310→\n   311→/-- AXIOM: Christ delegates ORDINATION authority (the power to\n   312→    transmit authority through the laying on of hands).\n   313→    Provenance: [Scripture] 2 Tim 1:6 (\"the gift of God that is in\n   314→    you through the laying on of my hands\"); Titus 1:5 (\"appoint\n   315→    elders in every town as I directed you\"); Acts 14:23 (\"they\n   316→    appointed elders for them in every church\").\n   317→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox accept this as\n   318→    sacramental ordination with ontological character. Protestants\n   319→    who practice ordination generally see it as functional\n   320→    appointment, not sacramental. -/\n   321→axiom christ_delegates_ordination :\n   322→  ordinationDomain.christDelegatedIt\n   323→\n   324→/-!\n   325→## Apostolic succession (the contested step)\n   326→\n   327→This is the axiom that extends delegation beyond the original Apostles.\n   328→Without it, the chain stops at the first generation. Catholics and\n   329→Orthodox accept it. Most Protestants do not.\n   330→-/\n   331→\n   332→/-- AXIOM (CCC §77, §862): Apostolic succession -- bishops are the\n   333→    Apostles' successors and inherit their delegated authorities.\n   334→    Provenance: [Tradition] CCC §77, §862; [Scripture] 2 Tim 2:2,\n   335→    Titus 1:5, Acts 1:20-26.\n   336→    Denominational scope: Catholic + Orthodox. This is the axiom\n   337→    that Protestants reject or reinterpret.\n   338→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: The chain is unbroken. Authority transfers\n   339→    validly across generations without loss or expiration. -/\n   340→axiom apostolic_succession_general :\n   341→  ∀ (d : AuthorityDomain),\n   342→    d.christDelegatedIt →\n   343→    -- Bishops possess this authority as successors of the Apostles\n   344→    True\n   345→\n   346→/-- AXIOM: Bishops can delegate specific authorities to priests.\n   347→    Provenance: [Tradition] CCC §1562-1567.\n   348→    Not all episcopal authority is delegated -- some (like ordination)\n   349→    bishops reserve to themselves. -/\n   350→axiom episcopal_delegation :\n   351→  ∀ (_d : AuthorityDomain),\n   352→    -- A bishop can authorize a priest to exercise this authority\n   353→    -- (with conditions -- e.g., exorcism needs explicit permission,\n   354→    -- absolution is given at ordination for most cases)\n   355→    True\n   356→\n   357→/-!\n   358→## The specific delegation registry\n   359→\n   360→This collects all the delegations with their metadata: Scripture,\n   361→denominational scope, and succession requirement.\n   362→-/\n   363→\n   364→/-- The complete registry of specific delegations from Christ. -/\n   365→def specificDelegations : List SpecificDelegation :=\n   366→  [ -- ECUMENICAL: Protestants already accept these\n   367→    { domain := teachingDomain\n   368→      scriptureRef := \"Mt 28:19-20\"\n   369→      scope := delegationEcumenical\n   370→      requiresSuccession := false }\n   371→  , { domain := baptismDomain\n   372→      scriptureRef := \"Mt 28:19\"\n   373→      scope := delegationEcumenical\n   374→      requiresSuccession := false }\n   375→    -- CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX: contested by Protestants\n   376→  , { domain := absolutionDomain\n   377→      scriptureRef := \"Jn 20:21-23\"\n   378→      scope := delegationCatholicOrthodox\n   379→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   380→  , { domain := eucharistDomain\n   381→      scriptureRef := \"Lk 22:19; 1 Cor 11:24-25\"\n   382→      scope := delegationCatholicOrthodox\n   383→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   384→  , { domain := anointingDomain\n   385→      scriptureRef := \"Mk 6:13; Jas 5:14\"\n   386→      scope := delegationCatholicOrthodox\n   387→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   388→  , { domain := exorcismDomain\n   389→      scriptureRef := \"Mk 6:7; Lk 10:17\"\n   390→      scope := delegationCatholicOrthodox\n   391→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   392→    -- CATHOLIC DISTINCTIVE: strongest claims\n   393→  , { domain := bindingLoosingDomain\n   394→      scriptureRef := \"Mt 16:19; Mt 18:18\"\n   395→      scope := delegationCatholicSpecific\n   396→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   397→  , { domain := ordinationDomain\n   398→      scriptureRef := \"2 Tim 1:6; Titus 1:5; Acts 14:23\"\n   399→      scope := delegationCatholicOrthodox\n   400→      requiresSuccession := true }\n   401→  ]\n   402→\n   403→/-!\n   404→## Authority chain theorems -- specific, not universal\n   405→\n   406→Instead of one universal theorem saying \"Christ delegated everything,\"\n   407→we prove the authority chain for EACH specific domain. A Protestant\n   408→reader can see exactly which chains they accept and which they reject.\n   409→-/\n   410→\n   411→/-- The specific authority chain theorem: for a domain where Christ\n   412→    SPECIFICALLY delegated authority (with a cited verse), the chain\n   413→    extends through apostolic succession to bishops and priests.\n   414→\n   415→    This replaces the old universal claim. The argument is:\n   416→    1. Christ has authority over this domain (Mt 28:18, plus domain-specific verse)\n   417→    2. Christ specifically delegated THIS authority (domain-specific verse)\n   418→    3. The delegation extends through succession (Catholic + Orthodox axiom)\n   419→\n   420→    The Protestant who accepts steps 1-2 for teaching and baptism but\n   421→    rejects step 3 (succession) will get a chain that stops at the\n   422→    Apostles. That is a coherent position -- and it is exactly where the\n   423→    real disagreement lies. -/\n   424→theorem authority_chain_specific (d : AuthorityDomain)\n   425→    (h_delegated : d.christDelegatedIt) :\n   426→    d.christHasIt ∧ d.christDelegatedIt := by\n   427→  exact ⟨christ_has_all_authority d, h_delegated⟩\n   428→\n   429→/-- Teaching authority chain -- ECUMENICAL.\n   430→    Both Catholics and Protestants accept that Christ commissioned\n   431→    the Apostles to teach. The disagreement is about whether this\n   432→    authority transfers through succession. -/\n   433→theorem teaching_authority :\n   434→    teachingDomain.christHasIt ∧ teachingDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   435→  authority_chain_specific teachingDomain christ_delegates_teaching\n   436→\n   437→/-- Baptism authority chain -- ECUMENICAL.\n   438→    Both Catholics and Protestants accept that Christ instituted\n   439→    baptism and commissioned the Apostles to baptize. -/\n   440→theorem baptism_authority :\n   441→    baptismDomain.christHasIt ∧ baptismDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   442→  authority_chain_specific baptismDomain christ_delegates_baptism\n   443→\n   444→/-- Absolution authority chain -- Catholic + Orthodox.\n   445→    Protestants read Jn 20:21-23 as a general commission to proclaim\n   446→    forgiveness, not a sacramental delegation. -/\n   447→theorem absolution_authority :\n   448→    absolutionDomain.christHasIt ∧ absolutionDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   449→  authority_chain_specific absolutionDomain christ_delegates_absolution\n   450→\n   451→/-- Eucharist authority chain -- Catholic + Orthodox.\n   452→    Protestants agree Christ said \"do this\" but read it as a memorial\n   453→    command, not a sacrificial delegation. -/\n   454→theorem eucharist_authority :\n   455→    eucharistDomain.christHasIt ∧ eucharistDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   456→  authority_chain_specific eucharistDomain christ_delegates_eucharist\n   457→\n   458→/-- Binding/loosing authority chain -- Catholic distinctive.\n   459→    Protestants read \"binding and loosing\" as teaching authority\n   460→    (declaring what is permitted), not judicial authority over sin. -/\n   461→theorem binding_loosing_authority :\n   462→    bindingLoosingDomain.christHasIt ∧ bindingLoosingDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   463→  authority_chain_specific bindingLoosingDomain christ_delegates_binding_loosing\n   464→\n   465→/-- Anointing the sick authority chain -- Catholic + Orthodox.\n   466→    James 5:14 is one of the strongest proof-texts since it explicitly\n   467→    mentions elders and anointing with oil. -/\n   468→theorem anointing_authority :\n   469→    anointingDomain.christHasIt ∧ anointingDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   470→  authority_chain_specific anointingDomain christ_delegates_anointing\n   471→\n   472→/-- Exorcism authority chain -- Catholic + Orthodox.\n   473→    Some Protestants (charismatic/Pentecostal) also practice exorcism\n   474→    but ground it in direct invocation of Jesus' name, not succession. -/\n   475→theorem exorcism_authority :\n   476→    exorcismDomain.christHasIt ∧ exorcismDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   477→  authority_chain_specific exorcismDomain christ_delegates_exorcism\n   478→\n   479→/-- Ordination authority chain -- Catholic + Orthodox.\n   480→    Protestants who practice ordination see it as functional appointment,\n   481→    not sacramental transmission of ontological character. -/\n   482→theorem ordination_authority :\n   483→    ordinationDomain.christHasIt ∧ ordinationDomain.christDelegatedIt :=\n   484→  authority_chain_specific ordinationDomain christ_delegates_ordination\n   485→\n   486→/-!\n   487→## What is NOT delegated\n   488→\n   489→These are authorities Christ possessed but did NOT delegate to the\n   490→Apostles or their successors. Modeling them makes the specificity\n   491→of the actual delegations more visible.\n   492→-/\n   493→\n   494→/-- An undelegated authority -- something Christ has but did not give\n   495→    to the Church. -/\n   496→structure UndelegatedAuthority where\n   497→  name : String\n   498→  /-- Scripture showing Christ has it -/\n   499→  christHasItRef : String\n   500→  /-- Why it was not delegated -/\n   501→  reason : String\n   502→\n   503→/-- Nature miracles -- Christ commands creation but did not delegate\n   504→    this to the Church. -/\n   505→def natureMiracles : UndelegatedAuthority :=\n   506→  { name := \"authority_over_nature\"\n   507→    christHasItRef := \"Mt 8:26-27 (calming the storm); Mt 14:25 (walking on water)\"\n   508→    reason := \"No delegation verse. No commission to calm storms or walk on water.\" }\n   509→\n   510→/-- Self-originated forgiveness -- Christ forgives by His own authority;\n   511→    priests forgive in His name (instrumental cause, not principal). -/\n   512→def selfOriginatedForgiveness : UndelegatedAuthority :=\n   513→  { name := \"forgiveness_by_own_authority\"\n   514→    christHasItRef := \"Mk 2:10 ('the Son of Man has authority on earth to forgive sins')\"\n   515→    reason := \"Priests forgive in persona Christi, not by their own power. The source of forgiveness remains God.\" }\n   516→\n   517→/-- Being the source of grace -- priests are channels of grace, not\n   518→    its origin. Grace comes from God; sacraments transmit it. -/\n   519→def sourceOfGrace : UndelegatedAuthority :=\n   520→  { name := \"source_of_grace\"\n   521→    christHasItRef := \"Jn 1:16 ('from his fullness we have all received, grace upon grace')\"\n   522→    reason := \"Priests administer sacraments as instruments. They do not generate grace.\" }\n   523→\n   524→/-- Registry of undelegated authorities, for contrast. -/\n   525→def undelegatedAuthorities : List UndelegatedAuthority :=\n   526→  [ natureMiracles\n   527→  , selfOriginatedForgiveness\n   528→  , sourceOfGrace ]\n   529→\n   530→/-!\n   531→## Denominational summary\n   532→\n   533→The Protestant who asks \"where does priestly authority come from?\"\n   534→can now see the precise answer:\n   535→\n   536→1. Christ possesses all authority (ECUMENICAL -- Mt 28:18)\n   537→2. Christ SPECIFICALLY delegated certain authorities with cited verses\n   538→3. Some of those delegations are ecumenical (teaching, baptism)\n   539→4. Others are contested (absolution, eucharist, binding/loosing,\n   540→   anointing, exorcism, ordination)\n   541→5. The contested delegations require apostolic succession (step 3 of\n   542→   the chain) to extend beyond the original Apostles\n   543→6. Apostolic succession is the load-bearing axiom that Protestants reject\n   544→\n   545→The Catholic is NOT claiming priests can do everything Jesus did.\n   546→The Catholic is claiming Jesus specifically delegated THESE particular\n   547→authorities -- and can cite chapter and verse for each one. The\n   548→delegation is specific, and the disagreement is about whether the\n   549→chain of transmission is unbroken.\n   550→-/\n   551→\n   552→end Catlib\n   553→"}]},"uuid":"4672edce-8258-4058-8b3c-eb781ee1f9bf","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:39:54.078Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e476ddb3-1e71-43b4-bf5f-c4f1e095b561","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}
