{"parentUuid":"4ea17d69-9e14-4d0a-b1ba-e51ac336a18b","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01B1rw5P1bDjmUfwddbEmsVX","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→\n     3→/-!\n     4→# CCC §1030-1032: Purgatory as Post-Mortem Purification\n     5→\n     6→## The Catechism claims\n     7→\n     8→\"All who die in God's grace and friendship, but still imperfectly purified,\n     9→are indeed assured of their eternal salvation; but after death they undergo\n    10→purification, so as to achieve the holiness necessary to enter the joy of\n    11→heaven.\" (§1030)\n    12→\n    13→\"The Church gives the name Purgatory to this final purification.\" (§1031)\n    14→\n    15→\"From the beginning the Church has honored the memory of the dead and offered\n    16→prayers in suffrage for them, above all the Eucharistic sacrifice, so that,\n    17→thus purified, they may attain the beatific vision of God.\" (§1032)\n    18→\n    19→## The argument chain\n    20→\n    21→1. Holiness is required for heaven (nothing impure can enter — Rev 21:27)\n    22→2. Some die in God's grace but imperfectly purified\n    23→3. These persons undergo a purification AFTER death\n    24→4. This purification is temporary (not eternal like hell)\n    25→5. The purified WILL reach heaven (assured salvation)\n    26→6. The living can help the dead through prayer (intercession crosses death)\n    27→\n    28→## Prediction\n    29→\n    30→I expect this to **expose a deep tension** with Hell.lean. Hell says death\n    31→is final (axiom 3: `death_is_final` — no post-mortem change of state).\n    32→Purgatory says post-mortem purification happens. These look contradictory.\n    33→\n    34→The Catholic resolution: death is final for the CHOICE (you cannot switch\n    35→from rejecting God to accepting Him), but not final for PURIFICATION\n    36→(you can be cleaned up after choosing God). This distinction is not made\n    37→explicit in the Catechism — it is a hidden structural assumption.\n    38→\n    39→## Findings\n    40→\n    41→- **Prediction vs. reality**: Confirmed — tension with Hell.lean is real and\n    42→  requires explicit resolution. The `death_is_final` axiom from Hell.lean\n    43→  must be reinterpreted as finality of CHOICE, not finality of all change.\n    44→- **Hidden assumptions**:\n    45→  1. Post-mortem change is possible (tension with death-is-final!)\n    46→  2. Temporal process after death (how does time work for disembodied souls?)\n    47→  3. Prayer efficacy crosses the life/death boundary\n    48→  4. Holiness is a SPECTRUM, not binary saved/damned\n    49→  5. The strongest Scripture (2 Macc 12:46) requires the 73-book canon\n    50→- **Denominational scope**: Catholic only. Protestants reject purgatory.\n    51→  Orthodox have a related but distinct concept (toll houses / aerial realm).\n    52→- **Assessment**: Tier 3 — multiple hidden premises, genuine tension with\n    53→  another formalized doctrine (Hell), and critical dependency on L4 (canon).\n    54→-/\n    55→\n    56→namespace Catlib.Creed\n    57→\n    58→open Catlib\n    59→\n    60→/-!\n    61→## Core types for purgatory\n    62→-/\n    63→\n    64→/-- The degree of holiness a person possesses.\n    65→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Holiness is a spectrum, not binary.\n    66→    The Catechism never argues for this — it assumes it. If holiness\n    67→    were binary (holy / not-holy), purgatory would be unnecessary:\n    68→    you either have it or you don't. Purgatory requires DEGREES. -/\n    69→opaque HolinessDegree : Type\n    70→\n    71→/-- Ordering on holiness degrees — some are higher than others. -/\n    72→opaque holinessLt : HolinessDegree → HolinessDegree → Prop\n    73→\n    74→/-- The threshold of holiness required for heaven. -/\n    75→axiom heavenThreshold : HolinessDegree\n    76→\n    77→/-- The holiness degree of a given person. -/\n    78→axiom personHoliness : Person → HolinessDegree\n    79→\n    80→/-- Whether a person died in God's grace (chose God, even if imperfectly purified). -/\n    81→opaque diedInGrace : Person → Prop\n    82→\n    83→/-- Whether a person died in mortal sin (chose against God). -/\n    84→opaque diedInMortalSin : Person → Prop\n    85→\n    86→/-- Whether a person is fully purified (holiness meets the threshold). -/\n    87→opaque fullyPurified : Person → Prop\n    88→\n    89→/-- Whether a person is in the state of purgatorial purification. -/\n    90→opaque inPurgatory : Person → Prop\n    91→\n    92→/-- Whether a living person prays for a dead person. -/\n    93→opaque praysFor : Person → Person → Prop\n    94→\n    95→/-- Whether prayer aids the purification of a person. -/\n    96→opaque prayerAidsPurification : Person → Prop\n    97→\n    98→/-- Whether a person has attained the beatific vision (heaven). -/\n    99→opaque attainsBeatificVision : Person → Prop\n   100→\n   101→/-!\n   102→## Axioms: CCC §1030-1032\n   103→\n   104→Each axiom is tagged with its Catechism source and any hidden assumptions.\n   105→-/\n   106→\n   107→/-- AXIOM 1 (§1030 + Rev 21:27): Nothing impure can enter heaven.\n   108→    Holiness at or above the threshold is required for the beatific vision.\n   109→    Provenance: [Scripture] Rev 21:27 — \"Nothing unclean will enter it.\"\n   110→    Also: Heb 12:14 — \"without holiness no one will see the Lord.\"\n   111→    DENOMINATIONAL: Ecumenical — Protestants agree holiness is required\n   112→    for heaven. They disagree about how it is achieved. -/\n   113→axiom holiness_required_for_heaven :\n   114→  ∀ (p : Person), attainsBeatificVision p → fullyPurified p\n   115→\n   116→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 1. -/\n   117→def purg_ax1_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rev 21:27; Heb 12:14\"\n   118→def purg_ax1_tag : DenominationalTag := ecumenical\n   119→\n   120→/-- AXIOM 2 (§1030): A middle state exists. Some die in grace but\n   121→    imperfectly purified — they chose God, but still carry impurity.\n   122→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1030\n   123→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: \"Imperfectly purified\" presupposes that holiness\n   124→    is a spectrum, not binary. If holiness were binary, you'd either\n   125→    be purified or not — no middle ground.\n   126→    DENOMINATIONAL: Catholic only. Protestants hold that Christ's\n   127→    righteousness covers the believer completely at justification\n   128→    (simul justus et peccator), so no further purification is needed. -/\n   129→axiom imperfect_purification_exists :\n   130→  ∃ (p : Person), diedInGrace p ∧ ¬fullyPurified p\n   131→\n   132→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 2. -/\n   133→def purg_ax2_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.definition 1030\n   134→def purg_ax2_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   135→\n   136→/-- AXIOM 3 (§1030): Post-mortem purification occurs.\n   137→    Those who die in grace but imperfectly purified undergo purification\n   138→    after death to achieve the holiness necessary for heaven.\n   139→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1030\n   140→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION 1: Post-mortem change is possible. This is in\n   141→    TENSION with Hell.lean's `death_is_final` axiom!\n   142→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION 2: There is a temporal process after death.\n   143→    How does time work for a disembodied soul? The Catechism never\n   144→    addresses this. -/\n   145→axiom post_mortem_purification :\n   146→  ∀ (p : Person), diedInGrace p → ¬fullyPurified p → inPurgatory p\n   147→\n   148→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 3. -/\n   149→def purg_ax3_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.definition 1030\n   150→def purg_ax3_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   151→\n   152→/-- AXIOM 4 (§1030): Purgatory is temporary — the purified WILL reach heaven.\n   153→    Unlike hell, which is permanent self-exclusion, purgatory has an end.\n   154→    \"They are indeed assured of their eternal salvation.\"\n   155→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1030\n   156→    DENOMINATIONAL: Catholic only. This is what distinguishes purgatory\n   157→    from hell — it is a state of ASSURED salvation, not uncertainty. -/\n   158→axiom purgatory_leads_to_heaven :\n   159→  ∀ (p : Person), inPurgatory p → attainsBeatificVision p\n   160→\n   161→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 4. -/\n   162→def purg_ax4_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.definition 1030\n   163→def purg_ax4_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   164→\n   165→/-- AXIOM 5 (§1032): Prayer for the dead is efficacious.\n   166→    The living can aid the purification of the dead through prayer,\n   167→    especially the Eucharistic sacrifice.\n   168→    Provenance: [Scripture] 2 Macc 12:46 — \"It is a holy and wholesome\n   169→    thought to pray for the dead, that they may be loosed from sins.\"\n   170→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Prayer efficacy crosses the life/death boundary.\n   171→    The Catechism assumes this without argument.\n   172→    CRITICAL DEPENDENCY: 2 Macc 12:46 is in a Deuterocanonical book.\n   173→    Under Luther's L4 (66-book canon), this verse is not Scripture.\n   174→    The scriptural case for prayer for the dead collapses under L4. -/\n   175→axiom prayer_aids_dead :\n   176→  ∀ (living dead : Person), praysFor living dead → inPurgatory dead →\n   177→    prayerAidsPurification dead\n   178→\n   179→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 5. -/\n   180→def purg_ax5_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"2 Macc 12:46\"\n   181→def purg_ax5_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   182→\n   183→/-- AXIOM 6: Those who die in mortal sin do NOT enter purgatory.\n   184→    Purgatory is only for those who die in God's grace.\n   185→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1033 (from Hell.lean's scope)\n   186→    This axiom distinguishes purgatory from hell: the person in\n   187→    purgatory CHOSE God. The person in hell REJECTED God. -/\n   188→axiom mortal_sin_excludes_purgatory :\n   189→  ∀ (p : Person), diedInMortalSin p → ¬inPurgatory p\n   190→\n   191→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 6. -/\n   192→def purg_ax6_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.definition 1033\n   193→def purg_ax6_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   194→\n   195→/-!\n   196→## Key theorems\n   197→-/\n   198→\n   199→/-- AXIOM 7: Those who die in grace AND are already fully purified go\n   200→    directly to heaven (no purgatory needed).\n   201→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1023\n   202→    STRUCTURAL NOTE: This axiom is REQUIRED to prove that dying in grace\n   203→    guarantees heaven. Without it, we can only show the imperfectly-purified\n   204→    reach heaven (via purgatory). The already-purified case needs its own\n   205→    axiom — the Catechism assumes this without stating it as a separate claim. -/\n   206→axiom purified_in_grace_sees_god :\n   207→  ∀ (p : Person), diedInGrace p → fullyPurified p → attainsBeatificVision p\n   208→\n   209→/-- Provenance tag for axiom 7. -/\n   210→def purg_ax7_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.definition 1023\n   211→def purg_ax7_tag : DenominationalTag := ecumenical\n   212→\n   213→/-- THEOREM 1: Everyone in purgatory will see God.\n   214→    This follows directly from axiom 4: purgatory leads to heaven.\n   215→    The important structural point: purgatory is a state of HOPE, not fear.\n   216→    The outcome is certain. -/\n   217→theorem purgatory_guarantees_vision :\n   218→    ∀ (p : Person), inPurgatory p → attainsBeatificVision p :=\n   219→  fun (p : Person) (h : inPurgatory p) => purgatory_leads_to_heaven p h\n   220→\n   221→/-- THEOREM 2: Purgatory results in full purification.\n   222→    If someone is in purgatory, they will attain the beatific vision.\n   223→    And the beatific vision requires full purification (axiom 1).\n   224→    So purgatory results in full purification. -/\n   225→theorem purgatory_achieves_holiness :\n   226→    ∀ (p : Person), inPurgatory p → fullyPurified p :=\n   227→  fun (p : Person) (h : inPurgatory p) =>\n   228→    holiness_required_for_heaven p (purgatory_leads_to_heaven p h)\n   229→\n   230→/-- THEOREM 3: Dying in grace guarantees eventual heaven.\n   231→    Either you are already fully purified (go directly to heaven via axiom 7),\n   232→    or you are not (go to purgatory via axiom 3, then to heaven via axiom 4).\n   233→    Either way, if you die in grace, you will see God.\n   234→    This is the core ASSURANCE claim of purgatory doctrine. -/\n   235→theorem grace_at_death_guarantees_heaven :\n   236→    ∀ (p : Person), diedInGrace p → attainsBeatificVision p :=\n   237→  fun (p : Person) (hg : diedInGrace p) =>\n   238→    Classical.byCases\n   239→      (fun (hp : fullyPurified p) =>\n   240→        purified_in_grace_sees_god p hg hp)\n   241→      (fun (hnp : ¬fullyPurified p) =>\n   242→        purgatory_leads_to_heaven p (post_mortem_purification p hg hnp))\n   243→\n   244→/-!\n   245→## The tension with Hell.lean: death_is_final\n   246→\n   247→Hell.lean declares:\n   248→\n   249→```\n   250→axiom death_is_final :\n   251→  ∀ (d : DeathState),\n   252→    d = DeathState.inMortalSin →\n   253→    ¬(∃ (d' : DeathState), d' = DeathState.repentant)\n   254→```\n   255→\n   256→At first glance, this contradicts purgatory. If death is final and no\n   257→post-mortem change is possible, how can post-mortem purification occur?\n   258→\n   259→The Catholic resolution requires a DISTINCTION that neither §1033 nor\n   260→§1030 makes explicit:\n   261→\n   262→- **Death is final for CHOICE**: You cannot switch from rejecting God\n   263→  to accepting Him (hell → purgatory is impossible), nor from accepting\n   264→  God to rejecting Him (purgatory → hell is impossible).\n   265→\n   266→- **Death is NOT final for PURIFICATION**: You can be cleaned up after\n   267→  choosing God. Purification is not a change of will — it is the\n   268→  completion of a will already oriented toward God.\n   269→\n   270→This distinction is theologically sophisticated but is a HIDDEN\n   271→ASSUMPTION. The Catechism never states it this way. It simply asserts\n   272→both \"death is final\" (§1033) and \"post-mortem purification occurs\"\n   273→(§1030) without acknowledging the apparent tension.\n   274→\n   275→We formalize the resolution below.\n   276→-/\n   277→\n   278→/-- The resolution: death is final for CHOICE, not for all change.\n   279→    A person who died in grace cannot later be in mortal sin.\n   280→    A person who died in mortal sin cannot later be in grace.\n   281→    But a person who died in grace CAN be further purified.\n   282→    Provenance: [Tradition] — theological inference, not stated in CCC.\n   283→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: This distinction is never made explicit in the\n   284→    Catechism. It is the structural requirement for both Hell and\n   285→    Purgatory to coexist without contradiction. -/\n   286→axiom death_finalizes_choice_not_state :\n   287→  ∀ (p : Person), diedInGrace p → ¬diedInMortalSin p\n   288→\n   289→/-- Provenance tag for the resolution axiom. -/\n   290→def resolution_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"theological inference\"\n   291→def resolution_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   292→\n   293→/-- THEOREM 4: The hell-purgatory boundary is absolute.\n   294→    No one in hell can reach purgatory. No one in purgatory can fall to hell.\n   295→    The choice made before death is permanent; only purification continues. -/\n   296→theorem hell_purgatory_boundary :\n   297→    ∀ (p : Person), diedInMortalSin p → ¬inPurgatory p :=\n   298→  fun (p : Person) (h : diedInMortalSin p) =>\n   299→    mortal_sin_excludes_purgatory p h\n   300→\n   301→/-- THEOREM 5: Grace at death and mortal sin at death are mutually exclusive.\n   302→    This is the structural foundation: the choice is binary and final,\n   303→    even though holiness is a spectrum. -/\n   304→theorem grace_and_mortal_sin_exclusive :\n   305→    ∀ (p : Person), diedInGrace p → ¬diedInMortalSin p :=\n   306→  fun (p : Person) (h : diedInGrace p) =>\n   307→    death_finalizes_choice_not_state p h\n   308→\n   309→/-!\n   310→## The canon dependency: purgatory under different Bibles\n   311→\n   312→The strongest scriptural support for purgatory is 2 Maccabees 12:46:\n   313→\"It is a holy and wholesome thought to pray for the dead, that they\n   314→may be loosed from sins.\"\n   315→\n   316→This verse is in a Deuterocanonical book — one of the seven books\n   317→Luther removed from the Old Testament. Under Luther's L4 axiom\n   318→(the canon is determinable without Church authority → 66 books),\n   319→2 Maccabees is not Scripture.\n   320→\n   321→Under the 66-book canon, the scriptural case for purgatory relies on:\n   322→- 1 Cor 3:13-15: \"each one's work will become manifest... the fire\n   323→  will test what sort of work each one has done... he himself will\n   324→  be saved, but only as through fire.\" Catholics read this as\n   325→  purgatorial fire; Protestants read it as a metaphor for judgment.\n   326→- Mt 12:32: \"whoever speaks against the Holy Spirit will not be\n   327→  forgiven, either in this age or in the age to come.\" Catholics\n   328→  argue the phrase \"or in the age to come\" implies SOME sins ARE\n   329→  forgiven in the age to come — which requires purgatory. Protestants\n   330→  read this as emphasis (not even in the next age), not implication.\n   331→\n   332→The exegetical case is significantly weaker without 2 Maccabees.\n   333→The doctrine of purgatory thus has a CRITICAL DEPENDENCY on L4\n   334→(which Bible you use). This is one of the clearest examples of\n   335→how the canon question (L4) cascades into specific doctrines.\n   336→-/\n   337→\n   338→/-- The scriptural evidence under the 73-book (Catholic) canon. -/\n   339→def purgatory_scripture_73 : List String :=\n   340→  [ \"2 Macc 12:46 — 'holy and wholesome thought to pray for the dead'\"\n   341→  , \"1 Cor 3:13-15 — 'saved, but only as through fire'\"\n   342→  , \"Mt 12:32 — 'not forgiven in this age or the age to come'\"\n   343→  , \"Rev 21:27 — 'nothing unclean will enter'\"\n   344→  ]\n   345→\n   346→/-- The scriptural evidence under the 66-book (Protestant) canon.\n   347→    Note: 2 Maccabees is gone. The remaining passages are subject\n   348→    to alternative exegesis. -/\n   349→def purgatory_scripture_66 : List String :=\n   350→  [ \"1 Cor 3:13-15 — 'saved, but only as through fire' (contested reading)\"\n   351→  , \"Mt 12:32 — 'not forgiven in this age or the age to come' (contested reading)\"\n   352→  , \"Rev 21:27 — 'nothing unclean will enter' (shared, but doesn't entail purgatory)\"\n   353→  ]\n   354→\n   355→/-!\n   356→## Denominational summary\n   357→\n   358→| Tradition  | Accepts purgatory? | Notes |\n   359→|------------|-------------------|-------|\n   360→| Catholic   | Yes               | Defined doctrine (CCC §1030-1032, Council of Florence, Council of Trent) |\n   361→| Lutheran   | No                | Rejected as unscriptural (under 66-book canon) |\n   362→| Reformed   | No                | Rejected; Christ's atonement is complete |\n   363→| Orthodox   | Partially          | Similar concept (aerial toll houses, prayers for the dead) but reject the Latin formulation |\n   364→\n   365→## Summary of hidden assumptions\n   366→\n   367→1. **Holiness is a spectrum** — not binary saved/damned. Without degrees\n   368→   of holiness, purgatory is unnecessary.\n   369→2. **Post-mortem change is possible** — in tension with `death_is_final`\n   370→   from Hell.lean. Resolved by distinguishing choice-finality from\n   371→   state-finality, but this distinction is never made explicit.\n   372→3. **Temporal process after death** — purification takes \"time\" in some\n   373→   sense. How does time work for a disembodied soul? Unanswered.\n   374→4. **Prayer crosses the death boundary** — the living can help the dead.\n   375→   This is a strong metaphysical claim, assumed without argument.\n   376→5. **The 73-book canon** — the strongest scriptural support requires\n   377→   2 Maccabees. Under the 66-book canon, the case is significantly weaker.\n   378→\n   379→The most important finding: purgatory and hell BOTH exist in the Catholic\n   380→system, but they require a distinction (choice-finality vs. state-finality)\n   381→that the Catechism never makes explicit. The proof assistant forced this\n   382→distinction to the surface.\n   383→-/\n   384→\n   385→end Catlib.Creed\n   386→"}]},"uuid":"86c15f94-e1d1-4fa2-9398-26b5ab8343e5","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:19.748Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"4ea17d69-9e14-4d0a-b1ba-e51ac336a18b","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"2019f799-6429-4fec-a55a-2060d87f54b5","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019sxf9sWDqAzypgrp1JBurm","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→\n     3→/-!\n     4→# God's Two Modes: Sustaining Being vs. Beatifying Communion\n     5→\n     6→## The paradox\n     7→\n     8→The Catechism holds both:\n     9→1. God sustains ALL existence at every moment (§301)\n    10→2. Hell is separation from God (§1033)\n    11→\n    12→If God sustains everything, how can anything be separated from God?\n    13→This looks like a contradiction. The proof assistant forces us to\n    14→resolve it.\n    15→\n    16→## The resolution (Aquinas, ST I q.8 + q.104)\n    17→\n    18→God relates to creation in (at least) two distinct modes:\n    19→\n    20→- **Sustaining mode**: God as the ground of all being. Without this,\n    21→  nothing exists at all. This is not optional — everything that IS,\n    22→  is sustained by God. You cannot be separated from this.\n    23→\n    24→- **Beatifying mode**: God as the source of communion, love, joy,\n    25→  the beatific vision. This is what the blessed in heaven experience.\n    26→  You CAN be separated from this — and that separation IS hell.\n    27→\n    28→The damned are sustained by God (they must be — they exist) but\n    29→separated from God's friendship. Hell is not separation from God's\n    30→POWER but from God's LOVE-AS-COMMUNION.\n    31→\n    32→## Why this matters\n    33→\n    34→This distinction connects three major doctrines:\n    35→- **Hell**: Separation from beatifying mode, not sustaining mode\n    36→- **Purgatory**: In sustaining mode AND beatifying mode (assured),\n    37→  but not yet fully purified to receive the beatific vision\n    38→- **Providence**: God's sustaining mode operates even through evil\n    39→  (connecting to the good/evil causation asymmetry)\n    40→\n    41→## Scripture basis\n    42→\n    43→- §301/sustaining: Col 1:17 (\"in him all things hold together\"),\n    44→  Heb 1:3 (\"sustaining all things by his powerful word\"),\n    45→  Acts 17:28 (\"in him we live and move and have our being\")\n    46→- §1033/separation: The rich man and Lazarus (Lk 16:19-31) — the\n    47→  rich man exists, is conscious, can speak, but is separated from\n    48→  Abraham's bosom by \"a great chasm\"\n    49→- Beatific vision: 1 Cor 13:12 (\"now we see in a mirror dimly, but\n    50→  then face to face\"), 1 Jn 3:2 (\"we shall see him as he is\")\n    51→\n    52→## Denominational scope\n    53→\n    54→- The sustaining/beatifying distinction: broadly Thomistic, Catholic\n    55→  distinctive in its formal articulation, but the underlying intuition\n    56→  (God sustains everything, hell is real separation) is ecumenical\n    57→- Annihilationism (the damned cease to exist): held by some\n    58→  Protestants (e.g., conditionalists), rejected by Catholic teaching\n    59→\n    60→## Prediction\n    61→\n    62→I expect this to **reveal deep hidden structure**. The two-mode\n    63→distinction will turn out to be a more fundamental version of P2\n    64→(two-tier causation) — applied not to God-and-creatures but to\n    65→God's own relationship with creation. This is the deepest modeling\n    66→choice in the entire project.\n    67→\n    68→## Findings\n    69→\n    70→- **Prediction vs. reality**: Confirmed — the two-mode distinction is\n    71→  genuinely foundational. It resolves the hell paradox, explains why\n    72→  purgatory is possible (you can be in sustaining mode and beatifying\n    73→  mode simultaneously, at different levels), and grounds the\n    74→  Providence causation asymmetry (God sustains beings that do evil,\n    75→  but doesn't beatify the evil act).\n    76→- **Surprise level**: Very high — the connection to purgatory was not\n    77→  predicted. The spectrum of communion with God (none in hell, partial\n    78→  in purgatory, full in heaven) emerges naturally from the two-mode model.\n    79→- **Assessment**: Tier 3 — the most structurally significant finding\n    80→  since the axiom-set-as-denomination result.\n    81→-/\n    82→\n    83→namespace Catlib.Creed\n    84→\n    85→open Catlib\n    86→\n    87→/-!\n    88→## The two modes of divine relation\n    89→-/\n    90→\n    91→/-- How God relates to a creature.\n    92→    This is the fundamental distinction that resolves the hell paradox. -/\n    93→inductive DivineMode where\n    94→  /-- Sustaining mode: God holds the creature in existence.\n    95→      Without this, the creature ceases to be entirely.\n    96→      This is NOT optional — everything that exists has this. -/\n    97→  | sustaining\n    98→  /-- Beatifying mode: God offers communion, love, friendship,\n    99→      and ultimately the beatific vision (seeing God \"face to face\").\n   100→      This CAN be refused. Refusing it IS hell. -/\n   101→  | beatifying\n   102→\n   103→/-- The state of a soul's relationship with God after death.\n   104→    Defined by which divine modes are active. -/\n   105→structure SoulState where\n   106→  /-- Is God sustaining this soul in existence? -/\n   107→  sustained : Prop\n   108→  /-- Is this soul in communion with God (beatifying mode)? -/\n   109→  inCommunion : Prop\n   110→  /-- Degree of purification (0 = unpurified, full = ready for vision) -/\n   111→  purified : Prop\n   112→\n   113→/-- AXIOM (§301, Col 1:17): God sustains ALL that exists.\n   114→    Provenance: [Scripture] Col 1:17 (\"in him all things hold together\"),\n   115→    Heb 1:3 (\"sustaining all things by his powerful word\"),\n   116→    Acts 17:28 (\"in him we live and move and have our being\").\n   117→    Denominational scope: Ecumenical — all Christians accept divine\n   118→    conservation of being. Even annihilationists agree God sustains\n   119→    things while they exist; they just think God can withdraw this. -/\n   120→axiom god_sustains_all :\n   121→  ∀ (s : SoulState), s.sustained\n   122→\n   123→/-- AXIOM (§1023-1024): The beatific vision requires full purification.\n   124→    Provenance: [Scripture] Rev 21:27 (\"nothing impure will ever enter\"),\n   125→    1 Jn 3:2 (\"we shall see him as he is\").\n   126→    Only the fully purified can see God \"face to face.\" -/\n   127→axiom beatific_vision_requires_purity :\n   128→  ∀ (s : SoulState), s.inCommunion → s.purified\n   129→\n   130→/-- AXIOM (§1033): Hell is the absence of beatifying mode.\n   131→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1033.\n   132→    The damned are sustained (they exist) but not in communion.\n   133→    THIS is what resolves the paradox: separation from God means\n   134→    separation from BEATIFYING mode, not from SUSTAINING mode. -/\n   135→axiom hell_is_absence_of_communion :\n   136→  ∀ (s : SoulState),\n   137→    ¬s.inCommunion → s.sustained → -- Still exists, but no communion\n   138→    True  -- This state IS hell\n   139→\n   140→/-- AXIOM: Existence without communion is possible but terrible.\n   141→    Provenance: [Scripture] Lk 16:23-24 (rich man in Hades:\n   142→    \"I am in agony in this flame\" — exists, conscious, suffering).\n   143→    [Tradition] Aquinas ST I-II q.87 a.4.\n   144→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Existence without any good is worse than\n   145→    non-existence. The damned would prefer annihilation, but God\n   146→    sustains them. Why? (See below.) -/\n   147→axiom existence_without_communion_is_suffering :\n   148→  ∀ (s : SoulState),\n   149→    s.sustained → ¬s.inCommunion →\n   150→    -- This state involves suffering (the suffering of privation)\n   151→    True\n   152→\n   153→/-!\n   154→## The three afterlife states as combinations of modes\n   155→\n   156→Heaven, purgatory, and hell are NOT three arbitrary categories.\n   157→They are the three possible combinations of the two modes:\n   158→-/\n   159→\n   160→/-- Heaven: sustained AND in full communion (beatified). -/\n   161→def heavenState : SoulState :=\n   162→  { sustained := True, inCommunion := True, purified := True }\n   163→\n   164→/-- Purgatory: sustained AND in communion (assured), but not yet\n   165→    fully purified. The soul is on its way to heaven.\n   166→    NOTE: \"in communion\" here means the person chose God — they\n   167→    died in grace. They are not yet FULLY in communion (beatific\n   168→    vision) because they need purification first. -/\n   169→def purgatoryState : SoulState :=\n   170→  { sustained := True, inCommunion := True, purified := False }\n   171→\n   172→/-- Hell: sustained but NOT in communion. Exists without any good.\n   173→    The soul is permanently separated from God's friendship. -/\n   174→def hellState : SoulState :=\n   175→  { sustained := True, inCommunion := False, purified := False }\n   176→\n   177→/-- Key theorem: all three states are sustained — nothing stops existing.\n   178→    God sustains the damned, the purifying, and the blessed alike. -/\n   179→theorem all_states_sustained :\n   180→    heavenState.sustained ∧ purgatoryState.sustained ∧ hellState.sustained := by\n   181→  exact ⟨trivial, trivial, trivial⟩\n   182→\n   183→/-- The hell paradox resolved: the damned are separated from God's\n   184→    communion but NOT from God's sustaining power. Both can be true\n   185→    simultaneously because they are different modes. -/\n   186→theorem hell_paradox_resolved :\n   187→    -- The damned exist (sustained)\n   188→    hellState.sustained ∧\n   189→    -- The damned are separated from communion\n   190→    ¬hellState.inCommunion := by\n   191→  constructor\n   192→  · exact trivial\n   193→  · intro h; exact absurd h (by simp [hellState])\n   194→\n   195→/-- Heaven requires full purification — you can't be in communion\n   196→    without being purified. -/\n   197→theorem heaven_requires_purity :\n   198→    heavenState.inCommunion → heavenState.purified :=\n   199→  fun _ => trivial\n   200→\n   201→/-- Purgatory is the state of being in communion (chose God) but\n   202→    not yet purified. This is why it's temporary — once purified,\n   203→    the soul transitions to full beatific vision. -/\n   204→theorem purgatory_is_transitional :\n   205→    purgatoryState.inCommunion ∧ ¬purgatoryState.purified := by\n   206→  constructor\n   207→  · exact trivial\n   208→  · intro h; exact absurd h (by simp [purgatoryState])\n   209→\n   210→/-!\n   211→## Why does God sustain the damned?\n   212→\n   213→Three possible axioms from the tradition. The Catechism doesn't\n   214→choose among them — it holds all three without resolving the tension.\n   215→-/\n   216→\n   217→/-- Option 1: Existence is intrinsically good.\n   218→    Even diminished existence (hell) is better than non-existence.\n   219→    Source: Aquinas ST I q.5 a.2 (\"being is itself a good\").\n   220→    Implication: God sustaining the damned IS an act of goodness. -/\n   221→axiom existence_is_intrinsically_good :\n   222→  ∀ (s : SoulState), s.sustained → True\n   223→  -- (The claim is: sustained existence is always a good, even in hell.\n   224→  --  This is debatable — some argue annihilation would be more merciful.)\n   225→\n   226→/-- Option 2: Respect for freedom.\n   227→    Annihilating the damned would override their choice.\n   228→    If they chose to exist apart from God, God honors that choice\n   229→    by sustaining their existence.\n   230→    Source: Connects to S1 (love requires freedom) and T1 (libertarian\n   231→    free will). Love does not coerce — not even by annihilation. -/\n   232→axiom respect_for_freedom_sustains :\n   233→  ∀ (s : SoulState),\n   234→    s.sustained → ¬s.inCommunion →\n   235→    -- God sustains because annihilation would violate their choice\n   236→    True\n   237→\n   238→/-- Option 3: Justice requires experienced consequences.\n   239→    The damned must experience the consequences of their choice.\n   240→    Annihilation would remove the consequence.\n   241→    Source: Aquinas ST Supp. q.99. -/\n   242→axiom justice_requires_consequences :\n   243→  ∀ (s : SoulState),\n   244→    s.sustained → ¬s.inCommunion →\n   245→    -- Justice is served by the soul experiencing separation\n   246→    True\n   247→\n   248→/-!\n   249→## The spectrum of communion\n   250→\n   251→The two-mode model reveals that the afterlife is not three\n   252→disconnected states — it's a SPECTRUM of communion with God:\n   253→\n   254→```\n   255→No communion          Partial/assured          Full communion\n   256→    |                      |                       |\n   257→   HELL              PURGATORY                  HEAVEN\n   258→    |                      |                       |\n   259→Sustained only     Sustained + in communion   Sustained + in communion\n   260→No purification    Being purified              Fully purified\n   261→Permanent          Temporary                   Permanent\n   262→```\n   263→\n   264→This is structurally beautiful: one axis (sustained/not) is always\n   265→\"sustained\" because God sustains everything. The other axis\n   266→(communion) ranges from none (hell) through assured-but-incomplete\n   267→(purgatory) to full (heaven). Purification is the process of\n   268→moving along the communion axis.\n   269→\n   270→## Connection to other findings\n   271→\n   272→1. **P2 (two-tier causation)**: The sustaining/beatifying distinction\n   273→   IS two-tier causation applied to God Himself — God operates in\n   274→   sustaining mode at one level and beatifying mode at another.\n   275→\n   276→2. **Providence (good/evil asymmetry)**: God sustains beings that\n   277→   do evil (sustaining mode) without causing the evil (not beatifying\n   278→   the evil act). The asymmetry maps to the two modes.\n   279→\n   280→3. **Purgatory**: The post-mortem change that purgatory requires is\n   281→   movement along the communion/purification axis, not a change in\n   282→   the choice axis. Death finalizes the choice; purgatory addresses\n   283→   the purification.\n   284→\n   285→4. **Freedom (P3 evil is privation)**: Hell is the ultimate privation —\n   286→   existence with all good removed. Since God is the source of all\n   287→   good, separation from God's beatifying mode IS the removal of all\n   288→   good. Hell is not a place where bad things happen; it's existence\n   289→   stripped of all good.\n   290→\n   291→## Summary of hidden assumptions\n   292→\n   293→1. **God relates to creation in at least two distinct modes**\n   294→   (sustaining and beatifying). This is never stated as a principle\n   295→   in the Catechism.\n   296→\n   297→2. **Separation from God means separation from beatifying mode only.**\n   298→   You cannot be separated from sustaining mode and still exist.\n   299→\n   300→3. **Existence without communion is worse than non-existence** —\n   301→   but God sustains the damned anyway (for reasons the tradition\n   302→   debates but doesn't resolve).\n   303→\n   304→4. **The afterlife is a spectrum of communion**, not three\n   305→   disconnected bins. Purgatory is a point on the spectrum, not\n   306→   a third category.\n   307→\n   308→5. **The two-mode distinction is the deepest structural principle**\n   309→   in the entire project — it unifies hell, purgatory, heaven,\n   310→   providence, and the privation theory of evil into one framework.\n   311→-/\n   312→\n   313→end Catlib.Creed\n   314→"}]},"uuid":"429ea3f2-bbbe-4660-86cd-c24c0e8645f6","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:20.032Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"2019f799-6429-4fec-a55a-2060d87f54b5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"793c03a8-8485-40df-a3d6-bf64c4b5bc5a","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01GeSjyYTF1JE4zgr2F6gQkL","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→import Catlib.MoralTheology.ConjugalEthics\n     3→import Catlib.MoralTheology.Freedom\n     4→import Catlib.Creed.Soul\n     5→\n     6→/-!\n     7→# Theology of the Body: Three Core Claims\n     8→\n     9→John Paul II's Theology of the Body (TOB, 1979–1984) is a 129-lecture\n    10→cycle that builds a theological anthropology from the ground up. It\n    11→extends and deepens the claims already formalized in ConjugalEthics.lean,\n    12→Freedom.lean, and Soul.lean.\n    13→\n    14→We formalize the three most foundational claims:\n    15→\n    16→1. **The Personalist Norm** — the only adequate response to a person is\n    17→   love; instrumental use of a person always violates dignity, even with\n    18→   consent.\n    19→2. **Concupiscence diminishes but does not destroy** — the Fall reduced\n    20→   but did not eliminate the capacity for authentic self-gift.\n    21→3. **The body as sign** — the body, and it alone, is capable of making\n    22→   visible what is invisible.\n    23→\n    24→## Structural note: PERSONALIST_NORM is a THEOREM, not an axiom\n    25→\n    26→In an earlier version, the personalist norm was axiomatized directly.\n    27→It is now DERIVED as a theorem from two axioms (IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION)\n    28→combined with S1 (God is love) from Axioms.lean. The derivation chain:\n    29→\n    30→1. God is love (S1 — `s1_god_is_love`, giving `godIsLove`)\n    31→2. Humans are in God's image (IMAGO_DEI)\n    32→3. An image participates in what it images (PARTICIPATION)\n    33→4. Therefore humans participate in love\n    34→5. Therefore the adequate response to a being that participates in love is love\n    35→6. Therefore PERSONALIST_NORM (now a theorem)\n    36→\n    37→Similarly, DIGNITY_IS_INTRINSIC and CONSENT_DOES_NOT_LEGITIMIZE_USE are\n    38→now derived theorems rather than axioms. Dignity follows from Imago Dei\n    39→(God's image is ontological, not functional, so dignity cannot depend on\n    40→external conditions). Consent-does-not-legitimize-use follows from the\n    41→personalist norm plus the fact that Use ≠ Love by definition.\n    42→\n    43→This is a structural improvement: the personalist norm now has explicit\n    44→theological grounding (not just Kant's categorical imperative), and\n    45→formal verification revealed the dependency chain.\n    46→\n    47→## Prediction\n    48→\n    49→I expect Claim 1 to **reveal hidden structure**: the inseparability\n    50→principle (ConjugalEthics.lean) should follow from the personalist norm,\n    51→which would mean TOB provides the missing derivation that Humanae Vitae\n    52→assumed without argument.\n    53→\n    54→I expect Claim 2 to **locate the Catholic position precisely** between\n    55→Pelagian optimism and Calvinist pessimism about fallen human nature —\n    56→the three-state anthropology should make the calibration explicit.\n    57→\n    58→I expect Claim 3 to **generate a surprising consequence**: if only\n    59→material signs can convey spiritual reality, then sacraments are\n    60→NECESSARY (not merely helpful), which would derive T3 (sacramental\n    61→efficacy) from a philosophical anthropology rather than asserting it\n    62→as a standalone tradition.\n    63→\n    64→## Findings\n    65→\n    66→- **Claim 1 confirmed — and improved**: The personalist norm does ground\n    67→  the inseparability principle. If the only adequate response to a person\n    68→  is love (= affirming their full good), and contraception withholds\n    69→  fertility (= taking pleasure while blocking full self-gift), then\n    70→  contraception = instrumental use of the other's body = violation of\n    71→  the personalist norm. The inseparability principle is a special case\n    72→  of the personalist norm applied to conjugal acts.\n    73→\n    74→  **Structural improvement**: The personalist norm is now DERIVED from\n    75→  S1 (God is love) + IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION, rather than axiomatized.\n    76→  This gives it explicit theological grounding: persons must be loved\n    77→  because they are images of the God who IS love, and as images they\n    78→  participate in what they image. The formal derivation reveals a\n    79→  dependency chain that Wojtyła assumed but never made fully explicit.\n    80→\n    81→- **Claim 1 surprise — consent does not legitimize use**: This is now\n    82→  a DERIVED theorem (was an axiom). Modern ethics typically treats\n    83→  consent as the SOLE criterion for legitimate sexual activity. TOB\n    84→  says: even if both parties consent to being used instrumentally, it\n    85→  remains a violation of dignity, because dignity is intrinsic and\n    86→  cannot be waived. The derivation connects to the object independence\n    87→  principle from SourcesOfMorality.lean: consent changes the agent's\n    88→  agreement but not the act's moral object (Use remains Use regardless\n    89→  of whether the other party agrees to it).\n    90→\n    91→- **Claim 2 confirmed**: The three-state anthropology (Original\n    92→  Integrity → Fallen → Redeemed) does locate the Catholic position\n    93→  precisely. Pelagianism says the Fall did no damage (capacity remains\n    94→  at maximum). Calvinism says the Fall destroyed the capacity entirely\n    95→  (total depravity). The Catholic position says the capacity is reduced\n    96→  but non-zero — damaged but not destroyed.\n    97→\n    98→- **Claim 3 confirmed**: Material mediation does entail sacramental\n    99→  necessity. If spiritual realities are accessible ONLY through material\n   100→  signs (the \"it alone\" exclusivity), then any channel of grace must\n   101→  involve a material sign — which is exactly what a sacrament is.\n   102→  T3 (sacramental efficacy) follows from the body-as-sign principle\n   103→  plus material mediation.\n   104→\n   105→- **Claim 3 generates the body-lie theorem**: If the body is a sign\n   106→  with inherent meaning, then a bodily act that contradicts its meaning\n   107→  is a \"lie told with the body.\" Contraception is such a lie: the\n   108→  conjugal act signifies total self-gift, but contraception withholds\n   109→  fertility. This provides a SECOND derivation of the contraception\n   110→  prohibition (the first being the inseparability principle).\n   111→\n   112→- **Assessment**: Tier 3 — all three claims reveal genuine hidden\n   113→  structure. The personalist norm grounding inseparability is the most\n   114→  significant finding: it provides the derivation that Humanae Vitae\n   115→  never gave. The refactoring from axiom to theorem makes the\n   116→  dependency chain explicit and reduces the axiom count by one (three\n   117→  axioms replaced by two).\n   118→-/\n   119→\n   120→set_option autoImplicit false\n   121→\n   122→namespace Catlib.MoralTheology.TheologyOfBody\n   123→\n   124→open Catlib\n   125→open Catlib.MoralTheology\n   126→open Catlib.MoralTheology.ConjugalEthics\n   127→open Catlib.Creed\n   128→\n   129→-- ============================================================================\n   130→-- ## Claim 1: The Personalist Norm\n   131→-- \"The opposite of love is not hate, but use.\" — Karol Wojtyła, Love and\n   132→-- Responsibility (1960)\n   133→-- ============================================================================\n   134→\n   135→/-!\n   136→## Claim 1: The Personalist Norm\n   137→\n   138→The personalist norm is the ethical foundation of the entire Theology of\n   139→the Body. It says: a person must never be merely a means to an end —\n   140→the only adequate response to a person is love (affirming the person's\n   141→full good). This is NOT just a restatement of Kant's categorical\n   142→imperative. Kant says: don't treat persons MERELY as means. Wojtyła\n   143→says: even treating a person as a means WITH CONSENT violates dignity,\n   144→because dignity is intrinsic and cannot be waived.\n   145→\n   146→In this formalization, the personalist norm is DERIVED (not axiomatized)\n   147→from IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION + S1 (God is love).\n   148→-/\n   149→\n   150→/-- The three possible orientations toward a person.\n   151→    Love: affirming the person's full good (willing their good for\n   152→    their own sake).\n   153→    Use: treating the person as a means to one's own end.\n   154→    Indifference: failing to engage with the person at all.\n   155→\n   156→    MODELING CHOICE: These are mutually exclusive orientations within\n   157→    a single relational act. A complex relationship may involve\n   158→    different orientations at different moments, but at any given\n   159→    moment the orientation is one of these three. -/\n   160→inductive RelationKind where\n   161→  /-- Affirming the person's full good for their own sake -/\n   162→  | Love\n   163→  /-- Treating the person as a means to one's own end -/\n   164→  | Use\n   165→  /-- Failing to engage with the person at all -/\n   166→  | Indifference\n   167→\n   168→/-- Whether a relational act respects the dignity of the person. -/\n   169→def RelationKind.respectsDignity : RelationKind → Prop\n   170→  | .Love => True\n   171→  | .Use => False\n   172→  | .Indifference => False\n   173→\n   174→/-- Whether a relational orientation involves instrumentalizing the person. -/\n   175→def RelationKind.isInstrumental : RelationKind → Prop\n   176→  | .Love => False\n   177→  | .Use => True\n   178→  | .Indifference => False\n   179→\n   180→-- ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n   181→-- New foundational types for the derivation\n   182→-- ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n   183→\n   184→/-- Whether a person is an image of God. This is an ontological property:\n   185→    being made in God's image is part of WHAT a person IS, not something\n   186→    they do or achieve. -/\n   187→opaque isImageOfGod : Person → Prop\n   188→\n   189→/-- Whether a being participates in love — i.e., love is part of their\n   190→    ontological constitution because they are an image of the God who\n   191→    IS love. This is the bridge between Imago Dei and the personalist norm. -/\n   192→opaque participatesInLove : Person → Prop\n   193→\n   194→/-- Whether love is the adequate response to a being. A being that\n   195→    participates in love calls for love as its proper response — anything\n   196→    less (use, indifference) fails to respond to what the being IS. -/\n   197→opaque loveIsAdequateResponse : Person → Prop\n   198→\n   199→-- ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n   200→-- The two new axioms (replacing three old ones)"}]},"uuid":"ac2eeaf8-d0d2-4e60-8c58-0ecc0305757d","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:25.915Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"793c03a8-8485-40df-a3d6-bf64c4b5bc5a","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"73350a94-b295-4932-808f-da3df8154db1","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01TJS64rmMmVE12Dc2xkuYEF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→\n     3→/-!\n     4→# CCC §1673: Exorcism — The Authority Chain\n     5→\n     6→## The Catechism claims\n     7→\n     8→\"Jesus performed exorcisms and from him the Church has received the\n     9→power and office of exorcizing.\" (§1673)\n    10→\n    11→\"The solemn exorcism, called 'a major exorcism,' can be performed only\n    12→by a priest and with the permission of the bishop.\" (§1673)\n    13→\n    14→## The authority delegation chain\n    15→\n    16→The Catechism claims a specific chain of authority for exorcism:\n    17→1. Jesus has authority over demons (Scripture: Mk 1:27, Lk 11:20)\n    18→2. Jesus delegated this to the Apostles (Scripture: Mk 6:7, Lk 10:17)\n    19→3. The Apostles delegated to their successors (Tradition: apostolic succession)\n    20→4. Bishops hold this authority today\n    21→5. Bishops can delegate to priests (with permission)\n    22→\n    23→## What we formalize\n    24→\n    25→The delegation chain and its hidden assumptions:\n    26→- Authority can be DELEGATED without being DIMINISHED\n    27→- The chain is UNBROKEN from Jesus to the present\n    28→- Delegation requires AUTHORIZATION from above\n    29→- The delegated power is the SAME power, not a lesser version\n    30→\n    31→## Prediction\n    32→\n    33→I expect this to **reveal hidden structure**. The delegation model\n    34→requires assumptions about authority transfer that the text doesn't\n    35→state: Can delegated authority be revoked? Can it expire? Is it\n    36→automatic with ordination or does each exorcism need fresh permission?\n    37→\n    38→## Findings\n    39→\n    40→- **Prediction vs. reality**: Confirmed. The authority chain requires:\n    41→  (1) authority is transferable without loss, (2) the chain is unbroken\n    42→  (apostolic succession), (3) a two-tier permission system (ordination\n    43→  gives potential, bishop gives activation), (4) the power operates on\n    44→  a specific ontology where demons are personal agents that can be\n    45→  commanded.\n    46→- **Surprise level**: Moderate — the two-tier permission model\n    47→  (ordination + bishop's permission) was not predicted. It's an\n    48→  interesting access control system.\n    49→- **Assessment**: Tier 2/3 — the authority chain is well-structured\n    50→  but the demon ontology is the genuinely interesting hidden assumption.\n    51→-/\n    52→\n    53→namespace Catlib.Sacraments\n    54→\n    55→open Catlib\n    56→\n    57→/-!\n    58→## Authority delegation model\n    59→-/\n    60→\n    61→/-- A role in the Church hierarchy. -/\n    62→inductive ChurchRole where\n    63→  | christ        -- Jesus Christ\n    64→  | apostle       -- The original twelve + Paul\n    65→  | bishop        -- Successor of the apostles\n    66→  | priest        -- Ordained by a bishop\n    67→  | layperson     -- Baptized but not ordained\n    68→\n    69→/-- An authority — a specific power to act in a domain. -/\n    70→structure SpiritualAuthority where\n    71→  /-- What domain does this authority cover? -/\n    72→  domain : String\n    73→  /-- Who currently holds it? -/\n    74→  holder : ChurchRole\n    75→  /-- Where did it come from? -/\n    76→  source : ChurchRole\n    77→\n    78→/-- The exorcism authority. -/\n    79→def exorcismAuthority (holder : ChurchRole) (source : ChurchRole) :\n    80→    SpiritualAuthority :=\n    81→  { domain := \"exorcism\", holder := holder, source := source }\n    82→\n    83→/-- AXIOM 1 (Scripture): Jesus has authority over demons.\n    84→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mk 1:27 (\"He commands even the unclean\n    85→    spirits, and they obey him\"), Lk 11:20 (\"by the finger of God\n    86→    I cast out demons\"). -/\n    87→axiom christ_has_exorcism_authority :\n    88→  ∃ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n    89→    a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧ a.holder = ChurchRole.christ\n    90→\n    91→/-- AXIOM 2 (Scripture): Jesus delegated authority to the Apostles.\n    92→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mk 6:7 (\"He gave them authority over\n    93→    unclean spirits\"), Lk 10:17 (\"Lord, even the demons are subject\n    94→    to us in your name\"). -/\n    95→axiom christ_delegated_to_apostles :\n    96→  ∃ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n    97→    a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧\n    98→    a.holder = ChurchRole.apostle ∧\n    99→    a.source = ChurchRole.christ\n   100→\n   101→/-- AXIOM 3 (Tradition): Apostolic succession — the Apostles'\n   102→    authority passed to their successors (bishops).\n   103→    Provenance: [Tradition] CCC §77, §861-862. This is the core\n   104→    claim of apostolic succession. Without it, the chain breaks.\n   105→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Authority transfer is valid across generations\n   106→    without loss or expiration. -/\n   107→axiom apostolic_succession :\n   108→  ∃ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n   109→    a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧\n   110→    a.holder = ChurchRole.bishop ∧\n   111→    a.source = ChurchRole.apostle\n   112→\n   113→/-- AXIOM 4 (§1673): Bishops can delegate exorcism to priests.\n   114→    \"Can be performed only by a priest and with the permission\n   115→    of the bishop.\"\n   116→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Two-tier permission model. Ordination gives\n   117→    the POTENTIAL to exorcize; the bishop's permission ACTIVATES it\n   118→    for a specific case. This is an access control system. -/\n   119→axiom bishop_delegates_to_priest :\n   120→  ∃ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n   121→    a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧\n   122→    a.holder = ChurchRole.priest ∧\n   123→    a.source = ChurchRole.bishop\n   124→\n   125→/-- The complete authority chain: Christ → Apostles → Bishops → Priests.\n   126→    This is derivable from the four axioms above. -/\n   127→theorem exorcism_authority_chain :\n   128→    -- Christ has it\n   129→    (∃ a : SpiritualAuthority, a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧ a.holder = ChurchRole.christ) ∧\n   130→    -- Delegated to apostles\n   131→    (∃ a : SpiritualAuthority, a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧ a.holder = ChurchRole.apostle) ∧\n   132→    -- Passed to bishops\n   133→    (∃ a : SpiritualAuthority, a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧ a.holder = ChurchRole.bishop) ∧\n   134→    -- Delegated to priests\n   135→    (∃ a : SpiritualAuthority, a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧ a.holder = ChurchRole.priest) := by\n   136→  refine ⟨christ_has_exorcism_authority, ?_, ?_, ?_⟩\n   137→  · obtain ⟨a, hd, hh, _⟩ := christ_delegated_to_apostles; exact ⟨a, hd, hh⟩\n   138→  · obtain ⟨a, hd, hh, _⟩ := apostolic_succession; exact ⟨a, hd, hh⟩\n   139→  · obtain ⟨a, hd, hh, _⟩ := bishop_delegates_to_priest; exact ⟨a, hd, hh⟩\n   140→\n   141→/-- AXIOM: Spiritual authority must come from above — you cannot\n   142→    be your own source of spiritual authority.\n   143→    Provenance: [Scripture] Jn 15:5 (\"without me you can do nothing\"),\n   144→    Heb 5:4 (\"no one takes this honor on himself\").\n   145→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: Authority is not democratically distributed.\n   146→    The chain is hierarchical by design. -/\n   147→axiom authority_requires_higher_source :\n   148→  ∀ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n   149→    a.domain = \"exorcism\" → a.holder = a.source → False\n   150→\n   151→theorem laypersons_cannot_exorcize :\n   152→    ¬(∃ (a : SpiritualAuthority),\n   153→      a.domain = \"exorcism\" ∧\n   154→      a.holder = ChurchRole.layperson ∧\n   155→      a.source = ChurchRole.layperson) := by\n   156→  intro ⟨a, hd, hh, hs⟩\n   157→  have : a.holder = a.source := by rw [hh, hs]\n   158→  exact authority_requires_higher_source a hd this\n   159→\n   160→/-!\n   161→## The demon ontology\n   162→\n   163→The exorcism teaching assumes a specific ontology:\n   164→- Demons are PERSONAL agents (they can be \"commanded\")\n   165→- They can POSSESS persons (occupy/control)\n   166→- They respond to AUTHORITY (they obey commands)\n   167→- They are FINITE (they can be expelled)\n   168→\n   169→This is a rich ontological commitment the Catechism makes without\n   170→argument. The existence of demons is declared \"a truth of faith\"\n   171→(§328 for angels; §391 for fallen angels/demons).\n   172→-/\n   173→\n   174→/-- A demon — a fallen angel, personal spiritual being. -/\n   175→structure Demon where\n   176→  /-- Demons are personal — they have intellect and will -/\n   177→  isPersonal : Prop\n   178→  /-- Demons are finite — limited in power -/\n   179→  isFinite : Prop\n   180→  /-- Demons can be commanded by proper authority -/\n   181→  respondsToAuthority : Prop\n   182→\n   183→/-- AXIOM 5 (§391-395): Demons exist as personal spiritual beings.\n   184→    Provenance: [Scripture] Mt 4:1-11 (temptation), Mk 5:1-20\n   185→    (Gerasene demoniac); [Tradition] Fourth Lateran Council (1215).\n   186→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: This is a literal ontological claim, not a\n   187→    metaphor for evil or mental illness. The Catechism explicitly\n   188→    distinguishes demonic possession from psychological illness (§1673). -/\n   189→axiom demons_exist :\n   190→  ∃ (d : Demon), d.isPersonal ∧ d.isFinite ∧ d.respondsToAuthority\n   191→\n   192→/-- AXIOM 6 (§1673): Possession is distinguishable from illness.\n   193→    \"Illness, especially psychological illness, is a very different\n   194→    matter; treating this is the concern of medical science.\"\n   195→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: There exists a reliable way to distinguish\n   196→    demonic possession from mental illness. The Catechism asserts\n   197→    the distinction but gives NO diagnostic criteria. This is\n   198→    perhaps the biggest epistemic gap in the exorcism teaching. -/\n   199→axiom possession_distinguishable_from_illness :\n   200→  -- There exists a way to tell the difference\n   201→  -- (the Catechism never says what that way is)\n   202→  True\n   203→\n   204→/-!\n   205→## Summary of hidden assumptions\n   206→\n   207→1. **Authority transfers without loss** — delegated power = original power\n   208→2. **The chain is unbroken** — apostolic succession (the biggest assumption)\n   209→3. **Two-tier permission** — ordination gives potential, bishop activates\n   210→4. **Hierarchical, not democratic** — laypersons excluded\n   211→5. **Demons are personal agents** — literal, not metaphorical\n   212→6. **Possession ≠ illness** — distinguishable but criteria unstated\n   213→-/\n   214→\n   215→end Catlib.Sacraments\n   216→"}]},"uuid":"d10ee25b-2e58-4db8-b3a0-404ea858b543","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:27.104Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"73350a94-b295-4932-808f-da3df8154db1","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}
