Every person with intellect bears the\n   205→    image of God as an ontological property — it is constitutive, not\n   206→    acquired.\n   207→\n   208→    Source: [Scripture] Gen 1:27 (\"God created man in his own image\").\n   209→    CCC §1700: \"The dignity of the human person is rooted in his creation\n   210→    in the image and likeness of God.\"\n   211→\n   212→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — all Christians accept this.\n   213→\n   214→    CONNECTS TO: S1 (God is love), Soul.lean axiom 4\n   215→    (only_humans_know_god — the rational soul grounds the image). -/\n   216→axiom IMAGO_DEI :\n   217→  ∀ (p : Person), p.hasIntellect = true → isImageOfGod p\n   218→\n   219→/-- Denominational tag: ecumenical. All Christians affirm Gen 1:27. -/\n   220→def imago_dei_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   221→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical],\n   222→    note := \"Universal Christian teaching; Gen 1:27; CCC §1700\" }\n   223→\n   224→/-- **AXIOM (Aquinas, ST I q.44-45): PARTICIPATION.**\n   225→    An image participates in what it images. If God is love (S1), and\n   226→    a person is God's image (IMAGO_DEI), then that person participates\n   227→    in love. Furthermore, participation in love makes love the adequate\n   228→    response to that being.\n   229→\n   230→    This axiom encodes two steps of the derivation chain:\n   231→    (a) image of God + God is love → participates in love\n   232→    (b) participates in love → love is the adequate response\n   233→\n   234→    Source: Aquinas, ST I q.44-45 (participation metaphysics).\n   235→    Denominational scope: Philosophical (Catholic/Thomistic).\n   236→\n   237→    CONNECTS TO: S1 (God is love), IMAGO_DEI,\n   238→    the personalist norm (derived below). -/\n   239→axiom PARTICIPATION :\n   240→  ∀ (p : Person),\n   241→    isImageOfGod p →\n   242→    godIsLove →\n   243→    participatesInLove p ∧ loveIsAdequateResponse p\n   244→\n   245→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic/Thomistic for the participation\n   246→    metaphysics. The conclusion (persons deserve love) is ecumenical;\n   247→    the Thomistic ROUTE to it is Catholic. -/\n   248→def participation_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   249→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   250→    note := \"Thomistic participation metaphysics; conclusion is ecumenical, route is Catholic\" }\n   251→\n   252→-- ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n   253→-- Derived theorems (formerly axioms)\n   254→-- ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~\n   255→\n   256→/-- **Lemma: Humans participate in love.**\n   257→    Derivation chain:\n   258→    1. God is love (S1 — `s1_god_is_love`)\n   259→    2. Humans are in God's image (IMAGO_DEI)\n   260→    3. Images participate in what they image (PARTICIPATION)\n   261→    4. ∴ Humans participate in love -/\n   262→theorem humans_participate_in_love\n   263→    (p : Person)\n   264→    (h_intellect : p.hasIntellect = true) :\n   265→    participatesInLove p := by\n   266→  have h_image := IMAGO_DEI p h_intellect\n   267→  have h_god_love := s1_god_is_love.1\n   268→  exact (PARTICIPATION p h_image h_god_love).1\n   269→\n   270→/-- **Lemma: Love is the adequate response to any human person.**\n   271→    From IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION + S1. -/\n   272→theorem love_is_adequate_response_to_persons\n   273→    (p : Person)\n   274→    (h_intellect : p.hasIntellect = true) :\n   275→    loveIsAdequateResponse p := by\n   276→  have h_image := IMAGO_DEI p h_intellect\n   277→  have h_god_love := s1_god_is_love.1\n   278→  exact (PARTICIPATION p h_image h_god_love).2\n   279→\n   280→/-- **AXIOM (bridge): ADEQUATE_RESPONSE_MEANS_ONLY_LOVE.**\n   281→    If love is the adequate response to a person, then ONLY Love\n   282→    (not Use, not Indifference) respects their dignity. This bridges\n   283→    the abstract \"love is adequate\" predicate to the concrete\n   284→    RelationKind enumeration.\n   285→\n   286→    This is a modeling axiom: it connects the opaque predicate\n   287→    `loveIsAdequateResponse` to the concrete `respectsDignity`\n   288→    function on RelationKind. Without it, there would be no link\n   289→    between the participation-based derivation and the three-valued\n   290→    relation kinds.\n   291→\n   292→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — if you accept that love is\n   293→    the adequate response, you accept that only love qualifies. -/\n   294→axiom ADEQUATE_RESPONSE_MEANS_ONLY_LOVE :\n   295→  ∀ (p : Person),\n   296→    loveIsAdequateResponse p →\n   297→    ∀ (rk : RelationKind), rk.respectsDignity → rk = RelationKind.Love\n   298→\n   299→/-- **THEOREM (TOB 15:1; Love and Responsibility ch.1): THE PERSONALIST NORM.**\n   300→    The only adequate response to a person is love. Use violates dignity;\n   301→    indifference fails to recognize dignity. A person is never a mere means.\n   302→\n   303→    This extends beyond Kant: Kant says don't treat persons MERELY as means.\n   304→    Wojtyła says: the positive response (love = willing the person's good\n   305→    for their own sake) is the ONLY adequate response.\n   306→\n   307→    DERIVED FROM: S1 (God is love) + IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION +\n   308→    ADEQUATE_RESPONSE_MEANS_ONLY_LOVE.\n   309→\n   310→    The derivation chain:\n   311→    1. God is love (S1)\n   312→    2. Humans are in God's image (IMAGO_DEI)\n   313→    3. Images participate in what they image (PARTICIPATION)\n   314→    4. ∴ Love is the adequate response to every person\n   315→    5. ∴ Only Love (not Use, not Indifference) respects dignity\n   316→\n   317→    PROVENANCE: The conclusion matches Love and Responsibility (1960),\n   318→    confirmed by TOB audiences (1979-1984). The derivation grounds it\n   319→    in Gen 1:27 (imago Dei) and 1 Jn 4:8 (God is love).\n   320→\n   321→    CONNECTS TO: S1 (God is love), Freedom.lean (love requires freedom). -/\n   322→theorem PERSONALIST_NORM\n   323→    (p : Person)\n   324→    (h_intellect : p.hasIntellect = true) :\n   325→    ∀ (rk : RelationKind), rk.respectsDignity → rk = RelationKind.Love := by\n   326→  have h_adequate := love_is_adequate_response_to_persons p h_intellect\n   327→  exact ADEQUATE_RESPONSE_MEANS_ONLY_LOVE p h_adequate\n   328→\n   329→/-- Denominational tag: broadly ecumenical for the norm itself.\n   330→    The principle that persons must not be used instrumentally is shared\n   331→    across Christian traditions (and indeed across most ethical traditions).\n   332→    The specific APPLICATION to contraception is Catholic. -/\n   333→def personalist_norm_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   334→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical],\n   335→    note := \"Ecumenical for the norm; Catholic for the application to contraception\" }\n   336→\n   337→/-- **THEOREM (TOB 13:2; CCC §1700): DIGNITY IS INTRINSIC.**\n   338→    Person dignity does not depend on consent, capability, or social\n   339→    valuation. It is a property of being a person, period.\n   340→\n   341→    DERIVED FROM: IMAGO_DEI. If dignity is rooted in being God's image,\n   342→    and being God's image is ontological (not functional), then dignity\n   343→    is intrinsic — it does not depend on any external condition.\n   344→\n   345→    PROVENANCE: Gen 1:27 (created in God's image); CCC §1700\n   346→    (\"The dignity of the human person is rooted in his creation in the\n   347→    image and likeness of God\").\n   348→\n   349→    CONNECTS TO: Soul.lean axiom 4 (only_humans_know_god — dignity is\n   350→    grounded in the rational soul's capacity for God). -/\n   351→theorem DIGNITY_IS_INTRINSIC\n   352→    (p : Person)\n   353→    (h_intellect : p.hasIntellect = true) :\n   354→    -- Dignity holds regardless of any external conditions\n   355→    ∀ (_consent _capability _socialValuation : Prop),\n   356→      -- Even if consent is absent, capability is zero, or society\n   357→      -- does not value this person, dignity remains.\n   358→      -- The proof: Imago Dei gives us isImageOfGod p, which is\n   359→      -- ontological and independent of these external conditions.\n   360→      isImageOfGod p := by\n   361→  intro _ _ _\n   362→  exact IMAGO_DEI p h_intellect\n   363→\n   364→/-- Denominational tag: ecumenical. All Christian traditions affirm\n   365→    intrinsic human dignity rooted in the imago Dei. -/\n   366→def dignity_intrinsic_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   367→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical],\n   368→    note := \"Universal Christian teaching; CCC §1700; Gen 1:27\" }\n   369→\n   370→/-- **THEOREM (Love and Responsibility ch.1; TOB 32:3):\n   371→    CONSENT DOES NOT LEGITIMIZE USE.**\n   372→    Even mutual bilateral consent to instrumental treatment remains a\n   373→    violation of the personalist norm. You cannot consent to having your\n   374→    dignity violated, because dignity is not yours to waive.\n   375→\n   376→    DERIVED FROM: PERSONALIST_NORM + the definition of RelationKind.\n   377→    Use.respectsDignity is False by definition. The personalist norm says\n   378→    only Love respects dignity. Therefore Use never respects dignity,\n   379→    regardless of consent. Consent changes the agent's agreement but not\n   380→    the act's moral object — Use remains Use whether or not the other\n   381→    party agrees to it. This connects to the object independence\n   382→    principle from SourcesOfMorality.lean.\n   383→\n   384→    This is the MOST COUNTERINTUITIVE consequence in the Theology of\n   385→    the Body. Modern sexual ethics is built on consent as the sole\n   386→    criterion. TOB says: consent is NECESSARY but NOT SUFFICIENT. Even\n   387→    fully consensual mutual use is still use — and use violates dignity.\n   388→\n   389→    PROVENANCE: Natural law reasoning (Love and Responsibility, 1960);\n   390→    TOB audience 32 (1980). Rooted in the ontological (not contractual)\n   391→    nature of dignity.\n   392→\n   393→    CONNECTS TO: PERSONALIST_NORM (use always violates),\n   394→    DIGNITY_IS_INTRINSIC (dignity cannot be waived),\n   395→    SourcesOfMorality.lean (object independence). -/\n   396→theorem CONSENT_DOES_NOT_LEGITIMIZE_USE\n   397→    (_p1 _p2 : Person) (consent1 consent2 : Prop) :\n   398→    -- Even when both parties fully consent...\n   399→    consent1 → consent2 →\n   400→    -- ...instrumental treatment remains a violation.\n   401→    -- Use.respectsDignity is definitionally False, so any assumption\n   402→    -- of it leads to a contradiction — consent is irrelevant.\n   403→    RelationKind.Use.respectsDignity → False := by\n   404→  intro _ _ h_use_respects\n   405→  -- RelationKind.Use.respectsDignity reduces to False by definition\n   406→  exact h_use_respects\n   407→\n   408→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic for the strong version. Many Protestant\n   409→    ethicists accept consent as sufficient within marriage. -/\n   410→def consent_use_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   411→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   412→    note := \"Challenges the consent-only framework; Protestant traditions vary\" }\n   413→\n   414→/-- **Theorem: The personalist norm grounds the inseparability principle.**\n   415→\n   416→    The inseparability principle (ConjugalEthics.lean) says the unitive\n   417→    and procreative meanings of the conjugal act cannot be deliberately\n   418→    separated. WHY? Because separating them = taking pleasure (unitive)\n   419→    while blocking full self-gift (procreative) = using the other person's\n   420→    body for one's own satisfaction = violating the personalist norm.\n   421→\n   422→    This provides the derivation that Humanae Vitae §12 asserted but\n   423→    never argued for. The inseparability principle is not a standalone\n   424→    axiom — it FOLLOWS from the personalist norm.\n   425→\n   426→    CONNECTS TO: ConjugalEthics.lean inseparability_principle,\n   427→    contraception_violates_inseparability. -/\n   428→theorem personalist_norm_grounds_inseparability\n   429→    (act : ConjugalAct)\n   430→    (_h_unitive : act.unitiveIntact)\n   431→    (h_not_procreative : ¬act.procreativeIntact)\n   432→    -- If procreative meaning is blocked, the act instrumentalizes\n   433→    -- (takes pleasure while withholding full self-gift = use)\n   434→    (_h_blocking_is_use : ¬act.procreativeIntact → RelationKind.Use.isInstrumental) :\n   435→    -- Then the act cannot have both meanings intact\n   436→    ¬act.bothMeaningsIntact := by\n   437→  intro ⟨_, h_proc⟩\n   438→  exact h_not_procreative h_proc\n   439→\n   440→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic for the derivation; the personalist\n   441→    norm itself is ecumenical. -/\n   442→def personalist_grounds_inseparability_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   443→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   444→    note := \"Derives inseparability from personalist norm; application to contraception is Catholic\" }\n   445→\n   446→-- ============================================================================\n   447→-- ## Claim 2: Concupiscence Distorts but Does NOT Destroy\n   448→-- \"Historical man\" retains the capacity for authentic self-gift,\n   449→-- though it is diminished by the Fall.\n   450→-- ============================================================================\n   451→\n   452→/-!\n   453→## Claim 2: Concupiscence Distorts but Does NOT Destroy\n   454→\n   455→TOB's three-state anthropology distinguishes:\n   456→- **Original Integrity**: the state before the Fall (Gen 1-2)\n   457→- **Fallen**: the state after the Fall, marked by concupiscence (Gen 3)\n   458→- **Redeemed**: the state of grace, progressively restored (Rom 6-8)\n   459→\n   460→The key claim: in the Fallen state, the capacity for authentic self-gift\n   461→(what TOB calls the \"nuptial meaning of the body\") is REDUCED but NOT\n   462→DESTROYED. This is the calibration that distinguishes Catholic\n   463→anthropology from both Pelagian optimism and Calvinist pessimism.\n   464→-/\n   465→\n   466→/-- The three anthropological states in salvation history.\n   467→    Every human person exists in one of these states with respect to\n   468→    their capacity for authentic self-gift.\n   469→\n   470→    MODELING CHOICE: These are discrete states, not a continuum. The\n   471→    transitions (Fall, Redemption) are events, not gradual shifts. But\n   472→    WITHIN the Redeemed state, restoration is gradual (see\n   473→    REDEMPTION_IS_PROGRESSIVE below). -/\n   474→inductive AnthropologicalState where\n   475→  /-- Before the Fall: full integrity, no concupiscence.\n   476→      The human person's desires are perfectly ordered toward the good. -/\n   477→  | OriginalIntegrity\n   478→  /-- After the Fall: concupiscence present, desires disordered.\n   479→      The capacity for self-gift is diminished but not destroyed. -/\n   480→  | Fallen\n   481→  /-- Under grace: being restored progressively.\n   482→      The capacity for self-gift is being healed and elevated. -/\n   483→  | Redeemed\n   484→\n   485→/-- The capacity for authentic self-gift — what TOB calls the\n   486→    \"nuptial meaning of the body.\" This is the ability to give oneself\n   487→    fully and freely to another person in love.\n   488→\n   489→    MODELING CHOICE: Graded like FreedomDegree (Freedom.lean). The\n   490→    capacity admits of degrees — you can have more or less of it.\n   491→    Zero would mean total incapacity for self-gift (total depravity).\n   492→    Maximum would mean perfect self-gift (original integrity or\n   493→    glorified state). -/\n   494→structure NuptialCapacity where\n   495→  /-- The degree of capacity (0 = none, higher = more) -/\n   496→  level : Nat\n   497→  /-- Whether desires are properly ordered toward the other's good -/\n   498→  desiresOrdered : Prop\n   499→  /-- Whether the person can freely choose self-gift over self-gratification -/\n   500→  canChooseSelfGift : Prop\n   501→\n   502→/-- A maximum nuptial capacity — the state of Original Integrity. -/\n   503→def NuptialCapacity.maximum : NuptialCapacity :=\n   504→  { level := 100, desiresOrdered := True, canChooseSelfGift := True }\n   505→\n   506→/-- A zero nuptial capacity — what total depravity would look like\n   507→    (the Catholic position denies this ever obtains). -/\n   508→def NuptialCapacity.zero : NuptialCapacity :=\n   509→  { level := 0, desiresOrdered := False, canChooseSelfGift := False }\n   510→\n   511→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 26:5, 29:4; CCC §405): CONCUPISCENCE DIMINISHES,\n   512→    NOT DESTROYS.**\n   513→    In the Fallen state, nuptial capacity is reduced but non-zero.\n   514→    Concupiscence (the disordering of desires after the Fall) weakens\n   515→    but does not eliminate the capacity for authentic self-gift.\n   516→\n   517→    This is the CENTRAL anthropological calibration of TOB. It says:\n   518→    - Against Pelagianism: the Fall DID cause real damage. Desires are\n   519→      genuinely disordered. Self-gift is harder, not just as easy.\n   520→    - Against Calvinism (total depravity): the Fall did NOT destroy the\n   521→      capacity entirely. Fallen humans CAN still choose self-gift,\n   522→      though imperfectly and with difficulty.\n   523→\n   524→    PROVENANCE: TOB audiences 26, 29 (1980); CCC §405 (\"human nature\n   525→    has not been totally corrupted: it is wounded in the natural powers\n   526→    proper to it\"); Council of Trent Session 5, Canon 1.\n   527→\n   528→    CONNECTS TO: Freedom.lean evil_diminishes_freedom (choosing evil\n   529→    reduces freedom, but doesn't eliminate it),\n   530→    S7 teleological_freedom (freedom is ordered toward the good). -/\n   531→axiom CONCUPISCENCE_DIMINISHES_NOT_DESTROYS :\n   532→  ∀ (nc : NuptialCapacity),\n   533→    -- In the Fallen state, capacity is diminished...\n   534→    nc.level > 0 →\n   535→    -- ...but the ability to choose self-gift remains\n   536→    nc.canChooseSelfGift\n   537→\n   538→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic for the precise calibration. The\n   539→    three-state structure (creation-fall-redemption) is ecumenical;\n   540→    the claim that the Fall does NOT produce total depravity is the\n   541→    Catholic distinctive (against Reformed theology). -/\n   542→def concupiscence_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   543→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   544→    note := \"Calibration is Catholic; three-state structure is ecumenical (creation-fall-redemption)\" }\n   545→\n   546→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 1-4; CCC §374-379, 396-409, 1987-1995):\n   547→    THREE-STATE ANTHROPOLOGY.**\n   548→    Human nature exists in one of three states (Original Integrity,\n   549→    Fallen, Redeemed), each with different freedom and capacity levels.\n   550→\n   551→    PROVENANCE: Scripture (Gen 1-3 for creation and fall; Rom 5-8 for\n   552→    redemption); CCC §374-379 (original justice), §396-409 (the fall),\n   553→    §1987-1995 (justification/grace).\n   554→\n   555→    CONNECTS TO: Freedom.lean FreedomDegree (each state has a different\n   556→    freedom level). -/\n   557→axiom THREE_STATE_ANTHROPOLOGY :\n   558→  ∀ (state : AnthropologicalState),\n   559→    match state with\n   560→    | .OriginalIntegrity => True   -- Full capacity\n   561→    | .Fallen            => True   -- Diminished capacity (but non-zero)\n   562→    | .Redeemed          => True   -- Capacity being restored\n   563→\n   564→/-- Denominational tag: the three-state structure is ecumenical. -/\n   565→def three_state_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   566→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical],\n   567→    note := \"Creation-fall-redemption narrative is shared across all Christian traditions\" }\n   568→\n   569→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 49:3; CCC §1999, §2001): REDEMPTION IS PROGRESSIVE.**\n   570→    Grace restores nuptial capacity incrementally, not instantaneously.\n   571→    The Redeemed state is a PROCESS, not an event (though it begins\n   572→    with an event — baptism/justification).\n   573→\n   574→    PROVENANCE: CCC §2001 (\"The preparation of man for the reception of\n   575→    grace is already a work of grace\"); Phil 1:6 (\"he who began a good\n   576→    work in you will carry it on to completion\"); 2 Cor 3:18 (\"being\n   577→    transformed… from one degree of glory to another\").\n   578→\n   579→    CONNECTS TO: S8 (grace is transformative, not merely forensic —\n   580→    transformation takes time), T2 (grace preserves freedom — progressive\n   581→    restoration requires ongoing cooperation). -/\n   582→axiom REDEMPTION_IS_PROGRESSIVE :\n   583→  ∀ (nc1 nc2 : NuptialCapacity),\n   584→    -- If capacity increases from nc1 to nc2...\n   585→    nc1.level < nc2.level →\n   586→    -- ...it happens through a process (not instantaneously)\n   587→    -- Modeled as: intermediate levels exist\n   588→    ∃ (nc_mid : NuptialCapacity),\n   589→      nc1.level < nc_mid.level ∧ nc_mid.level < nc2.level\n   590→\n   591→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic (transformative grace is progressive).\n   592→    Lutheran view: justification is forensic and instantaneous.\n   593→    Reformed view: sanctification is progressive, but justification\n   594→    is a one-time declaration. -/\n   595→def redemption_progressive_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   596→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   597→    note := \"Catholic: grace progressively transforms. Lutheran: justification is forensic/instantaneous\" }\n   598→\n   599→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 49:3; CCC §2002; cf. T2): COOPERATION REQUIRED.**\n   600→    Restoration of nuptial capacity requires the person's free\n   601→    cooperation with grace. Grace enables but does not coerce.\n   602→\n   603→    This is T2 (grace preserves freedom) applied to sexual ethics:\n   604→    you cannot be FORCED into the capacity for authentic self-gift.\n   605→    It must be freely cultivated.\n   606→\n   607→    PROVENANCE: CCC §2002 (\"God's free initiative demands man's free\n   608→    response\"); Council of Trent Session 6, Chapter 5; TOB audience 49.\n   609→\n   610→    CONNECTS TO: T2 (grace preserves freedom), t2_grace_preserves_freedom\n   611→    (Axioms.lean). -/\n   612→axiom COOPERATION_REQUIRED :\n   613→  ∀ (p : Person) (g : Grace) (nc : NuptialCapacity),\n   614→    -- Grace is given and the person has some capacity...\n   615→    graceGiven p g → nc.level > 0 →\n   616→    -- ...but restoration requires free cooperation\n   617→    cooperatesWithGrace p g → nc.canChooseSelfGift\n   618→\n   619→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic (synergism). -/\n   620→def cooperation_required_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   621→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   622→    note := \"Catholic synergism: grace + free cooperation. Against monergism.\" }\n   623→\n   624→/-- **Theorem: The Fallen state is BETWEEN Pelagianism and total depravity.**\n   625→\n   626→    Pelagianism: the Fall caused no damage to nuptial capacity.\n   627→    Total depravity (Calvinism): the Fall destroyed nuptial capacity entirely.\n   628→    Catholic (TOB): the Fall diminished but did not destroy nuptial capacity.\n   629→\n   630→    We show this by exhibiting: capacity is non-zero (against Calvinism)\n   631→    AND capacity is less than maximum (against Pelagianism).\n   632→\n   633→    CONNECTS TO: CONCUPISCENCE_DIMINISHES_NOT_DESTROYS,\n   634→    Freedom.lean evil_diminishes_freedom. -/\n   635→theorem fallen_not_total_depravity\n   636→    (nc : NuptialCapacity)\n   637→    (h_nonzero : nc.level > 0)\n   638→    (h_diminished : nc.level < NuptialCapacity.maximum.level) :\n   639→    -- Non-zero capacity (against total depravity)...\n   640→    nc.level > 0\n   641→    -- ...AND less than maximum (against Pelagianism)\n   642→    ∧ nc.level < 100 := by\n   643→  exact ⟨h_nonzero, h_diminished⟩\n   644→\n   645→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic for the calibration. -/\n   646→def fallen_not_total_depravity_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   647→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   648→    note := \"Catholic calibration between Pelagian optimism and Calvinist pessimism\" }\n   649→\n   650→-- ============================================================================\n   651→-- ## Claim 3: \"The Body, and It Alone, Is Capable of Making Visible\n   652→--    What Is Invisible\"\n   653→-- (TOB 19:4)\n   654→-- ============================================================================\n   655→\n   656→/-!\n   657→## Claim 3: The Body as Sign\n   658→\n   659→This is perhaps TOB's most original philosophical contribution. It says:\n   660→\n   661→1. The body is a SIGN — it bears meaning that refers beyond itself to\n   662→   the spiritual (the person's interior life, their dignity, their\n   663→   vocation to love).\n   664→2. The body is the ONLY sign — in the created order, spiritual realities\n   665→   are accessible ONLY through material signs.\n   666→3. Signs can be truthful or lying — a bodily act that contradicts its\n   667→   inherent meaning is a \"lie told with the body.\"\n   668→\n   669→This is NOT the same as hylomorphism (P1, Soul.lean). Hylomorphism says\n   670→the soul is the FORM of the body (constitutive relation). Body-as-sign\n   671→says the body REVEALS the soul (semiotic relation). The form-relation\n   672→is ontological; the sign-relation is epistemological.\n   673→-/\n   674→\n   675→/-- Whether a bodily act bears meaning that refers beyond itself\n   676→    to the spiritual. -/\n   677→opaque isSign : Prop → Prop\n   678→\n   679→/-- Whether a material sign makes a spiritual reality accessible\n   680→    (epistemically available) to persons in the created order. -/\n   681→opaque makesAccessible : Prop → Prop → Prop\n   682→\n   683→/-- The inherent meaning of a bodily act — what it signifies by\n   684→    its nature, independent of the agent's subjective intention.\n   685→    Example: the conjugal act inherently signifies total self-gift. -/\n   686→opaque inherentMeaning : Prop → Prop\n   687→\n   688→/-- Whether a bodily act contradicts its inherent meaning. -/\n   689→def contradictsInherentMeaning (bodilyAct : Prop) (agentAction : Prop) : Prop :=\n   690→  inherentMeaning bodilyAct ∧ ¬agentAction\n   691→\n   692→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 19:4): BODY AS SIGN.**\n   693→    The body is a sign — it bears meaning that refers beyond itself\n   694→    to the spiritual. The body reveals the person.\n   695→\n   696→    This is NOT hylomorphism (P1). Hylomorphism says the soul is the\n   697→    FORM of the body (the soul makes matter into a body). Body-as-sign\n   698→    says the body REVEALS the soul (the body makes the invisible person\n   699→    visible). The first is an ontological claim about constitution; the\n   700→    second is a semiotic claim about manifestation.\n   701→\n   702→    PROVENANCE: TOB audience 19 (1980); Rom 1:20 (\"his invisible\n   703→    attributes… have been clearly perceived… in the things that have\n   704→    been made\"); CCC §1146 (\"Signs of the human world… can express\n   705→    the presence of God\").\n   706→\n   707→    CONNECTS TO: Soul.lean (hylomorphism — the body CAN be a sign\n   708→    because the soul IS its form; form grounds sign). -/\n   709→axiom BODY_AS_SIGN :\n   710→  ∀ (bodilyAct : Prop), isSign bodilyAct\n   711→\n   712→/-- Denominational tag: ecumenical for the general principle that\n   713→    bodies have spiritual significance. Catholic + Orthodox for the\n   714→    strong semiotic version. -/\n   715→def body_as_sign_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   716→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   717→    note := \"Strong version: Catholic + Orthodox. General principle (bodies have spiritual significance): ecumenical\" }\n   718→\n   719→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 19:4; CCC §1146-1148): MATERIAL MEDIATION.**\n   720→    In the created order, spiritual realities are accessible ONLY\n   721→    through material signs. The body is the exclusive medium through\n   722→    which the invisible becomes visible.\n   723→\n   724→    This is the \"it alone\" exclusivity claim. It says: you cannot\n   725→    access spiritual realities directly (in this life). You must go\n   726→    through matter — through bodies, through signs, through sacraments.\n   727→\n   728→    PROVENANCE: TOB audience 19 (1980); CCC §1146 (\"In human life,\n   729→    signs and symbols occupy an important place\"); CCC §1148 (\"the\n   730→    cosmos… can become the place where God's presence is manifested\");\n   731→    Jn 1:14 (\"The Word became flesh\" — God himself used material\n   732→    mediation to reveal himself).\n   733→\n   734→    CONNECTS TO: T3 (sacramental efficacy — if material signs are the\n   735→    ONLY channel, then sacraments are necessary, not optional). -/\n   736→axiom MATERIAL_MEDIATION :\n   737→  ∀ (spiritualReality : Prop),\n   738→    -- If a spiritual reality is made accessible...\n   739→    (∃ (materialSign : Prop), makesAccessible materialSign spiritualReality) →\n   740→    -- ...it is accessible ONLY through material signs\n   741→    ∀ (channel : Prop), makesAccessible channel spiritualReality → isSign channel\n   742→\n   743→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic + Orthodox for the strong version.\n   744→    Protestants generally affirm that God can work through material\n   745→    means but deny the exclusivity claim (God can also work directly\n   746→    through the Word alone). -/\n   747→def material_mediation_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   748→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   749→    note := \"Strong exclusivity: Catholic + Orthodox. Protestants: God also works directly through the Word\" }\n   750→\n   751→/-- **AXIOM (TOB 32:3; Love and Responsibility ch.3): SIGN TRUTHFULNESS.**\n   752→    A bodily act that contradicts its inherent meaning is a \"lie told\n   753→    with the body.\" Just as spoken words can be true or false, bodily\n   754→    acts can be truthful (expressing what they inherently mean) or\n   755→    lying (contradicting what they inherently mean).\n   756→\n   757→    Example: The conjugal act inherently means \"I give myself totally\n   758→    to you.\" If performed while deliberately withholding fertility\n   759→    (contraception), the body \"says\" total self-gift while the agent\n   760→    withholds — this is a contradiction, a body-lie.\n   761→\n   762→    PROVENANCE: TOB audience 32 (1980); Love and Responsibility ch.3;\n   763→    CCC §2370 (contraception as contrary to the moral law).\n   764→\n   765→    CONNECTS TO: PERSONALIST_NORM (body-lies instrumentalize the other\n   766→    person), ConjugalEthics.lean inseparability_principle. -/\n   767→axiom SIGN_TRUTHFULNESS :\n   768→  ∀ (bodilyAct agentAction : Prop),\n   769→    -- If the body's inherent meaning is contradicted by the agent's action...\n   770→    contradictsInherentMeaning bodilyAct agentAction →\n   771→    -- ...the act is a lie told with the body (morally disordered)\n   772→    isEvil (contradictsInherentMeaning bodilyAct agentAction)\n   773→\n   774→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic + Orthodox for the strong version.\n   775→    The general principle that bodily acts have moral significance\n   776→    is ecumenical. -/\n   777→def sign_truthfulness_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   778→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   779→    note := \"Strong version: Catholic + Orthodox. General principle: ecumenical\" }\n   780→\n   781→/-- **Theorem: The body-as-sign principle grounds sacramental efficacy.**\n   782→\n   783→    If spiritual realities are accessible ONLY through material signs\n   784→    (MATERIAL_MEDIATION), then any channel through which grace reaches\n   785→    a person must be a material sign — which is exactly what a sacrament\n   786→    is. Therefore sacraments are NECESSARY (not just helpful) for grace\n   787→    to reach persons in the created order.\n   788→\n   789→    This derives T3 (sacramental efficacy, Axioms.lean t3_sacramental_efficacy)\n   790→    from the body-as-sign anthropology rather than asserting it as a\n   791→    standalone tradition.\n   792→\n   793→    CONNECTS TO: T3 (t3_sacramental_efficacy), MATERIAL_MEDIATION,\n   794→    BODY_AS_SIGN. -/\n   795→theorem body_sign_grounds_sacraments\n   796→    (spiritualReality : Prop)\n   797→    (materialSign : Prop)\n   798→    (h_accessible : makesAccessible materialSign spiritualReality)\n   799→    (h_mediation : (∃ (ms : Prop), makesAccessible ms spiritualReality) →\n   800→      ∀ (channel : Prop), makesAccessible channel spiritualReality → isSign channel) :\n   801→    -- Any channel conveying this spiritual reality must be a sign\n   802→    isSign materialSign := by\n   803→  exact h_mediation ⟨materialSign, h_accessible⟩ materialSign h_accessible\n   804→\n   805→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic for the derivation of sacramental\n   806→    necessity from material mediation. -/\n   807→def body_sign_sacraments_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   808→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   809→    note := \"Derives T3 from material mediation; Protestant: sacraments are signs, not necessary channels\" }\n   810→\n   811→/-- **Theorem: Contraception is a lie told with the body.**\n   812→\n   813→    The conjugal act has an inherent meaning (total self-gift, including\n   814→    fertility). Contraception retains the bodily act while withholding\n   815→    fertility. This contradicts the act's inherent meaning — the body\n   816→    \"says\" total gift while the agent withholds. By SIGN_TRUTHFULNESS,\n   817→    this contradiction is a body-lie, which is morally disordered.\n   818→\n   819→    This provides a SECOND derivation of the immorality of contraception\n   820→    (the first being the inseparability principle from ConjugalEthics.lean).\n   821→    The two derivations converge: the inseparability principle says you\n   822→    can't separate the meanings; the body-lie theorem says separating them\n   823→    is a form of lying.\n   824→\n   825→    CONNECTS TO: ConjugalEthics.lean contraception_violates_inseparability,\n   826→    SIGN_TRUTHFULNESS, PERSONALIST_NORM. -/\n   827→theorem contraception_is_body_lie\n   828→    (conjugalActMeaning : Prop)  -- \"total self-gift including fertility\"\n   829→    (contraceptiveAction : Prop) -- \"self-gift minus fertility\"\n   830→    (_h_inherent : inherentMeaning conjugalActMeaning)\n   831→    (_h_withholds : ¬contraceptiveAction)\n   832→    (h_contradicts : contradictsInherentMeaning conjugalActMeaning contraceptiveAction) :\n   833→    -- Contraception is morally disordered (a body-lie)\n   834→    isEvil (contradictsInherentMeaning conjugalActMeaning contraceptiveAction) := by\n   835→  exact SIGN_TRUTHFULNESS conjugalActMeaning contraceptiveAction h_contradicts\n   836→\n   837→/-- Denominational tag: Catholic. -/\n   838→def contraception_body_lie_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   839→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic],\n   840→    note := \"Catholic: contraception contradicts the body's sign-meaning. CCC §2370\" }\n   841→\n   842→/-!\n   843→## Summary of Hidden Assumptions\n   844→\n   845→Formalizing the three core TOB claims required these assumptions:\n   846→\n   847→1. **Imago Dei** (AXIOM) — humans are made in God's image. This is the\n   848→   ontological ground of dignity. Combined with S1 (God is love) and\n   849→   PARTICIPATION, it yields the personalist norm as a THEOREM.\n   850→\n   851→2. **Participation** (AXIOM) — an image participates in what it images.\n   852→   This is the Thomistic metaphysical bridge: if God is love and humans\n   853→   are God's image, then humans participate in love, making love the\n   854→   adequate response to them.\n   855→\n   856→3. **Adequate response bridge** (AXIOM) — if love is the adequate\n   857→   response to a person, then only the Love orientation (not Use or\n   858→   Indifference) respects dignity. This is a modeling axiom connecting\n   859→   the opaque participation predicate to the concrete RelationKind type.\n   860→\n   861→4. **The personalist norm** (THEOREM, formerly axiom) — derived from\n   862→   S1 + IMAGO_DEI + PARTICIPATION. Use always violates dignity, even\n   863→   with consent.\n   864→\n   865→5. **Consent does not legitimize use** (THEOREM, formerly axiom) —\n   866→   derived from the definition of RelationKind: Use.respectsDignity\n   867→   is definitionally False, so consent is irrelevant.\n   868→\n   869→6. **Dignity is intrinsic** (THEOREM, formerly axiom) — derived from\n   870→   IMAGO_DEI: the image of God is ontological, not dependent on\n   871→   consent, capability, or social valuation.\n   872→\n   873→7. **The Fall diminished but did not destroy** — this is a specific\n   874→   calibration claim. Too optimistic (Pelagianism) and too pessimistic\n   875→   (Calvinism) are both rejected. The exact degree of damage is an\n   876→   empirical-metaphysical claim that cannot be derived from first principles.\n   877→\n   878→8. **Redemption is progressive, not instantaneous** — transformation takes\n   879→   time and requires cooperation. This connects to the Catholic rejection\n   880→   of forensic justification (Lutheran) and irresistible grace (Calvinist).\n   881→\n   882→9. **The body is a sign, not just matter** — the body bears meaning. This\n   883→   is a semiotic claim, distinct from hylomorphism (ontological).\n   884→\n   885→10. **Material mediation is exclusive** — spiritual realities are accessible\n   886→    ONLY through material signs. This is the strongest claim and the one\n   887→    most Protestants would reject (they affirm God can work directly through\n   888→    the Word without material mediation).\n   889→\n   890→11. **Signs can lie** — bodily acts can contradict their inherent meaning,\n   891→    and such contradictions are morally disordered. This requires that bodily\n   892→    acts HAVE inherent meanings (a teleological claim about the body).\n   893→\n   894→**Structural note**: The refactoring from 3 axioms to 2 axioms (+1 bridge\n   895→axiom) is a net improvement because the personalist norm, dignity, and\n   896→consent theorems now have explicit theological grounding rather than being\n   897→asserted as standalone principles. The derivation chain (God is love →\n   898→humans image God → humans participate in love → love is the adequate\n   899→response → only Love respects dignity) makes the dependency structure\n   900→visible.\n   901→-/\n   902→\n   903→end Catlib.MoralTheology.TheologyOfBody\n   904→"}]},"uuid":"5322c8d2-c36d-4e9e-887a-95e1687b3c69","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:31.539Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"c191a51a-c114-41cd-a517-16b305680f5f","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"f99fd5b1-729d-4a40-9d7e-f58dacc8d8dd","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_015rGuRX55WB4FjFHkfDcmqX","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→import Catlib.Creed.Soul\n     3→import Catlib.Creed.Purgatory\n     4→import Catlib.Creed.DivineModes\n     5→\n     6→set_option autoImplicit false\n     7→\n     8→/-!\n     9→# The Three Major Marian Dogmas\n    10→\n    11→## The Catechism claims\n    12→\n    13→\"Called in the Gospels 'the mother of Jesus,' Mary is acclaimed by Elizabeth,\n    14→at the prompting of the Spirit, as 'the mother of my Lord.'\" (CCC §495)\n    15→\n    16→\"Mary is truly 'Mother of God' since she is the mother of the eternal Son\n    17→of God made man, who is God himself.\" (CCC §509)\n    18→\n    19→\"The most Blessed Virgin Mary was, from the first moment of her conception,\n    20→by a singular grace and privilege of almighty God and by virtue of the merits\n    21→of Jesus Christ, Savior of the human race, preserved immune from all stain\n    22→of original sin.\" (CCC §491, quoting Ineffabilis Deus)\n    23→\n    24→\"The most Blessed Virgin Mary, when the course of her earthly life was\n    25→completed, was taken up body and soul into the glory of heaven.\" (CCC §974,\n    26→quoting Munificentissimus Deus)\n    27→\n    28→## The key structural insight\n    29→\n    30→The three Marian dogmas form a DEPENDENCY CHAIN:\n    31→\n    32→```\n    33→Hypostatic Union (Chalcedon 451)\n    34→  └→ Theotokos (Ephesus 431) [+ MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS]\n    35→       └→ Immaculate Conception (1854) [+ RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION + FITTINGNESS + PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY]\n    36→            └→ Assumption (1950) [+ SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY + P1 hylomorphism]\n    37→```\n    38→\n    39→Each later dogma requires every earlier one. Rejecting any link breaks\n    40→the entire chain downstream.\n    41→\n    42→## Prediction\n    43→\n    44→I expect three things:\n    45→1. **Theotokos will be surprisingly easy** — it is really a Christological\n    46→   theorem (about Christ's nature) disguised as a Marian title. The proof\n    47→   should be straightforward from the hypostatic union.\n    48→2. **Immaculate Conception will be assumption-rich** — it will require the\n    49→   most novel axioms (retroactive redemption, fittingness-as-evidence,\n    50→   papal infallibility). The dependency chain IS the finding.\n    51→3. **The Assumption will reveal the hylomorphism connection** — the reason\n    52→   the Assumption insists on BODILY assumption (not just the soul going to\n    53→   heaven) is precisely because hylomorphism (P1) says the person IS the\n    54→   body-soul composite. Without P1, you could just say Mary's soul went to\n    55→   heaven and be done.\n    56→\n    57→## Findings\n    58→\n    59→- **Prediction 1 confirmed**: Theotokos IS a Christological theorem. The\n    60→  proof is two lines: Christ is a divine person (hypostatic union), Mary\n    61→  bore Christ (Scripture), motherhood targets persons not natures, therefore\n    62→  Mary bore a divine person. The \"Marian\" dogma is really about Christ.\n    63→- **Prediction 2 confirmed**: Immaculate Conception requires FOUR new axioms\n    64→  beyond the base set. The most striking is RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION — the claim\n    65→  that Christ's merits can be applied backwards in time to Mary's conception.\n    66→  This is a genuinely novel metaphysical commitment with no clear parallel\n    67→  elsewhere in the system. FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE is also distinctive:\n    68→  it turns an aesthetic judgment (\"it would be fitting\") into an epistemological\n    69→  principle (\"therefore God did it\").\n    70→- **Prediction 3 confirmed**: The Assumption explicitly depends on P1\n    71→  (hylomorphism). Without the soul-as-form-of-body model, there is no\n    72→  theological reason to insist on BODILY assumption. The connection to\n    73→  DivineModes also emerged: Mary enters the heavenState (full beatifying\n    74→  communion, body and soul).\n    75→- **Surprise**: The denominational pattern is itself informative. Theotokos\n    76→  is nearly ecumenical (Luther and Calvin accepted it). Immaculate Conception\n    77→  is Catholic only (Orthodox reject the Western framing; Protestants reject\n    78→  it entirely). The Assumption is Catholic only (Orthodox accept \"Dormition\"\n    79→  but with different framing). The axiom count tracks the denominational\n    80→  narrowing: 2 axioms (ecumenical) → 6 axioms (Catholic only) → 7+ axioms\n    81→  (Catholic only). More axioms = fewer traditions that accept the conclusion.\n    82→- **Assessment**: Tier 3 — the dependency chain and axiom-accumulation pattern\n    83→  are genuine structural findings. The connection between hylomorphism and\n    84→  the Assumption is non-obvious.\n    85→-/\n    86→\n    87→namespace Catlib.Creed\n    88→\n    89→open Catlib\n    90→\n    91→-- ============================================================================\n    92→-- FOUNDATIONAL TYPES FOR CHRISTOLOGY AND MARIOLOGY\n    93→-- ============================================================================\n    94→\n    95→/-- A nature — divine or human. In Christology, the question of how many\n    96→    natures a person has is the central issue. -/\n    97→inductive Nature where\n    98→  /-- The divine nature — possessed by God -/\n    99→  | divine\n   100→  /-- Human nature — possessed by every human being -/\n   101→  | human\n   102→\n   103→/-- A divine person — an individual subsistent in the divine or incarnate realm.\n   104→    The key Christological point: a person can possess MULTIPLE natures\n   105→    (as Christ does under the hypostatic union). -/\n   106→structure IncarnateSubject where\n   107→  /-- The name or identifier of this person -/\n   108→  name : String\n   109→  /-- The natures this person possesses -/\n   110→  natures : List Nature\n   111→  /-- Whether this person is divine (has the divine nature) -/\n   112→  isDivine : Prop\n   113→\n   114→/-- Whether a person has a given nature in their list. -/\n   115→def IncarnateSubject.hasNature (p : IncarnateSubject) (n : Nature) : Prop :=\n   116→  n ∈ p.natures\n   117→\n   118→/-- The motherhood relation: one person bore another.\n   119→    Motherhood is a relation between PERSONS, not between a mother and\n   120→    a nature. This distinction is the crux of the Theotokos dogma. -/\n   121→opaque bore : Person → IncarnateSubject → Prop\n   122→\n   123→/-- Whether a person has original sin. -/\n   124→opaque hasOriginalSin : Person → Prop\n   125→\n   126→/-- Whether a person is preserved from original sin at conception. -/\n   127→opaque preservedFromOriginalSin : Person → Prop\n   128→\n   129→/-- Whether a person ever committed any personal sin. -/\n   130→opaque committedPersonalSin : Person → Prop\n   131→\n   132→/-- Whether a person's body is subject to the corruption that results from sin. -/\n   133→opaque bodySubjectToCorruption : Person → Prop\n   134→\n   135→/-- Whether a person was assumed body and soul into heavenly glory. -/\n   136→opaque bodilyAssumed : Person → Prop\n   137→\n   138→/-- Christ, as a IncarnateSubject with two natures. -/\n   139→def christ : IncarnateSubject :=\n   140→  { name := \"Christ\"\n   141→    natures := [Nature.divine, Nature.human]\n   142→    isDivine := True }\n   143→\n   144→/-- Mary, as a human person (using the foundation Person type). -/\n   145→def mary : Person := Person.human\n   146→\n   147→-- ============================================================================\n   148→-- DOGMA 1: THEOTOKOS — Mother of God (Council of Ephesus, 431)\n   149→-- ============================================================================\n   150→\n   151→/-!\n   152→## Dogma 1: Theotokos\n   153→\n   154→The key insight: Theotokos is a CHRISTOLOGICAL test disguised as a Marian title.\n   155→To deny that Mary is the Mother of God, you must deny either:\n   156→- The hypostatic union (Christ is one divine person with two natures), OR\n   157→- That motherhood targets persons (not natures)\n   158→\n   159→Nestorius tried a third option — \"Mary is Christotokos (mother of Christ's\n   160→human nature) but not Theotokos (mother of God)\" — but this implicitly\n   161→separates Christ into two persons (one divine, one human), which IS the\n   162→denial of the hypostatic union.\n   163→\n   164→Denominational scope: NEARLY ECUMENICAL. Luther explicitly affirmed Theotokos\n   165→(\"Mary is the Mother of God\" — Luther's Works, vol. 21, p. 326). Calvin\n   166→also accepted it (Institutes II.14.4). The major Reformers agreed because\n   167→they agreed on the hypostatic union.\n   168→-/\n   169→\n   170→/-- **AXIOM: HYPOSTATIC_UNION** — Christ is one person with two natures (divine and human).\n   171→    Source: Council of Chalcedon (451); CCC §466-469.\n   172→    \"We confess that one and the same Christ, Lord, and only-begotten Son, is to\n   173→    be acknowledged in two natures... the distinction of natures being in no way\n   174→    abolished by their union, but rather the characteristic property of each nature\n   175→    being preserved, and concurring into one Person.\" (Chalcedon Definition)\n   176→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — accepted by Catholic, Orthodox, and all\n   177→    major Protestant traditions. Denial of this IS Christological heresy by the\n   178→    standards of virtually all Christians. -/\n   179→axiom HYPOSTATIC_UNION :\n   180→  christ.isDivine ∧\n   181→  christ.hasNature Nature.divine ∧\n   182→  christ.hasNature Nature.human\n   183→\n   184→def hypostatic_union_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Chalcedon 451; CCC §466-469\"\n   185→def hypostatic_union_tag : DenominationalTag := ecumenical\n   186→\n   187→/-- **AXIOM: MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS** — Motherhood is a relation to a PERSON,\n   188→    not to a nature. A mother does not give birth to a nature — she gives birth\n   189→    to a person who HAS that nature.\n   190→    Source: Council of Ephesus (431); CCC §466, §495.\n   191→    This is the hidden axiom that Nestorius denied. He wanted to say Mary gave\n   192→    birth to Christ's human nature but not to Christ's divine nature. But you\n   193→    don't give birth to natures — you give birth to persons.\n   194→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — once stated clearly, virtually no one\n   195→    denies this. Even Nestorius did not explicitly deny it; he simply failed\n   196→    to see its implications. -/\n   197→axiom MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS :\n   198→  ∀ (mother : Person) (child : IncarnateSubject),\n   199→    bore mother child →\n   200→    -- The mother is mother of the PERSON (with all their natures),"}]},"uuid":"41b8e59e-e9bf-4005-818e-57e4b6a2082a","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:32.279Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f99fd5b1-729d-4a40-9d7e-f58dacc8d8dd","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"0d0e5bba-2d46-436c-b0f2-8b7712f372b5","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01ETgHBsew1ZkeRRC7jKHmBr","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import Catlib.Foundations\n     2→import Catlib.MoralTheology.Sin\n     3→import Catlib.Creed.Grace\n     4→import Catlib.Creed.DivineModes\n     5→import Catlib.Creed.Purgatory\n     6→\n     7→/-!\n     8→# CCC §1422–1470: The Sacrament of Reconciliation (Confession)\n     9→\n    10→The most cross-cutting formalization in catlib. This file connects:\n    11→\n    12→- **Basic.lean**: Person, Sin, Grace, Action, FreeChoice, Denomination\n    13→- **Axioms.lean**: S8 (grace necessary & transformative), T2 (grace preserves\n    14→  freedom), T3 (sacramental efficacy), S5 (sin separates)\n    15→- **Authority.lean**: absolution_authority, absolutionDomain, christ_delegates_absolution,\n    16→  apostolic_succession_general, episcopal_delegation\n    17→- **Love.lean**: LoveKind.agape, mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity, agape_requires_freedom\n    18→- **Sin.lean**: SinfulAct, isMortal, GraceState, mortal_sin_causes_loss_of_grace\n    19→- **Grace.lean**: GraceType.prevenient, prevenient_grace_unconditioned,\n    20→  divine_initiative_preserves_freedom, TypedGrace, grace_bootstrapping_resolved\n    21→- **DivineModes.lean**: SoulState, heavenState, hellState, DivineMode\n    22→- **Purgatory.lean**: HolinessDegree, fullyPurified, diedInGrace\n    23→\n    24→## The Catechism claims\n    25→\n    26→\"It is called the sacrament of conversion because it makes sacramentally present\n    27→Jesus' call to conversion.\" (§1423)\n    28→\n    29→\"It is called the sacrament of Penance, since it consecrates the Christian\n    30→sinner's personal and ecclesial steps of conversion, penance, and satisfaction.\"\n    31→(§1423)\n    32→\n    33→\"It is called the sacrament of confession, since the disclosure or confession of\n    34→sins to a priest is an essential element.\" (§1424)\n    35→\n    36→\"It is called the sacrament of Reconciliation, since it imparts to the sinner\n    37→the love of God who reconciles.\" (§1424)\n    38→\n    39→## The three acts of the penitent (§1450-1460)\n    40→\n    41→1. **Contrition**: \"sorrow of the soul and detestation of the sin committed,\n    42→   together with the resolution not to sin again\" (§1451)\n    43→2. **Confession**: \"the confession (or disclosure) of sins… frees in some\n    44→   way and facilitates the reconciliation\" (§1455-1456)\n    45→3. **Satisfaction**: \"an act of reparation that the confessor imposes on\n    46→   the penitent… absolution takes away sin, but it does not remedy all the\n    47→   disorders sin has caused\" (§1459)\n    48→\n    49→## The minister's act (§1461-1467)\n    50→\n    51→\"Since Christ entrusted to his apostles the ministry of reconciliation, bishops\n    52→who are their successors, and priests, the bishops' collaborators, continue to\n    53→exercise this ministry.\" (§1461)\n    54→\n    55→## The effects (§1468-1470)\n    56→\n    57→\"The whole power of the sacrament of Penance consists in restoring us to God's\n    58→grace and joining us with him in an intimate friendship.\" (§1468)\n    59→\n    60→\"Reconciliation with God is thus the purpose and effect of this sacrament.\" (§1468)\n    61→\n    62→\"It must be recalled that… the temporal punishment of sin remains.\" (§1472-1473)\n    63→\n    64→## The grace bootstrapping recurrence (§1489)\n    65→\n    66→\"To come back to communion with God after having lost it through sin is a process\n    67→born of the grace of God who is rich in mercy… One must be moved by grace to\n    68→respond to the merciful love of God who loved us first.\" (§1489)\n    69→\n    70→THIS IS THE SAME BOOTSTRAPPING PROBLEM AS §2001 (Grace.lean):\n    71→- Contrition requires HOPE (a theological virtue)\n    72→- Hope requires GRACE\n    73→- But the sinner is in mortal sin — charity destroyed, separated from God\n    74→- Resolution: PREVENIENT GRACE enables the initial movement toward contrition\n    75→- God initiates the return, just as God initiates the first coming to faith\n    76→\n    77→## The Luther connection\n    78→\n    79→Luther's 95 Theses (1517) were NOT primarily about confession itself —\n    80→they were about INDULGENCES. Indulgences claim to address the TEMPORAL\n    81→PUNISHMENT that remains after absolution (§1472-1473).\n    82→\n    83→The logical chain:\n    84→1. Absolution removes guilt (eternal punishment)\n    85→2. But temporal punishment REMAINS (§1472: \"temporal_punishment_survives_absolution\")\n    86→3. Indulgences claim to remit temporal punishment through the Church's treasury of merit\n    87→4. Luther objected: if guilt is removed, why does punishment remain?\n    88→\n    89→Under Protestant axioms:\n    90→- No purgatory → no post-mortem temporal punishment\n    91→- No temporal punishment → indulgences are incoherent\n    92→- `temporal_punishment_survives_absolution` is the theorem that makes\n    93→  indulgences COHERENT under Catholic axioms and INCOHERENT under Protestant ones\n    94→\n    95→This is why Reconciliation completes the Reformation narrative: the sacrament\n    96→itself is not the main dispute — the RESIDUAL temporal punishment is.\n    97→-/\n    98→\n    99→set_option autoImplicit false\n   100→\n   101→namespace Catlib.Sacraments.Reconciliation\n   102→\n   103→open Catlib\n   104→open Catlib.MoralTheology\n   105→open Catlib.Creed\n   106→open Catlib.Foundations.Love\n   107→\n   108→-- ============================================================================\n   109→-- § 1. Core Types\n   110→-- ============================================================================\n   111→\n   112→/-- Contrition — genuine sorrow for sin with a firm purpose of amendment.\n   113→    CCC §1451: \"Among the penitent's acts contrition occupies first place.\n   114→    Contrition is 'sorrow of the soul and detestation of the sin committed,\n   115→    together with the resolution not to sin again.'\"\n   116→\n   117→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — all Christians agree repentance\n   118→    requires genuine sorrow and intent to change. Even Protestants who\n   119→    reject sacramental confession affirm the need for contrition.\n   120→\n   121→    STRUCTURAL NOTE: Contrition is a FREE ACT of the will. It requires\n   122→    the penitent to (1) recognize the sin, (2) be genuinely sorry, and\n   123→    (3) resolve not to repeat it. All three are volitional.\n   124→\n   125→    Cross-ref: agape_requires_freedom (Love.lean) — contrition, like\n   126→    charity, is impossible without free will. -/\n   127→structure Contrition where\n   128→  /-- The person expressing contrition -/\n   129→  penitent : Person\n   130→  /-- The sin for which the person is contrite -/\n   131→  sin : SinfulAct\n   132→  /-- Genuine sorrow for the sin (not merely fear of punishment) -/\n   133→  genuineSorrow : Prop\n   134→  /-- Firm purpose of amendment — intent not to sin again -/\n   135→  firmPurpose : Prop\n   136→  /-- The penitent acts freely -/\n   137→  isFree : Prop\n   138→\n   139→/-- Confession — the disclosure of sins to a priest.\n   140→    CCC §1456: \"All mortal sins of which penitents after a diligent\n   141→    self-examination are conscious must be recounted by them in confession.\"\n   142→\n   143→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX — sacramental confession\n   144→    to a priest. Protestants hold that confession should be made\n   145→    directly to God (1 Jn 1:9), though Luther himself valued\n   146→    private confession and never abolished it.\n   147→\n   148→    Cross-ref: absolutionDomain (Authority.lean) — the priest's authority\n   149→    to hear confession derives from the same delegation chain as absolution. -/\n   150→structure Confession where\n   151→  /-- The person confessing -/\n   152→  penitent : Person\n   153→  /-- The priest hearing the confession -/\n   154→  priest : Person\n   155→  /-- The sins disclosed -/\n   156→  sinsDisclosed : List SinfulAct\n   157→  /-- The confession is complete (all mortal sins recounted) -/\n   158→  isComplete : Prop\n   159→\n   160→/-- Satisfaction — the penance assigned by the priest.\n   161→    CCC §1459-1460: \"Many sins wrong our neighbor. One must do what is\n   162→    possible in order to repair the harm… absolution takes away sin, but\n   163→    it does not remedy all the disorders sin has caused.\"\n   164→\n   165→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX — penance as a required\n   166→    act. Protestants may encourage acts of reparation but do not require\n   167→    them as part of a sacramental process.\n   168→\n   169→    STRUCTURAL NOTE: Satisfaction addresses TEMPORAL PUNISHMENT — the\n   170→    residual effects of sin that remain even after guilt is removed.\n   171→    This is the connection point to Purgatory.lean and to the\n   172→    indulgence controversy.\n   173→\n   174→    Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — temporal punishment is the same concept\n   175→    that purgatory addresses post-mortem. Satisfaction addresses it\n   176→    pre-mortem. -/\n   177→structure Satisfaction where\n   178→  /-- The person performing the penance -/\n   179→  penitent : Person\n   180→  /-- The penance is actually performed (not merely assigned) -/\n   181→  penancePerformed : Prop\n   182→\n   183→/-- Absolution — the priest's act of forgiving sins in persona Christi.\n   184→    CCC §1461-1462: \"Since Christ entrusted to his apostles the ministry\n   185→    of reconciliation, bishops who are their successors, and priests, the\n   186→    bishops' collaborators, continue to exercise this ministry.\"\n   187→\n   188→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX — the priest pronounces\n   189→    absolution with sacramental authority. Protestants hold that only God\n   190→    forgives sins; ministers can declare forgiveness but not effect it.\n   191→\n   192→    Cross-ref: absolution_authority (Authority.lean) — the priest's\n   193→    authority to absolve traces through the delegation chain:\n   194→    Christ (Mk 2:10) → Apostles (Jn 20:23) → bishops (apostolic\n   195→    succession) → priests (episcopal delegation).\n   196→\n   197→    Cross-ref: P2 two-tier causation (Axioms.lean) — the priest acts as\n   198→    instrumental cause; Christ is the principal cause. The priest's\n   199→    absolution and Christ's forgiveness do not compete (non-contrastive\n   200→    transcendence). -/"}]},"uuid":"038f8fd3-571d-4260-8812-83c23c357fdb","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:32.801Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"0d0e5bba-2d46-436c-b0f2-8b7712f372b5","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}
