{"parentUuid":"dab8e63c-5948-419f-8012-d5e47c072d75","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01LtaDu8i2JrsXFJhETZGPyY","type":"tool_result","content":"   200→    -- The mother is mother of the PERSON (with all their natures),\n   201→    -- not mother of one nature in isolation\n   202→    child.isDivine → True\n   203→\n   204→def motherhood_targets_persons_provenance : Provenance :=\n   205→  Provenance.tradition \"Ephesus 431; CCC §466, §495\"\n   206→def motherhood_targets_persons_tag : DenominationalTag := ecumenical\n   207→\n   208→/-- **GIVEN (Scripture)**: Mary bore Jesus Christ.\n   209→    Source: Lk 1:31 (\"you will conceive in your womb and bear a son\"),\n   210→    Mt 1:18-25, Lk 2:6-7.\n   211→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — no Christian tradition denies this. -/\n   212→axiom MARY_BORE_CHRIST :\n   213→  bore mary christ\n   214→\n   215→def mary_bore_christ_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Lk 1:31; Mt 1:18-25\"\n   216→def mary_bore_christ_tag : DenominationalTag := ecumenical\n   217→\n   218→/-- **THEOREM: Theotokos** — Mary is the Mother of God.\n   219→\n   220→    The proof:\n   221→    1. Mary bore Christ (Scripture: Lk 1:31)\n   222→    2. Christ is a divine person (Hypostatic Union: Chalcedon 451)\n   223→    3. Motherhood targets persons, not natures (Ephesus 431)\n   224→    4. Therefore Mary bore a divine person — she is the Mother of God.\n   225→\n   226→    This is a THEOREM, not an axiom. It FOLLOWS from the hypostatic union\n   227→    plus the principle that motherhood targets persons. The Marian title\n   228→    is really a Christological conclusion.\n   229→\n   230→    Source: Council of Ephesus (431); CCC §495, §509.\n   231→    Denominational scope: Nearly ecumenical. Luther and Calvin both accepted it.\n   232→    Some modern Protestants avoid the title out of discomfort with Marian\n   233→    language, but their own Christology entails it. -/\n   234→theorem theotokos :\n   235→    bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine :=\n   236→  ⟨MARY_BORE_CHRIST, HYPOSTATIC_UNION.1⟩\n   237→\n   238→def theotokos_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   239→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic, Denomination.lutheran, Denomination.reformed]\n   240→    note := \"Nearly ecumenical — Luther and Calvin both accepted; some modern Protestants avoid the title\" }\n   241→\n   242→/-- **THEOREM: rejecting_theotokos_implies_nestorianism** — Denying that Mary is\n   243→    the Mother of God requires denying either the hypostatic union or that\n   244→    motherhood targets persons.\n   245→\n   246→    If you accept both (1) Christ is one divine person with two natures AND\n   247→    (2) motherhood is a relation to persons, then Theotokos follows necessarily.\n   248→    To deny Theotokos you MUST reject at least one premise.\n   249→\n   250→    This is why Ephesus condemned Nestorius: his denial of Theotokos implied\n   251→    (whether he intended it or not) that Christ is two persons, which destroys\n   252→    the hypostatic union.\n   253→\n   254→    Source: Council of Ephesus (431), CCC §466. -/\n   255→theorem rejecting_theotokos_implies_nestorianism\n   256→    (h_union : christ.isDivine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.divine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.human)\n   257→    (h_motherhood : bore mary christ → christ.isDivine → True)\n   258→    (h_bore : bore mary christ) :\n   259→    -- Given the hypostatic union, motherhood-targets-persons, and the\n   260→    -- scriptural fact that Mary bore Christ, theotokos cannot be denied:\n   261→    bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine :=\n   262→  have _ := h_motherhood h_bore h_union.1\n   263→  ⟨h_bore, h_union.1⟩\n   264→\n   265→-- ============================================================================\n   266→-- DOGMA 2: IMMACULATE CONCEPTION (Pius IX, Ineffabilis Deus, 1854)\n   267→-- ============================================================================\n   268→\n   269→/-!\n   270→## Dogma 2: The Immaculate Conception\n   271→\n   272→The most assumption-rich of the Marian dogmas. The dependency chain IS the finding.\n   273→\n   274→This dogma states that Mary was preserved from original sin from the first moment\n   275→of her conception, by a singular grace and privilege of almighty God, in view of\n   276→the merits of Jesus Christ.\n   277→\n   278→### Scripture basis — HONESTLY THIN\n   279→\n   280→The primary text is Lk 1:28 — the angel's greeting \"kecharitomene\" (κεχαριτωμένη),\n   281→which the Vulgate renders \"gratia plena\" (full of grace). Catholics read this as\n   282→implying Mary was in a permanent, complete state of grace from conception.\n   283→Protestants read it as a present description, not a statement about conception.\n   284→\n   285→Gen 3:15 (the protoevangelium — \"I will put enmity between you and the woman\")\n   286→is used typologically. The \"woman\" is read as Mary, and \"total enmity\" with the\n   287→serpent is taken to imply sinlessness. This is typological exegesis, not direct\n   288→statement.\n   289→\n   290→This has the THINNEST scriptural basis of the three major Marian dogmas.\n   291→The definition relies primarily on Tradition, theological reasoning (fittingness),\n   292→and papal authority.\n   293→\n   294→### The four new axioms required\n   295→\n   296→1. ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED — ecumenical (broadly)\n   297→2. RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION — Catholic only, genuinely novel metaphysics\n   298→3. FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE — Catholic only, epistemological principle\n   299→4. PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY — Catholic only, the authority axiom\n   300→\n   301→Each adds assumptions that narrow the denominational scope.\n   302→\n   303→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC ONLY.\n   304→- Orthodox reject the Western framing of original sin (they hold \"ancestral sin\"\n   305→  but not inherited guilt in the Augustinian sense).\n   306→- Protestants reject it entirely (no scriptural basis under sola scriptura,\n   307→  and they reject papal authority to define dogma).\n   308→-/\n   309→\n   310→/-- **AXIOM: ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED** — Original sin is transmitted to every\n   311→    human being at conception. Every person is conceived in a state of\n   312→    separation from original justice.\n   313→    Source: Rom 5:12 (\"sin came into the world through one man, and death\n   314→    through sin, and so death spread to all men because all sinned\");\n   315→    CCC §404 (\"original sin is transmitted with human nature, by propagation,\n   316→    not by imitation\").\n   317→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL (broadly) — Catholic, Orthodox (with\n   318→    different framing as \"ancestral sin\"), and Protestant traditions all\n   319→    hold some version of inherited fallenness. The exact mechanism and\n   320→    nature differ significantly. -/\n   321→axiom ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED :\n   322→  ∀ (p : Person), ¬preservedFromOriginalSin p → hasOriginalSin p\n   323→\n   324→def original_sin_inherited_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rom 5:12; CCC §404\"\n   325→def original_sin_inherited_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   326→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical], note := \"broadly shared; Orthodox frame differently as 'ancestral sin'\" }\n   327→\n   328→/-- **AXIOM: RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION** — Christ's redemptive merits can be\n   329→    applied outside of linear time. Specifically, they can be applied\n   330→    BACKWARDS to Mary's conception \"in view of\" Christ's future sacrifice.\n   331→    Source: CCC §492 (\"From among the descendants of Eve, God chose the\n   332→    Virgin Mary... 'in view of the merits of her Son'\").\n   333→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: This is a genuinely NOVEL metaphysical claim.\n   334→    It asserts that a future event (Christ's death) can have retroactive\n   335→    causal efficacy on a past event (Mary's conception). No other doctrine\n   336→    in the system makes this kind of temporal claim.\n   337→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC ONLY — Protestants reject this as\n   338→    philosophically ungrounded. The claim that redemption can work\n   339→    \"backwards in time\" has no clear parallel in Scripture or in the\n   340→    broader theological tradition. -/\n   341→axiom RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION :\n   342→  ∀ (p : Person),\n   343→    -- If God wills it, redemption can be applied retroactively\n   344→    -- (i.e., before Christ's sacrifice chronologically occurs)\n   345→    godWillsSalvation p →\n   346→    -- Then preservation from original sin is possible even before the Cross\n   347→    True\n   348→\n   349→def retroactive_redemption_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"CCC §492; Ineffabilis Deus\"\n   350→def retroactive_redemption_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   351→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic]\n   352→    note := \"Catholic only — genuinely novel metaphysical claim; no clear parallel in other doctrines\" }\n   353→\n   354→/-- **AXIOM: FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE** — The convenientissimum principle:\n   355→    if something is maximally fitting for God's plan, and God is omnipotent,\n   356→    then God did it.\n   357→    Source: Scholastic theology; Bl. Duns Scotus's \"potuit, decuit, fecit\"\n   358→    (\"God could do it, it was fitting, therefore He did it\");\n   359→    CCC §487-489 (the fittingness arguments for Mary's privileges).\n   360→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: This turns an aesthetic/teleological judgment into\n   361→    an epistemological principle. \"It would be beautiful if X\" becomes\n   362→    \"therefore X is true.\" Protestants reject this as a valid inference.\n   363→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC — rooted in Scholastic theology.\n   364→    Protestants hold that God's actions must be known from Scripture, not\n   365→    inferred from fittingness. -/\n   366→axiom FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE :\n   367→  ∀ (claim : Prop),\n   368→    -- If it is maximally fitting for God's plan\n   369→    -- (placeholder: represented as a Prop that the claim is fitting)\n   370→    True →\n   371→    -- Then we may hold it as true (God who is omnipotent did what was fitting)\n   372→    -- NOTE: This is an axiom schema — it enables concluding truths from\n   373→    -- fittingness arguments. Protestants reject this entire pattern.\n   374→    claim → claim\n   375→\n   376→def fittingness_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Scholastic theology; Duns Scotus potuit-decuit-fecit\"\n   377→def fittingness_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   378→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic]\n   379→    note := \"Catholic — Protestants reject fittingness as epistemological evidence\" }\n   380→\n   381→/-- **AXIOM: PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY** — The Pope, when speaking ex cathedra on\n   382→    matters of faith and morals, defines dogma that is irreformable.\n   383→    Source: Vatican I (1870), Pastor Aeternus; CCC §891.\n   384→    \"The Roman Pontiff, head of the college of bishops, enjoys this\n   385→    infallibility in virtue of his office, when, as supreme pastor and teacher\n   386→    of all the faithful... he proclaims by a definitive act a doctrine\n   387→    pertaining to faith or morals.\"\n   388→    This is the AUTHORITY axiom. Without it, no pope can unilaterally define\n   389→    new dogma. The Immaculate Conception (1854) and the Assumption (1950)\n   390→    are the only two ex cathedra dogmatic definitions in history.\n   391→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC ONLY — this is the authority axiom that\n   392→    Protestantism most sharply rejects. Orthodox reject papal supremacy. -/\n   393→axiom PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY :\n   394→  ∀ (dogma : Prop),\n   395→    -- If the Pope defines a dogma ex cathedra\n   396→    True →\n   397→    -- The dogma is irreformable (held to be true)\n   398→    dogma → dogma\n   399→\n   400→def papal_infallibility_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Vatican I 1870; CCC §891\"\n   401→def papal_infallibility_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   402→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic]\n   403→    note := \"Catholic only — the authority axiom Protestantism most sharply rejects; Orthodox reject papal supremacy\" }\n   404→\n   405→/-- Whether it is fitting that the Mother of God be sinless. -/\n   406→opaque fittingThatMotherOfGodBeSinless : Prop\n   407→\n   408→/-- Whether the Pope has defined the Immaculate Conception ex cathedra. -/\n   409→opaque icDefinedExCathedra : Prop\n   410→\n   411→/-!\n   412→### The Immaculate Conception: proof strategy\n   413→\n   414→The argument chain:\n   415→1. Mary is the Mother of God (Theotokos — Dogma 1)\n   416→2. It is maximally fitting that the Mother of God be free from all sin (fittingness)\n   417→3. God can apply Christ's merits retroactively (retroactive redemption)\n   418→4. The Pope has defined this ex cathedra (papal infallibility)\n   419→5. Therefore: Mary was preserved from original sin\n   420→\n   421→Source: Pius IX, Ineffabilis Deus (1854); CCC §491-492.\n   422→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC ONLY.\n   423→- Orthodox: reject the Western framing of original sin\n   424→- Protestants: reject premises 2 (fittingness), 3 (retroactive redemption),\n   425→  and 4 (papal infallibility)\n   426→\n   427→HONESTY NOTE on scriptural basis (CONTESTED):\n   428→- Lk 1:28 (kecharitomene / \"full of grace\"): Catholics read this as implying\n   429→  a permanent, complete state of grace from conception. Protestants read it\n   430→  as a present description. The Greek participle is debated.\n   431→- Gen 3:15 (protoevangelium): typological reading, not direct statement.\n   432→- This has the THINNEST scriptural basis of the major Marian dogmas. The\n   433→  definition relies primarily on Tradition, fittingness reasoning, and\n   434→  papal authority.\n   435→\n   436→NOTE ON FORMALIZATION: An initial proof attempt tried to derive the\n   437→incompatibility of \"preserved from original sin\" and \"has original sin\" from\n   438→existing axioms. It failed — revealing that we need an explicit axiom\n   439→(PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN) connecting the two as contradictories. This is\n   440→semantically obvious (\"preserved from X\" means \"does not have X\") but must\n   441→be stated in a formal system. The proof assistant forced this hidden\n   442→assumption to the surface.\n   443→-/\n   444→\n   445→/-- **AXIOM: PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN** — Being preserved from original sin\n   446→    and having original sin are contradictory.\n   447→    This is an analytic truth from the meaning of \"preserved from.\"\n   448→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL (definitional). -/\n   449→axiom PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN :\n   450→  ∀ (p : Person), preservedFromOriginalSin p → ¬hasOriginalSin p\n   451→\n   452→/-- **THEOREM: immaculate_conception** (proper version) — Mary was preserved\n   453→    from original sin and therefore does not have original sin.\n   454→\n   455→    Given that Mary was preserved (the doctrinal claim supported by\n   456→    fittingness, retroactive redemption, and papal definition), the\n   457→    consequence follows by the semantics of preservation.\n   458→\n   459→    The REAL work of this dogma is not in the theorem but in the AXIOMS\n   460→    needed to establish the premise (preservedFromOriginalSin mary).\n   461→    The axiom count tells the story:\n   462→    - HYPOSTATIC_UNION (ecumenical)\n   463→    - MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS (ecumenical)\n   464→    - ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED (broadly ecumenical)\n   465→    - RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION (Catholic only)\n   466→    - FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE (Catholic only)\n   467→    - PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY (Catholic only)\n   468→    Three Catholic-only axioms are needed. This is why Protestants reject it. -/\n   469→theorem immaculate_conception_proper\n   470→    (h_preserved : preservedFromOriginalSin mary) :\n   471→    ¬hasOriginalSin mary :=\n   472→  PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN mary h_preserved\n   473→\n   474→def immaculate_conception_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   475→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic]\n   476→    note := \"Catholic only; Orthodox reject Western framing; Protestants reject entirely\" }\n   477→\n   478→/-- Mary never committed personal sin either.\n   479→    Source: CCC §493; Council of Trent, Session 6, Canon 23.\n   480→    This is a STRONGER claim than the Immaculate Conception (which is about\n   481→    original sin only). The Catechism holds Mary was free from ALL sin. -/\n   482→axiom MARY_SINLESS :\n   483→  ¬committedPersonalSin mary\n   484→\n   485→def mary_sinless_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.tradition \"Council of Trent Session 6 Canon 23; CCC §493\"\n   486→def mary_sinless_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   487→\n   488→-- ============================================================================\n   489→-- DOGMA 3: THE ASSUMPTION (Pius XII, Munificentissimus Deus, 1950)\n   490→-- ============================================================================\n   491→\n   492→/-!\n   493→## Dogma 3: The Assumption of Mary\n   494→\n   495→The longest dependency chain — each dogma builds on the previous.\n   496→\n   497→The definition (Munificentissimus Deus, 1950) literally begins:\n   498→\"The Immaculate Virgin, preserved free from all stain of original sin...\"\n   499→The Assumption EXPLICITLY DEPENDS on the Immaculate Conception.\n   500→\n   501→### The argument chain:\n   502→1. Mary was sinless (Immaculate Conception + personal sinlessness)\n   503→2. Death and bodily corruption are consequences of sin (Rom 5:12, Gen 3:19)\n   504→3. A sinless person's body is not subject to the corruption caused by sin\n   505→4. Mary's body was not subject to corruption\n   506→5. Mary was assumed body and soul into heaven\n   507→\n   508→### The hylomorphism (P1) connection:\n   509→Why does the dogma insist on BODILY assumption? Why not just say Mary's\n   510→soul went to heaven (which no one would dispute)?\n   511→\n   512→Because of P1: the person IS the composite of soul and body. Under\n   513→hylomorphism, the soul without the body is an INCOMPLETE person. If Mary\n   514→is fully glorified, she must be glorified AS A COMPLETE PERSON — body and\n   515→soul. Without hylomorphism, you could just say her soul is in heaven and\n   516→the body doesn't matter.\n   517→\n   518→### The DivineModes connection:\n   519→Mary enters the heavenState from DivineModes.lean: full beatifying communion,\n   520→body and soul. She is sustained by God AND in full communion — the complete\n   521→realization of what heaven means.\n   522→\n   523→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC (defined 1950).\n   524→- Orthodox accept the \"Dormition\" (falling asleep) of Mary and her bodily\n   525→  presence in heaven, but with different theological framing and without\n   526→  the ex cathedra definition.\n   527→- Protestants reject it entirely (no scriptural basis).\n   528→-/\n   529→\n   530→/-- **AXIOM: DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN** — Death and bodily corruption\n   531→    entered the world through sin. Without sin, there would be no death.\n   532→    Source: Rom 5:12 (\"sin came into the world through one man, and death\n   533→    through sin\"); Gen 3:19 (\"you are dust, and to dust you shall return\");\n   534→    CCC §1008 (\"Death is a consequence of sin\").\n   535→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL (broadly) — most Christians accept this\n   536→    in some form, though interpretations vary (physical death vs. spiritual\n   537→    death, universal vs. representative). -/\n   538→axiom DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN :\n   539→  ∀ (p : Person),\n   540→    (hasOriginalSin p ∨ committedPersonalSin p) →\n   541→    bodySubjectToCorruption p\n   542→\n   543→def death_consequence_sin_provenance : Provenance := Provenance.scripture \"Rom 5:12; Gen 3:19; CCC §1008\"\n   544→def death_consequence_sin_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   545→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.ecumenical], note := \"broadly shared; interpretations vary\" }\n   546→\n   547→/-- **AXIOM: SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY** — If a person never\n   548→    sinned (neither original nor personal sin), their body is not subject\n   549→    to the corruption that results from sin.\n   550→    Source: Theological reasoning from DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN\n   551→    (the contrapositive: no sin → no corruption-from-sin);\n   552→    CCC §966, §974.\n   553→    HIDDEN ASSUMPTION: This is the contrapositive of DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN,\n   554→    but stated as a separate axiom because the reasoning involves an\n   555→    additional step: not just \"no sin → no death\" but \"no sin → bodily\n   556→    integrity preserved for assumption into glory.\"\n   557→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC — the inference from sinlessness to bodily\n   558→    integrity is accepted primarily in Catholic theology. -/\n   559→axiom SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY :\n   560→  ∀ (p : Person),\n   561→    ¬hasOriginalSin p →\n   562→    ¬committedPersonalSin p →\n   563→    ¬bodySubjectToCorruption p\n   564→\n   565→def sinlessness_integrity_provenance : Provenance :=\n   566→  Provenance.tradition \"theological reasoning; CCC §966, §974\"\n   567→def sinlessness_integrity_tag : DenominationalTag := catholicOnly\n   568→\n   569→/-- **THEOREM: assumption_follows_from_ic** — The Assumption follows from\n   570→    the Immaculate Conception through a chain of reasoning.\n   571→\n   572→    The chain:\n   573→    1. Immaculate Conception: Mary was preserved from original sin\n   574→    2. Personal sinlessness: Mary never committed personal sin (Trent)\n   575→    3. Sinlessness implies bodily integrity: no sin → body not subject to corruption\n   576→    4. Mary's body was not subject to corruption\n   577→    5. Therefore: Mary was assumed body and soul into glory\n   578→\n   579→    The BODILY dimension comes from P1 (hylomorphism):\n   580→    - Under P1, the person IS the body-soul composite (Soul.lean)\n   581→    - A soul without its body is an INCOMPLETE substance\n   582→    - Full glorification requires the COMPLETE person: body AND soul\n   583→    - Therefore the Assumption must be BODILY, not just spiritual\n   584→\n   585→    Source: Pius XII, Munificentissimus Deus (1950); CCC §966, §974.\n   586→\n   587→    DEPENDENCY: This theorem requires EVERYTHING from Dogmas 1 and 2,\n   588→    plus P1 (hylomorphism) and SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY.\n   589→    It is the terminus of the longest dependency chain in Mariology. -/\n   590→theorem assumption_follows_from_ic\n   591→    (_h_no_original : ¬hasOriginalSin mary)\n   592→    (_h_no_personal : ¬committedPersonalSin mary)\n   593→    (h_bodily_integrity : ¬bodySubjectToCorruption mary)\n   594→    (_h_hylomorphism : ∀ (p : HylomorphicPerson), p.soulIsForm → p.composition.isUnified)\n   595→    (h_assumed : bodilyAssumed mary) :\n   596→    -- Mary was assumed body and soul, AND her body was not subject to corruption\n   597→    bodilyAssumed mary ∧ ¬bodySubjectToCorruption mary :=\n   598→  ⟨h_assumed, h_bodily_integrity⟩\n   599→\n   600→/-- **THEOREM: sinlessness_to_integrity** — The derivation from sinlessness\n   601→    to bodily integrity, which is the key intermediate step. -/\n   602→theorem sinlessness_to_integrity\n   603→    (h_preserved : preservedFromOriginalSin mary)\n   604→    (h_no_personal : ¬committedPersonalSin mary) :\n   605→    ¬bodySubjectToCorruption mary :=\n   606→  SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY mary\n   607→    (PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN mary h_preserved)\n   608→    h_no_personal\n   609→\n   610→/-- The Assumption connects to DivineModes: Mary enters the heavenState\n   611→    (full beatifying communion, body and soul).\n   612→    The heavenState from DivineModes.lean has:\n   613→    - sustained = True (God sustains her in existence)\n   614→    - inCommunion = True (full beatifying communion)\n   615→    - purified = True (fully purified — indeed, never needed purification) -/\n   616→theorem assumption_is_full_communion :\n   617→    heavenState.sustained ∧ heavenState.inCommunion ∧ heavenState.purified := by\n   618→  exact ⟨trivial, trivial, trivial⟩\n   619→\n   620→def assumption_tag : DenominationalTag :=\n   621→  { acceptedBy := [Denomination.catholic]\n   622→    note := \"Catholic (defined 1950); Orthodox accept 'Dormition' with different framing; Protestants reject\" }\n   623→\n   624→-- ============================================================================\n   625→-- THE DEPENDENCY CHAIN — made explicit\n   626→-- ============================================================================\n   627→\n   628→/-!\n   629→## The dependency chain\n   630→\n   631→Each later dogma requires every earlier one. The axiom count grows at each step,\n   632→and the denominational scope narrows correspondingly.\n   633→\n   634→```\n   635→STEP 1: Theotokos (2 axioms — ecumenical)\n   636→  Axioms: HYPOSTATIC_UNION, MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS\n   637→  + Given: MARY_BORE_CHRIST (Scripture)\n   638→  Scope: Nearly ecumenical (Luther & Calvin accepted)\n   639→\n   640→STEP 2: Immaculate Conception (6 axioms — Catholic only)\n   641→  Inherits: everything from Step 1\n   642→  Adds: ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED, RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION,\n   643→        FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE, PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY\n   644→  Scope: Catholic only\n   645→\n   646→STEP 3: Assumption (8+ axioms — Catholic only)\n   647→  Inherits: everything from Steps 1 and 2\n   648→  Adds: SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY,\n   649→        DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN, P1 (hylomorphism)\n   650→  Scope: Catholic only\n   651→```\n   652→\n   653→The pattern: more axioms → narrower scope → fewer traditions agree.\n   654→This is the axiom-set-as-denomination principle applied to Mariology.\n   655→-/\n   656→\n   657→/-- **THEOREM: theotokos_required_for_ic** — The Immaculate Conception\n   658→    presupposes Theotokos. The definition begins with Mary as Mother of God;\n   659→    without that, the fittingness argument (\"it is fitting that the MOTHER\n   660→    OF GOD be sinless\") has no force.\n   661→\n   662→    If Mary is just an ordinary woman who happened to bear a human prophet,\n   663→    there is no special reason she should be preserved from original sin.\n   664→    The fittingness argument REQUIRES her to be the Mother of God. -/\n   665→theorem theotokos_required_for_ic\n   666→    (h_theotokos : bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine)\n   667→    (h_preserved : preservedFromOriginalSin mary) :\n   668→    -- Both Theotokos AND Immaculate Conception hold together\n   669→    (bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine) ∧ preservedFromOriginalSin mary :=\n   670→  ⟨h_theotokos, h_preserved⟩\n   671→\n   672→/-- **THEOREM: ic_required_for_assumption** — The Assumption presupposes\n   673→    the Immaculate Conception. The definition (Munificentissimus Deus)\n   674→    literally begins \"The Immaculate Virgin...\"\n   675→\n   676→    The logical chain: IC (Mary sinless) → sinlessness implies bodily\n   677→    integrity → body not subject to corruption → bodily assumption.\n   678→    Without IC, the chain breaks at the first link. -/\n   679→theorem ic_required_for_assumption\n   680→    (h_preserved : preservedFromOriginalSin mary)\n   681→    (h_no_personal : ¬committedPersonalSin mary)\n   682→    (h_assumed : bodilyAssumed mary) :\n   683→    -- IC + sinlessness + bodily integrity + assumption all hold\n   684→    preservedFromOriginalSin mary ∧ ¬committedPersonalSin mary ∧\n   685→    ¬bodySubjectToCorruption mary ∧ bodilyAssumed mary :=\n   686→  ⟨h_preserved, h_no_personal,\n   687→   SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY mary\n   688→     (PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN mary h_preserved) h_no_personal,\n   689→   h_assumed⟩\n   690→\n   691→/-- **THEOREM: full_marian_chain** — The complete dependency chain:\n   692→    Hypostatic Union → Theotokos → Immaculate Conception → Assumption.\n   693→\n   694→    This makes the chain explicit: all four propositions hold together,\n   695→    and each depends on the previous. Rejecting any link breaks the\n   696→    chain downstream. -/\n   697→theorem full_marian_chain\n   698→    (h_union : christ.isDivine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.divine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.human)\n   699→    (h_bore : bore mary christ)\n   700→    (h_preserved : preservedFromOriginalSin mary)\n   701→    (h_no_personal : ¬committedPersonalSin mary)\n   702→    (h_assumed : bodilyAssumed mary) :\n   703→    -- The full chain holds:\n   704→    -- 1. Hypostatic union\n   705→    (christ.isDivine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.divine ∧ christ.hasNature Nature.human) ∧\n   706→    -- 2. Theotokos\n   707→    (bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine) ∧\n   708→    -- 3. Immaculate Conception\n   709→    (preservedFromOriginalSin mary ∧ ¬hasOriginalSin mary) ∧\n   710→    -- 4. Assumption (with bodily integrity)\n   711→    (bodilyAssumed mary ∧ ¬bodySubjectToCorruption mary) :=\n   712→  ⟨ h_union\n   713→  , ⟨h_bore, h_union.1⟩\n   714→  , ⟨h_preserved, PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN mary h_preserved⟩\n   715→  , ⟨h_assumed, SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY mary\n   716→      (PRESERVATION_EXCLUDES_SIN mary h_preserved) h_no_personal⟩\n   717→  ⟩\n   718→\n   719→/-- **THEOREM: chain_breaks_without_union** — Without the hypostatic union,\n   720→    Theotokos has no force, and the downstream dogmas lose their foundation.\n   721→\n   722→    If Christ is not divine, then \"Mother of God\" is meaningless, the\n   723→    fittingness argument for IC fails, and the Assumption loses its\n   724→    theological motivation. -/\n   725→theorem chain_breaks_without_union\n   726→    (h_not_divine : ¬christ.isDivine) :\n   727→    -- Cannot conclude Theotokos (Mary as Mother of GOD)\n   728→    ¬(bore mary christ ∧ christ.isDivine) := by\n   729→  intro ⟨_, h_divine⟩\n   730→  exact h_not_divine h_divine\n   731→\n   732→-- ============================================================================\n   733→-- DENOMINATIONAL SUMMARY\n   734→-- ============================================================================\n   735→\n   736→/-- Denominational scope of each Marian axiom and theorem.\n   737→    The pattern is clear: more axioms → narrower acceptance. -/\n   738→def marianDenominationalScope : List (String × DenominationalTag) :=\n   739→  [ -- Dogma 1: Theotokos (nearly ecumenical)\n   740→    (\"HYPOSTATIC_UNION\",              hypostatic_union_tag)\n   741→  , (\"MOTHERHOOD_TARGETS_PERSONS\",    motherhood_targets_persons_tag)\n   742→  , (\"MARY_BORE_CHRIST\",             mary_bore_christ_tag)\n   743→  , (\"theotokos (theorem)\",          theotokos_tag)\n   744→    -- Dogma 2: Immaculate Conception (Catholic only)\n   745→  , (\"ORIGINAL_SIN_INHERITED\",       original_sin_inherited_tag)\n   746→  , (\"RETROACTIVE_REDEMPTION\",       retroactive_redemption_tag)\n   747→  , (\"FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE\",      fittingness_tag)\n   748→  , (\"PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY\",          papal_infallibility_tag)\n   749→  , (\"immaculate_conception (thm)\",  immaculate_conception_tag)\n   750→    -- Dogma 3: Assumption (Catholic only)\n   751→  , (\"DEATH_IS_CONSEQUENCE_OF_SIN\",  death_consequence_sin_tag)\n   752→  , (\"SINLESSNESS_IMPLIES_BODILY_INTEGRITY\", sinlessness_integrity_tag)\n   753→  , (\"assumption (theorem)\",         assumption_tag)\n   754→  ]\n   755→\n   756→/-!\n   757→## Hidden assumptions — summary\n   758→\n   759→1. **Motherhood targets persons, not natures** (Dogma 1): Nestorius denied\n   760→   this implicitly. Once stated, it seems obvious — but it is the load-bearing\n   761→   premise of Theotokos.\n   762→\n   763→2. **Retroactive redemption** (Dogma 2): Christ's merits can be applied\n   764→   backwards in time. This is a genuinely novel metaphysical commitment with\n   765→   no clear parallel elsewhere in the system. It is the most philosophically\n   766→   adventurous claim in the entire Marian corpus.\n   767→\n   768→3. **Fittingness as evidence** (Dogma 2): \"It would be fitting, therefore\n   769→   God did it.\" This epistemological principle (potuit, decuit, fecit) is\n   770→   distinctively Scholastic. Protestants reject this entire pattern of\n   771→   reasoning.\n   772→\n   773→4. **Hylomorphism grounds bodily assumption** (Dogma 3): Without P1 (the\n   774→   person IS the body-soul composite), there is no reason to insist on\n   775→   BODILY assumption. You could just say Mary's soul went to heaven. The\n   776→   Assumption is the most visible downstream consequence of P1.\n   777→\n   778→5. **Thin scriptural basis for IC** (Dogma 2): Lk 1:28 (kecharitomene) is\n   779→   the primary text, and its interpretation is genuinely contested. Gen 3:15\n   780→   is typological. The Immaculate Conception relies more on Tradition and\n   781→   theological reasoning than on direct scriptural statement. This is honest\n   782→   and should be acknowledged.\n   783→\n   784→6. **Papal infallibility as load-bearing axiom** (Dogmas 2 & 3): Both the\n   785→   IC (1854) and the Assumption (1950) are ex cathedra definitions. Without\n   786→   PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY, neither can be defined as irreformable dogma. This\n   787→   axiom does more work in Mariology than anywhere else in the system.\n   788→-/\n   789→\n   790→end Catlib.Creed\n   791→"}]},"uuid":"c3b672d9-9ec4-4fe3-b09b-4598316d838d","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:40:36.642Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"dab8e63c-5948-419f-8012-d5e47c072d75","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}

{"parentUuid":"d39bec78-bdc2-48f5-84e9-b7bcb58f067b","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"90bfc06d-2f27-4c98-843f-d48b7935dcd3","agentId":"a507233507e5567eb","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_018UcyQ5gf16upwu1SnVf1Ey","type":"tool_result","content":"   200→    transcendence). -/\n   201→structure Absolution where\n   202→  /-- The priest granting absolution -/\n   203→  priest : Person\n   204→  /-- The penitent receiving absolution -/\n   205→  penitent : Person\n   206→  /-- The priest has valid authority to absolve\n   207→      Cross-ref: absolutionDomain.christDelegatedIt (Authority.lean) -/\n   208→  hasAuthority : Prop\n   209→  /-- The absolution is pronounced -/\n   210→  isPronounced : Prop\n   211→\n   212→/-- The complete sacramental act of Reconciliation, comprising all four\n   213→    components: contrition (penitent), confession (penitent), absolution\n   214→    (priest), and satisfaction (penitent).\n   215→\n   216→    CCC §1491: \"The sacrament of Penance is a whole consisting in three\n   217→    actions of the penitent and the priest's absolution.\"\n   218→\n   219→    STRUCTURAL NOTE: This is where the ASYMMETRY becomes visible.\n   220→    Mortal sin is ONE act (a single sinful choice). Reconciliation\n   221→    requires FOUR components (contrition + confession + absolution +\n   222→    satisfaction) plus prevenient grace. Destruction is cheaper than\n   223→    restoration. -/\n   224→structure ReconciliationAct where\n   225→  /-- Genuine contrition for the sin -/\n   226→  contrition : Contrition\n   227→  /-- Confession of the sin to a priest -/\n   228→  confession : Confession\n   229→  /-- Priestly absolution -/\n   230→  absolution : Absolution\n   231→  /-- Satisfaction (penance) -/\n   232→  satisfaction : Satisfaction\n   233→  /-- The penitent is consistent across all components -/\n   234→  penitentConsistent : contrition.penitent = confession.penitent\n   235→    ∧ confession.penitent = absolution.penitent\n   236→    ∧ absolution.penitent = satisfaction.penitent\n   237→  /-- The priest is consistent between confession and absolution -/\n   238→  priestConsistent : confession.priest = absolution.priest\n   239→\n   240→-- ============================================================================\n   241→-- § 2. Temporal Punishment — the residual effect of sin after absolution\n   242→-- ============================================================================\n   243→\n   244→/-!\n   245→### Temporal vs. Eternal Punishment\n   246→\n   247→CCC §1472-1473: \"Grave sin deprives us of communion with God and therefore\n   248→makes us incapable of eternal life, the privation of which is called the\n   249→'eternal punishment' of sin. On the other hand every sin, even venial,\n   250→entails an unhealthy attachment to creatures, which must be purified either\n   251→here on earth, or after death in the state called Purgatory. This\n   252→purification frees one from what is called the 'temporal punishment' of sin.\"\n   253→\n   254→The distinction:\n   255→- **Eternal punishment** = loss of communion with God (guilt). Absolution removes this.\n   256→- **Temporal punishment** = disordered attachments / damage caused by sin. Absolution\n   257→  does NOT fully remove this.\n   258→\n   259→This distinction is the load-bearing joint between Reconciliation and Purgatory.\n   260→It is also the precise point Luther contested via indulgences.\n   261→\n   262→Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — purgatory IS the post-mortem resolution of\n   263→temporal punishment for those who die in grace.\n   264→\n   265→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC. Protestants deny the temporal/eternal\n   266→punishment distinction. Under Protestant axioms, Christ's atonement\n   267→removes ALL punishment — there is no residual temporal effect.\n   268→-/\n   269→\n   270→/-- Whether a person carries temporal punishment from past sins.\n   271→    Temporal punishment represents the residual disorder and damage\n   272→    caused by sin — even after the guilt (eternal punishment) is removed.\n   273→\n   274→    Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — this is what purgatory addresses\n   275→    post-mortem. Satisfaction addresses it pre-mortem. -/\n   276→opaque hasTemporalPunishment : Person → Prop\n   277→\n   278→/-- Whether a person's eternal punishment (guilt) has been removed. -/\n   279→opaque eternalPunishmentRemitted : Person → Prop\n   280→\n   281→-- ============================================================================\n   282→-- § 3. Axioms\n   283→-- ============================================================================\n   284→\n   285→/-!\n   286→### Axiom group 1: The conditions for valid reconciliation\n   287→-/\n   288→\n   289→/-- AXIOM (§1451): Contrition requires genuine sorrow and firm purpose.\n   290→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1451.\n   291→    Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — all Christians agree repentance\n   292→    must be sincere. -/\n   293→axiom contrition_requires_sincerity :\n   294→  ∀ (c : Contrition), c.genuineSorrow ∧ c.firmPurpose → c.isFree\n   295→\n   296→/-- AXIOM (§1456): Valid confession requires completeness for mortal sins.\n   297→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1456.\n   298→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX. -/\n   299→axiom confession_requires_completeness :\n   300→  ∀ (conf : Confession) (sa : SinfulAct),\n   301→    sa.isMortal →\n   302→    conf.isComplete →\n   303→    True -- The completeness condition is met\n   304→\n   305→/-- AXIOM (§1461, Jn 20:23): Valid absolution requires the delegation chain.\n   306→    Provenance: [Scripture] Jn 20:23; [Tradition] CCC §1461.\n   307→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX.\n   308→\n   309→    Cross-ref: absolution_authority (Authority.lean) — this axiom\n   310→    connects to the specific delegation chain for absolution:\n   311→    Christ → Apostles (Jn 20:23) → bishops → priests.\n   312→\n   313→    Cross-ref: christ_delegates_absolution (Authority.lean) —\n   314→    the delegation is specifically cited with chapter and verse.\n   315→\n   316→    The priest acts in persona Christi — as instrumental cause, not\n   317→    principal cause (P2 two-tier causation, Axioms.lean). -/\n   318→axiom absolution_requires_authority :\n   319→  ∀ (a : Absolution), a.isPronounced → a.hasAuthority\n   320→\n   321→/-!\n   322→### Axiom group 2: The effects of reconciliation\n   323→-/\n   324→\n   325→/-- AXIOM (§1468): Valid reconciliation restores the state of grace.\n   326→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1468.\n   327→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX.\n   328→\n   329→    Cross-ref: mortal_sin_causes_loss_of_grace (Sin.lean) — mortal sin\n   330→    REMOVES grace; reconciliation RESTORES it. These are inverse operations,\n   331→    but the inverse is much harder (asymmetric).\n   332→\n   333→    Cross-ref: GraceState (Sin.lean) — the state transitions from\n   334→    notInGrace back to inGrace. -/\n   335→axiom reconciliation_restores_grace :\n   336→  ∀ (r : ReconciliationAct) (state : SpiritualState),\n   337→    r.contrition.genuineSorrow →\n   338→    r.contrition.firmPurpose →\n   339→    r.contrition.isFree →\n   340→    r.confession.isComplete →\n   341→    r.absolution.hasAuthority →\n   342→    r.absolution.isPronounced →\n   343→    r.satisfaction.penancePerformed →\n   344→    state.person = r.contrition.penitent →\n   345→    state.graceState = GraceState.notInGrace →\n   346→    ∃ (newState : SpiritualState),\n   347→      newState.person = state.person ∧\n   348→      newState.graceState = GraceState.inGrace\n   349→\n   350→/-- AXIOM (§1468): Reconciliation restores charity (agape).\n   351→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1468 (\"restoring us to God's grace\n   352→    and joining us with him in an intimate friendship\").\n   353→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX.\n   354→\n   355→    Cross-ref: mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity (Love.lean) — mortal sin\n   356→    reduces agape to degree 0. Reconciliation raises it above 0.\n   357→\n   358→    Cross-ref: LoveKind.agape (Love.lean) — the supernatural love\n   359→    that was destroyed by mortal sin is specifically restored. -/\n   360→axiom reconciliation_restores_agape :\n   361→  ∀ (r : ReconciliationAct) (tl : TypedLove),\n   362→    r.contrition.genuineSorrow →\n   363→    r.contrition.firmPurpose →\n   364→    r.absolution.hasAuthority →\n   365→    r.absolution.isPronounced →\n   366→    tl.kind = LoveKind.agape →\n   367→    tl.lover = r.contrition.penitent →\n   368→    tl.degree = 0 →\n   369→    ∃ (tl' : TypedLove),\n   370→      tl'.kind = LoveKind.agape ∧\n   371→      tl'.lover = tl.lover ∧\n   372→      tl'.beloved = tl.beloved ∧\n   373→      tl'.degree > 0\n   374→\n   375→/-- AXIOM (§1473): Eternal punishment is remitted by absolution, but\n   376→    temporal punishment may remain.\n   377→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1472-1473.\n   378→    Denominational scope: CATHOLIC.\n   379→\n   380→    This is the theorem that makes indulgences COHERENT under Catholic\n   381→    axioms. Under Protestant axioms (no temporal/eternal distinction),\n   382→    this axiom is rejected, and indulgences become incoherent.\n   383→\n   384→    Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — temporal punishment that remains at\n   385→    death is what purgatory addresses. Satisfaction (penance) addresses\n   386→    it before death. -/\n   387→axiom absolution_remits_eternal_not_temporal :\n   388→  ∀ (r : ReconciliationAct),\n   389→    r.contrition.genuineSorrow →\n   390→    r.absolution.hasAuthority →\n   391→    r.absolution.isPronounced →\n   392→    -- Eternal punishment (guilt) IS removed\n   393→    eternalPunishmentRemitted r.contrition.penitent ∧\n   394→    -- Temporal punishment MAY remain\n   395→    -- (satisfaction/penance partially addresses it, but may not fully resolve it)\n   396→    True  -- temporal punishment's persistence is possible, not guaranteed\n   397→\n   398→/-!\n   399→### Axiom group 3: The grace bootstrapping recurrence\n   400→\n   401→CCC §1489: \"To come back to communion with God after having lost it through\n   402→sin is a process born of the grace of God.\"\n   403→\n   404→**THIS IS THE SAME BOOTSTRAPPING PROBLEM AS §2001 (Grace.lean).**\n   405→\n   406→The recurrence:\n   407→1. Contrition requires HOPE (you must believe reconciliation is possible)\n   408→2. Hope is a theological virtue requiring GRACE\n   409→3. But you are in mortal sin — grace destroyed, charity at zero\n   410→4. So you need grace to get the grace that enables contrition\n   411→5. Resolution: PREVENIENT GRACE (GraceType.prevenient from Grace.lean)\n   412→   enables the initial movement toward contrition\n   413→6. God initiates the return, just as God initiates the first coming to faith\n   414→\n   415→Cross-ref: prevenient_grace_unconditioned (Grace.lean) — the same axiom\n   416→that breaks the §2001 circle also breaks the reconciliation circle.\n   417→\n   418→Cross-ref: divine_initiative_preserves_freedom (Grace.lean) — the\n   419→prevenient grace that enables contrition does NOT coerce the penitent.\n   420→The sinner remains free to reject the movement toward repentance.\n   421→\n   422→Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL in substance — even Protestants agree\n   423→that God initiates repentance (Eph 2:8-9, \"by grace you have been saved\n   424→through faith, and this is not your own doing\"). The specific mechanism\n   425→(prevenient grace as a typed grace distinct from sanctifying grace) is\n   426→Catholic, but the principle (God starts the process) is shared.\n   427→-/\n   428→\n   429→/-- AXIOM (§1489): Contrition requires prevenient grace.\n   430→    A person in mortal sin cannot generate contrition from their own\n   431→    resources — they need God's prior initiative.\n   432→    Provenance: [Definition] CCC §1489; [Tradition] Council of Orange.\n   433→\n   434→    Cross-ref: prevenient_grace_unconditioned (Grace.lean) — the same\n   435→    axiom that resolves the §2001 bootstrapping problem.\n   436→\n   437→    Cross-ref: GraceType.prevenient (Grace.lean) — the type of grace\n   438→    that precedes any human response. -/\n   439→axiom contrition_requires_prevenient_grace :\n   440→  ∀ (c : Contrition),\n   441→    c.genuineSorrow →\n   442→    c.firmPurpose →\n   443→    ∃ (g : TypedGrace),\n   444→      g.graceType = GraceType.prevenient ∧\n   445→      g.recipient = c.penitent ∧\n   446→      g.freelyGiven\n   447→\n   448→-- ============================================================================\n   449→-- § 4. Key Theorems\n   450→-- ============================================================================\n   451→\n   452→/-!\n   453→### Theorem 1: Reconciliation restores charity\n   454→\n   455→If all conditions of a valid reconciliation are met, agape (which mortal\n   456→sin destroyed) is restored to a degree greater than zero.\n   457→\n   458→Cross-ref: mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity (Love.lean) — the destruction.\n   459→Cross-ref: reconciliation_restores_agape — the restoration axiom.\n   460→\n   461→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX.\n   462→-/\n   463→\n   464→/-- Reconciliation restores charity (agape) from zero to positive.\n   465→    This is the inverse of mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity (Love.lean).\n   466→\n   467→    The derivation chain:\n   468→    1. Mortal sin destroyed charity (Love.lean: mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity)\n   469→    2. Penitent has genuine contrition, makes complete confession\n   470→    3. Priest has authority and pronounces absolution (Authority.lean chain)\n   471→    4. Penance is performed\n   472→    5. Therefore agape is restored (degree > 0)\n   473→\n   474→    STRUCTURAL NOTE: Step 1 is ONE act. Steps 2-4 are THREE acts plus\n   475→    the priest's act. The asymmetry is inherent: destruction is one act,\n   476→    restoration is four. -/\n   477→theorem reconciliation_restores_charity\n   478→    (r : ReconciliationAct) (tl : TypedLove)\n   479→    (h_sorrow : r.contrition.genuineSorrow)\n   480→    (h_purpose : r.contrition.firmPurpose)\n   481→    (h_auth : r.absolution.hasAuthority)\n   482→    (h_pronounced : r.absolution.isPronounced)\n   483→    (h_agape : tl.kind = LoveKind.agape)\n   484→    (h_lover : tl.lover = r.contrition.penitent)\n   485→    (h_destroyed : tl.degree = 0) :\n   486→    ∃ (tl' : TypedLove),\n   487→      tl'.kind = LoveKind.agape ∧\n   488→      tl'.lover = tl.lover ∧\n   489→      tl'.beloved = tl.beloved ∧\n   490→      tl'.degree > 0 :=\n   491→  reconciliation_restores_agape r tl h_sorrow h_purpose h_auth h_pronounced\n   492→    h_agape h_lover h_destroyed\n   493→\n   494→/-!\n   495→### Theorem 2: Reconciliation restores communion with God\n   496→\n   497→Charity restored → beatifying mode restored. If agape is above zero,\n   498→the person is in the state of communion described by DivineModes.lean.\n   499→\n   500→Cross-ref: SoulState (DivineModes.lean) — the beatifying mode.\n   501→Cross-ref: heavenState (DivineModes.lean) — full communion.\n   502→Cross-ref: mortal_sin_can_destroy_charity (Love.lean) — what broke communion.\n   503→\n   504→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX.\n   505→-/\n   506→\n   507→/-- Restoring charity implies restoring the beatifying mode of divine\n   508→    relation. When agape is above zero, the person is in communion.\n   509→\n   510→    The connection to DivineModes.lean:\n   511→    - hellState: sustained = True, inCommunion = False (no agape toward God)\n   512→    - heavenState: sustained = True, inCommunion = True (full agape)\n   513→    - Reconciliation moves the soul from hellState-like (no communion)\n   514→      to a state where communion is restored.\n   515→\n   516→    This theorem connects Love.lean (agape > 0) to DivineModes.lean\n   517→    (inCommunion = True). -/\n   518→axiom charity_implies_communion :\n   519→  ∀ (p : Person) (tl : TypedLove),\n   520→    tl.kind = LoveKind.agape →\n   521→    tl.lover = p →\n   522→    tl.degree > 0 →\n   523→    ∃ (s : SoulState), s.sustained ∧ s.inCommunion\n   524→\n   525→theorem reconciliation_restores_communion\n   526→    (r : ReconciliationAct) (tl : TypedLove)\n   527→    (h_sorrow : r.contrition.genuineSorrow)\n   528→    (h_purpose : r.contrition.firmPurpose)\n   529→    (h_auth : r.absolution.hasAuthority)\n   530→    (h_pronounced : r.absolution.isPronounced)\n   531→    (h_agape : tl.kind = LoveKind.agape)\n   532→    (h_lover : tl.lover = r.contrition.penitent)\n   533→    (h_destroyed : tl.degree = 0) :\n   534→    ∃ (s : SoulState), s.sustained ∧ s.inCommunion := by\n   535→  -- Step 1: reconciliation restores agape to degree > 0\n   536→  obtain ⟨tl', h_kind', h_lover', _, h_deg'⟩ :=\n   537→    reconciliation_restores_charity r tl h_sorrow h_purpose h_auth\n   538→      h_pronounced h_agape h_lover h_destroyed\n   539→  -- Step 2: agape > 0 implies communion (charity_implies_communion)\n   540→  exact charity_implies_communion r.contrition.penitent tl' h_kind'\n   541→    (h_lover' ▸ h_lover ▸ rfl) h_deg'\n   542→\n   543→/-!\n   544→### Theorem 3: Grace bootstrapping in reconciliation\n   545→\n   546→The same pattern as Grace.lean's grace_bootstrapping_resolved:\n   547→prevenient grace is unconditionally available and enables the\n   548→contrition that starts the reconciliation process.\n   549→\n   550→Cross-ref: grace_bootstrapping_resolved (Grace.lean) — the same\n   551→structural pattern appearing in a different context.\n   552→\n   553→Cross-ref: prevenient_grace_unconditioned (Grace.lean) — the axiom\n   554→that breaks the circle.\n   555→\n   556→Denominational scope: ECUMENICAL — God initiates repentance.\n   557→-/\n   558→\n   559→/-- The grace bootstrapping problem appears in reconciliation:\n   560→    the sinner needs grace to be contrite, but is in mortal sin\n   561→    (without grace). Prevenient grace breaks the circle.\n   562→\n   563→    Derivation:\n   564→    1. The sinner is in mortal sin → no sanctifying grace\n   565→    2. Contrition requires hope → hope requires grace\n   566→    3. But prevenient grace is unconditioned (Grace.lean)\n   567→    4. Therefore prevenient grace enables contrition\n   568→    5. Contrition (+ confession + absolution + satisfaction) → sanctifying grace restored\n   569→\n   570→    This is structurally identical to the §2001 bootstrapping problem.\n   571→    The SAME axiom (prevenient_grace_unconditioned) resolves BOTH cases.\n   572→    This is not a coincidence — it reflects the Catholic principle that\n   573→    God ALWAYS initiates. -/\n   574→theorem grace_bootstrapping_in_reconciliation\n   575→    (p : Person)\n   576→    (h_free : p.hasFreeWill = true) :\n   577→    ∃ (g : TypedGrace),\n   578→      g.graceType = GraceType.prevenient ∧\n   579→      g.recipient = p ∧\n   580→      g.freelyGiven :=\n   581→  -- Identical to grace_bootstrapping_resolved (Grace.lean)!\n   582→  -- The same axiom resolves both bootstrapping problems.\n   583→  prevenient_grace_unconditioned p h_free\n   584→\n   585→/-!\n   586→### Theorem 4: Temporal punishment survives absolution\n   587→\n   588→Absolution removes guilt (eternal punishment) but temporal punishment\n   589→may remain. This is the foundational claim that makes indulgences\n   590→coherent under Catholic axioms.\n   591→\n   592→Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — temporal punishment that remains at death\n   593→is what purgatory addresses post-mortem.\n   594→\n   595→Cross-ref: The Luther connection — Luther's objection was not to\n   596→confession but to INDULGENCES, which claim to address temporal\n   597→punishment. If temporal punishment does not survive absolution,\n   598→indulgences are incoherent.\n   599→\n   600→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC. Protestants deny the survival of\n   601→temporal punishment after forgiveness.\n   602→-/\n   603→\n   604→/-- Temporal punishment survives absolution. Guilt (eternal punishment)\n   605→    is removed, but the disorder caused by sin remains and must be\n   606→    addressed through penance (satisfaction) or purgatory.\n   607→\n   608→    This theorem is the hinge of the Reformation dispute over indulgences:\n   609→    - Under Catholic axioms: temporal punishment survives → indulgences\n   610→      (which address temporal punishment) are coherent\n   611→    - Under Protestant axioms: no temporal punishment survives →\n   612→      indulgences are incoherent\n   613→\n   614→    Cross-ref: Purgatory.lean — the post-mortem continuation of this\n   615→    temporal punishment is exactly what purgatory addresses. -/\n   616→theorem temporal_punishment_survives_absolution\n   617→    (r : ReconciliationAct)\n   618→    (h_sorrow : r.contrition.genuineSorrow)\n   619→    (h_auth : r.absolution.hasAuthority)\n   620→    (h_pronounced : r.absolution.isPronounced) :\n   621→    -- Eternal punishment is remitted\n   622→    eternalPunishmentRemitted r.contrition.penitent := by\n   623→  have ⟨h_eternal, _⟩ :=\n   624→    absolution_remits_eternal_not_temporal r h_sorrow h_auth h_pronounced\n   625→  exact h_eternal\n   626→\n   627→/-!\n   628→### Theorem 5: Destruction is asymmetric to restoration\n   629→\n   630→Mortal sin = 1 act (a single sinful choice with full knowledge and\n   631→complete consent). Reconciliation = contrition + confession + absolution +\n   632→satisfaction + prevenient grace. The inverse operation is strictly harder.\n   633→\n   634→This is a STRUCTURAL finding: the Catechism's sacramental theology\n   635→embodies the thermodynamic intuition that breaking is easier than fixing.\n   636→\n   637→Cross-ref: SinfulAct.isMortal (Sin.lean) — the single act of destruction.\n   638→Cross-ref: ReconciliationAct — the four-component act of restoration.\n   639→\n   640→Denominational scope: CATHOLIC + ORTHODOX (the specific components).\n   641→The asymmetry principle itself is ecumenical — all Christians agree\n   642→that repentance requires more than just \"undoing\" a sin.\n   643→-/\n   644→\n   645→/-- The asymmetry between destruction and restoration.\n   646→\n   647→    Mortal sin is a single act satisfying three conditions (gravity,\n   648→    knowledge, consent). Reconciliation requires four components\n   649→    (contrition, confession, absolution, satisfaction) plus prevenient\n   650→    grace. The inverse is strictly harder.\n   651→\n   652→    Formalized as: a single SinfulAct can destroy grace, but restoring\n   653→    grace requires a ReconciliationAct (which has four sub-components).\n   654→\n   655→    This theorem proves both directions:\n   656→    (a) A single mortal sin can cause loss of grace\n   657→    (b) Restoration requires all four components of reconciliation -/\n   658→theorem destruction_asymmetric_to_restoration\n   659→    (sa : SinfulAct)\n   660→    (state : SpiritualState)\n   661→    (h_mortal : sa.isMortal)\n   662→    (h_in_grace : state.graceState = GraceState.inGrace) :\n   663→    -- (a) ONE sinful act suffices for destruction\n   664→    (∃ (newState : SpiritualState),\n   665→      newState.person = state.person ∧\n   666→      newState.graceState = GraceState.notInGrace) ∧\n   667→    -- (b) restoration requires a full ReconciliationAct (existentially)\n   668→    (∀ (r : ReconciliationAct) (lostState : SpiritualState),\n   669→      lostState.person = state.person →\n   670→      lostState.graceState = GraceState.notInGrace →\n   671→      r.contrition.genuineSorrow →\n   672→      r.contrition.firmPurpose →\n   673→      r.contrition.isFree →\n   674→      r.confession.isComplete →\n   675→      r.absolution.hasAuthority →\n   676→      r.absolution.isPronounced →\n   677→      r.satisfaction.penancePerformed →\n   678→      lostState.person = r.contrition.penitent →\n   679→      ∃ (restoredState : SpiritualState),\n   680→        restoredState.person = state.person ∧\n   681→        restoredState.graceState = GraceState.inGrace) := by\n   682→  constructor\n   683→  · -- (a) mortal sin causes loss of grace (Sin.lean)\n   684→    exact mortal_sin_causes_loss_of_grace sa state h_mortal h_in_grace\n   685→  · -- (b) reconciliation restores grace (requires all components)\n   686→    intro r lostState h_person h_lost h_sorrow h_purpose h_free h_complete\n   687→      h_auth h_pronounced h_penance h_penitent\n   688→    obtain ⟨restored, h_rp, h_rg⟩ :=\n   689→      reconciliation_restores_grace r lostState h_sorrow h_purpose h_free\n   690→        h_complete h_auth h_pronounced h_penance h_penitent h_lost\n   691→    exact ⟨restored, h_person ▸ h_rp, h_rg⟩\n   692→\n   693→/-!\n   694→### Theorem 6: Reconciliation requires authority\n   695→\n   696→Valid absolution requires the delegation chain from Authority.lean.\n   697→This is the sacramental form of the general principle that spiritual\n   698→authority must be delegated, not self-assumed.\n These are not bugs -- Lean type-checks them -- but they have zero logical content. They could be deleted and nothing in the project would break, because no downstream theorem depends on them asserting anything.\n\nThe second most serious problem is the disconnected axiom systems. The 15 base axioms in Axioms.lean were created as a unification layer, but 9 of 13 formalization files still use their own local axioms. The base axioms are largely dead code -- declared but not used by the files they were meant to ground.\n\n### Top 5 Highest-Priority Fixes\n\n1. **Fix the 38 vacuous axioms.** Every axiom concluding with `→ True` or `claim → claim` should be reformalized to assert something a reasonable person could deny. This is the single largest source of formalization failure. T2 (`P ∨ ¬P`) is the most egregious: it claims to distinguish Catholic synergism from Protestant monergism but is trivially true under any theology.\n\n2. **Unify the type systems.** `Person` vs. `Agent`, `Sin` vs. `SinfulAct`, `Grace` vs. `TypedGrace`, `FreedomDegree` (opaque) vs. `FreedomDegree` (structure) -- these parallel types prevent cross-file reasoning. Create explicit bridge lemmas or unify the types.\n\n3. **Wire the base axioms into the formalization files.** The 15 base axioms should replace the ~50 local axioms that duplicate them. Currently the base axiom layer is a catalog, not a foundation.\n\n4. **Fix FITTINGNESS_AS_EVIDENCE and PAPAL_INFALLIBILITY** in MarianDogma.lean. Both are `claim → claim` (the identity function). They are the two axioms most critical to the Marian dependency chain and both are vacuous.\n\n5. **Resolve the Hell/Purgatory tension formally.** `death_is_final` from Hell.lean says no post-mortem change is possible. `post_mortem_purification` from Purgatory.lean says it is. The `death_finalizes_choice_not_state` axiom in Purgatory.lean addresses this conceptually but does not formally supersede or restrict `death_is_final`. The two axioms are potentially inconsistent as stated."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":20444,"cache_read_input_tokens":133065,"output_tokens":8622,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":20444},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZHjthCswcN5PUQmaD6gt","type":"assistant","uuid":"545c5ee3-26d7-4241-9bfd-9ea63df9b8fc","timestamp":"2026-03-22T07:43:18.971Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/home/ngundotra/Documents/catlib","sessionId":"8380db11-61bc-4b9e-bc7e-b8c33a25885e","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"master","slug":"hidden-honking-hellman"}
